## Stage 2a — Unit 1: Registry Overview

**OBS-103-001:** R103 love is assigned to cluster C17 (relational-grace cluster). C17 is the programme's relational cluster — covering the vocabulary of love, mercy, compassion, grace, fellowship, forgiveness, and related dispositions. Love as the lead word of C17 is structurally significant: it is the cluster's definitional centre, not one member among others. The cluster assignment signals that love is to be understood primarily as a relational phenomenon — orientation toward another — rather than as a purely internal emotional state.

**OBS-103-002:** The sb_classification is 'Spirit-Soul Interface'. No reasoning field is visible in the data package. This classification positions love at the boundary between the deepest personal centre (spirit) and the experiential-relational dimension (soul). It is consistent with the data: agapē is commanded (will/spirit-level act) and also felt (soul-level affect), and chesed is a covenant orientation (spirit) that expresses itself in relational acts. The Spirit-Soul Interface classification appears well-founded but will be tested against the anchor verse evidence in Unit 7.

**OBS-103-003:** The assigned dimension is 'Relational/Social'. The Dimension Review is complete (v1.9, 2026-04-09). The dimension assignment carries the programme's 10-dimension vocabulary result: love's primary dimension is Relational Disposition — orientation toward another. This is the confirmed output of the Dimension Review and is taken as settled input for Stage 2a.

**OBS-103-004:** The registry description names love as 'the most foundational and most theologically dense word in the entire corpus.' This is an unusually strong claim in the programme's own documentation. Its implications: (a) love may govern or generate other characteristics rather than standing as one virtue among equals; (b) the vocabulary must be examined not just for what it says about love but for what it reveals about the architecture of the inner life as a whole. Both the DIM-103-001 and DIM-103-002 findings (§N items) are grounded in this foundational claim.

**OBS-103-005:** The term inventory is exceptional in scale: 79 OWNER + 59 XREF = 138 total terms. OWNER active verses = 1,156. This exceeds any other registry examined so far in the programme. The breadth of the vocabulary — spanning Hebrew ahavah, chesed, racham, dod, and Greek agapē, phileō, and the entire philo-compound family — means that 'love' in this registry is not a single inner-being state but a vocabulary cluster covering a spectrum of relational orientations. The analytical challenge is taxonomy, not scarcity.

**OBS-103-006:** The term sharing ratio is 0.701 — 96 of 137 phase1 terms are shared with other registries. This is the highest sharing ratio in the programme's C17 cluster. Love's vocabulary bleeds into compassion (racham family), mercy (chesed B / eleos), goodness (tov family), desire (ahav family), hatred (sane — structural opposite), and the philo-compound family shared with desire (R043). This ratio signals that love's boundaries are the most porous in the programme — a critical analytical challenge for Stage 2b.

### Unit 1 Progress Sign-off
```
Unit 1 COMPLETE: 2026-04-30
  Units covered: Registry overview, cluster, sb_classification, dimension, description, term counts
  Observations written: 6 (OBS-103-001 through OBS-103-006)
  SD pointers raised: 0
  Path 3 items resolved: 0
```

## Stage 2a — Unit 2: XREF Terms

59 XREF terms present. Grouped by semantic family for reading.

**Greek XREF — Good/Goodness family (agathos root):**
- G0014 agathoergeō (to do good, 2 occ), G0015 agathopoieō (to do good, 8), G0016 agathopoiia (doing good, 1), G0017 agathopoios (doing good, 1), G0018 agathos (good, 90), G0019 agathōsunē (goodness, 17). Owning registry: R067 (goodness).
- G0865 afilagathos (hating good, 1) — a philo-compound negative. Also XREF.

**OBS-103-007:** The agathos family (goodness, R067) is a substantial XREF presence — 6 terms including the high-frequency G0018 (90 active verses). The connection is not coincidental: love and goodness share the tov/agathos root nexus (see SD DIM-103-SD009 already raised). The XREF status of this family confirms that 'love as goodness' is a known cross-registry boundary: when Scripture says God's love is expressed as goodness (Psa 25:7 — 'according to your steadfast love... for the sake of your goodness'), the two registries are interpenetrating rather than parallel.

**Greek XREF — Peace family (eirēnē root):**
- G1514 eirēneuō (be at peace, 4), G1515 eirēnē (peace, 84), G1516 eirēnikos (peaceful, 2), G1517 eirēnopoieō (to make peace, 2). Owning registry: R117 (peace).

**OBS-103-008:** Peace (R117) appears as XREF with 84 active occurrences of eirēnē — the highest single-term XREF count in the package. Peace co-occurs with love in 68 shared verses (§5). The shared anchors include Rom 1:7 (love and peace in the same greeting formula) and Gal 5:22 (peace as second fruit after love). The structural question is whether peace is love's consequence or its companion — a question for Stage 2b, not yet answerable from lexical data alone.

**Greek XREF — Philo-compound extensions:**
- G5364 filanthrōpōs (benevolently, 1), G5367 filautos (selfish, 1), G5376K filippos (Philippi, 2 — proper noun, analytically inert), G5381 filoxenia (hospitality, 2), G5382 filoxenos (hospitable, 3), G5389 filotimeomai (to aspire, 3), G5390 filofronōs (hospitably, 1), G5391 filofrōn (friendly, 1).

**OBS-103-009:** The philo-compound XREF family reveals a structural feature of the Greek love vocabulary: philo- as a prefix generates a taxonomy of love-directed-toward-objects. The XREF set here includes hospitality (love of strangers), self-love (filautos — negative), aspiration (love of honour), and friendliness. These are distinct from the OWNER philo-compounds (love of money, love of pleasure, love of dispute, love of brothers, love of God). Together they confirm that the Greek vocabulary treats love as fundamentally directional — what it is depends on what it is toward. The moral evaluation of any love-form is determined entirely by its object.

**Hebrew XREF — Desire/longing family:**
- H2530A chamad (to desire, 20), H2530B chamudah (precious thing, 20), H2531 chemed (delight, 6), H2532A chemdah (desire, 16), H2532B chamudah (desirable thing, 16), H2836A chashaq (to desire, 8), H2836B chashaq (to connect, 3), H2837 chesheq (desire, 4), H2838 chashuq (ring, 8 — likely architectural), H2839 chishuq (spoke, 1 — architectural). Owning registry: R043 (desire).

**OBS-103-010:** The desire family (R043) is the largest Hebrew XREF group. The chamad and chashaq roots share semantic space with love at the boundary of delight, attachment, and longing. Chamad is used for both legitimate delight (Song 2:3) and prohibited coveting (Exo 20:17). The XREF placement confirms that desire and love share a root-level mechanism — attachment to an object — and the moral question is the same in both: what is the object, and is it rightly ordered? This is the OT parallel to the philo-compound structure noted in OBS-103-009. The programme has correctly distinguished desire (R043) from love (R103) as separate registries, but the boundary is inherently porous.

**Hebrew XREF — Beauty/pleasantness family:**
- H3302 yaphah (be beautiful, 8), H3304 yepheh-piyphah (pretty, 1), H3308 yophi (beauty, 19), H4261 machmad (desire, 13), H4262 machmod (desirable, 1), H4516 manamim (delicacy, 1), H4999 navah (habitation, 12 — likely physical), H5273B naim (musical, 2), H5276 naem (be pleasant, 8), H5278 noam (pleasantness, 7), H5282 naaman (pleasantness, 1).

**OBS-103-011:** The beauty and pleasantness family appears as XREF — not OWNER — confirming a programme decision that aesthetic delight is adjacent to but not constitutive of love. However, the group descriptions for OWNER terms like H5000 naeh (lovely) and H5273A naim (pleasant) show these are included as OWNER, suggesting the line between aesthetic delight and relational love is drawn at the group level rather than the term level. This is analytically important: some pleasant/beautiful terms carry inner-being love content in specific groups, while others remain aesthetic.

**Hebrew XREF — Womb/compassion boundary:**
- H7356A racham (womb, 5), H7358 rechem (womb, 25), H7359 rachamin (compassion, 1), H7362 rachamani (compassionate, 1). Owning registry: R023 (compassion).

**OBS-103-012:** The womb-compassion XREF set is analytically critical. H7356B rachamim (compassion, OWNER, 39 active verses) sits in the OWNER list while H7356A racham (womb) and H7358 rechem (physical womb) sit in XREF. The data quality flag SD-025 (already raised) notes ~23 contamination verses where the womb-sense verses entered the rachamim data. The XREF placement of the physical-womb senses confirms the programme's intent: compassion-as-inner-being is OWNER; womb-as-body-part is XREF. But the etymological unity of the root means the boundary cannot be cleanly maintained at the verse level — Isa 49:15 deliberately uses both.

**Hebrew XREF — Hate/oppose family:**
- H8135 sinah (hating, 16), H8146 sani (hated, 1). Owning registry: H8130 sane (to hate) — OWNER in R103.

**OBS-103-013:** The hate family presents a structural note: H8130 sane (to hate, 139 active verses) is OWNER, while H8135 sinah (hating) and H8146 sani (hated) are XREF. This confirms that love's structural opposite is embedded within the registry — not merely noted from outside. Group 550-001 (sane) names hatred as 'the inner moral disposition opposed to love.' The inclusion of the hate vocabulary as OWNER is a deliberate programme decision: to understand love, its negation must be analysed within the same framework. This is analytically significant for T1.3 (Boundary) in Stage 2b.

**Hebrew XREF — Tov/goodness family:**
- H2896A tov (pleasant, 306), H2896B tov (good, 89), H2896C tovah (welfare, 62), H2243 chov (breast, 1 — likely physical/architectural).

**OBS-103-014:** The tov family in XREF (all forms of 'good/pleasant') with combined occurrence of 457 confirms that goodness and love share a root-level vocabulary. H2895 tov (be pleasing, OWNER) and H2898 tuv (goodness, OWNER) are distinguished from H2896 tov as XREF. The programme has separated the goodness-as-love-expression strands (OWNER) from the broader goodness vocabulary (XREF, owned by R067 goodness). This boundary will require attention in T6 (Distinctions) in Stage 2b.

**Hebrew XREF — Other:**
- H0159 ohav (beloved, 1), H2530A through H2532B (desire — already noted), H2616A chasad (be kind, 2), H2616B chasad (to shame, 1), H2617B chesed (shame, 3) — the negative sense of chesed as 'shameful/disgraceful' act.

**OBS-103-015:** H2617B chesed (shame, 3) as XREF is notable. The primary OWNER form H2617A chesed (kindness/steadfast love, 169 active verses) is among the most significant OWNER terms in the registry. But chesed has a second semantic pole — in a small set of verses, it carries the sense of 'shameful act' or 'disgrace.' The programme's XREF placement of this sense confirms awareness of the semantic duality. Analytically, this is a boundary marker: the highest love-loyalty word in the OT has a minor semantic field that runs in exactly the opposite direction.

## Stage 2a — Unit 3: OWNER Terms — Lexical Foundation

**Note on data availability:** The data package carries the OWNER term inventory table (transliteration, gloss, active verse count, occ_count) and group descriptions. Full meaning parse, root family detail, and LSJ entries reside in the database and are not reproduced in the package. Lexical observations below are grounded in what is available: glosses, transliterations, group descriptions, and the analytical programme description. Per the instruction's gap protocol, this is noted and the record proceeds.

**Working structure:** 79 OWNER terms grouped by root family for reading efficiency.

---

### Greek OWNER terms — agapē root family

**G0025 agapaō** (to love) — 107 active / 344 total occurrences. The primary NT verb for love. Root: agap- (of uncertain pre-classical etymology, possibly from agamai — to wonder/admire). The LXX uses agapaō extensively to translate aheb and chesed, embedding the Hebrew covenantal sense into the Greek form.

**G0026 agapē** (love) — 68 active / 133 total. The noun form. Almost entirely a biblical/LXX coinage — rare in classical Greek. This is analytically significant: the word most associated with Christian love did not carry an established secular meaning that could be imported. Its meaning is largely constituted by its scriptural usage.

**G0027 agapētos** (beloved) — 60 active / 79 total. Passive participial form — 'one who is loved.' Used for Christ (Mat 3:17 — 'my beloved Son') and believers (Rom 1:7).

**OBS-103-016:** The agapē root family (G0025/G0026/G0027) together covers 235 active verses. The noun agapē is effectively a LXX/NT coinage — it did not enter the vocabulary carrying pre-loaded secular Greek meaning. This means its semantic content is entirely constituted by the contexts in which Scripture uses it. Every group where agapē/agapaō appears is constitutive of the word's meaning rather than merely illustrative. This has methodological implications: for agapē, the programme's own corpus IS the definitional source.

---

### Greek OWNER terms — phileō root family

**G5368 fileō** (to love/be fond of) — 21 active / 52 total. Natural affection, friendship-love. The classical Greek word for love between friends and family.
**G5370 filēma** (kiss) — 7 active / 9 total. The kiss as physical expression of phileō.
**G5373 filia** (friendship) — 1 active / 10 total. The noun form of friendship-love.
**G5360 filadelfia** (brotherly love) — 5 active / 6 total. Love of brothers/sisters in faith.
**G5361 filadelfos** (loving the brothers) — 1 active / 1 total.
**G5362 filandros** (husband-loving) — 1 active / 1 total.
**G5363 filanthrōpia** (benevolence/love of humanity) — 2 active / 2 total.
**G5365 filarguria** (love of money) — 1 active / 2 total.
**G5366 filarguros** (money-loving) — 2 active / 2 total.
**G5369 filēdonos** (pleasure-loving) — 1 active / 1 total.
**G5377 filotheos** (God-loving) — 1 active / 1 total.
**G5379 filoneikia** (love of dispute) — 1 active / 1 total.
**G5380 filoneikos** (dispute-loving) — 1 active / 2 total.
**G5383 filoprōteuō** (to love to be first) — 1 active / 2 total.
**G5384 filos** (friend) — 27 active / 101 total. The person-type of phileō — the one who loves as a friend.
**G5387 filostorgos** (affectionate) — 1 active / 1 total. Family affection.
**G5388 filoteknos** (child-loving) — 1 active / 1 total.
**G2705 katafileō** (to kiss) — 6 active / 21 total. The intensive/repeated kiss.
**G4375 prosfilēs** (lovely) — 1 active / 2 total. That which merits love.
**G5358 filagathos** (lover of good) — 1 active / 1 total.
**G0866 afilarguros** (not greedy/free from love of money) — 2 active / 2 total.
**G5569 pseudadelfos** (false brother) — 2 active / 2 total. The person-type negation.

**OBS-103-017:** The philo-compound family (22 OWNER terms) reveals a structural feature unique to Greek: philo- as a generative prefix creates a systematic taxonomy of love-directed-toward-objects. The taxonomy includes:
- Legitimate objects: brothers (filadelfia), husband (filandros), children (filoteknos), God (filotheos), good (filagathos), humanity (filanthrōpia), friends (filos)
- Disordered objects: money (filarguria, filarguros), pleasure (filēdonos), dispute (filoneikia), primacy (filoprōteuō)
- Negation forms: not-money-loving (afilarguros), false-brother (pseudadelfos)

The taxonomy implies a single inner-being mechanism — attachment/orientation toward — whose moral character is entirely determined by its object. Love of money and love of God are structurally identical acts of inner attachment; what differs is the object, not the mechanism.

**OBS-103-018:** G5384 filos (friend, 27 active / 101 total) is the largest-occurrence term in the philo-family. It names not the act but the person-type — the one characterised by philos-love. This is the programme's clearest example in R103 of a person-type term (per T7.1 prompt 6). The friend is one whose inner orientation of loyal affection has become their defining relational identity. The negative counterpart is pseudadelfos (false brother) — the person whose apparent community-bond is inner deception.

---

### Greek OWNER terms — adelfos (brother/sister) family and firstborn

**G0079 adelfē** (sister) — 25 active / 130 total.
**G0081 adelfotēs** (brotherhood) — 2 active / 2 total.
**G4416 prōtotokos** (firstborn) — 9 active / 134 total.
**G4415 prōtotokia** (birthright) — 1 active / 10 total.

**OBS-103-019:** The adelfos/adelfē family and the prōtotokos (firstborn) group occupy a sub-sector of the love vocabulary that is relational-identity rather than affective. They name structural relationships within the community of love: sister, brotherhood, firstborn. Their inclusion as OWNER terms reflects a programme decision that the vocabulary of love encompasses not just inner dispositions but the relational structures those dispositions create. The firstborn/birthright terms reach their significance via Rom 8:29 (Christ as firstborn among many brothers) and Heb 12:16 (Esau selling birthright — disordering the inner love of the sacred).

---

### Greek OWNER terms — miscellaneous

**G1518 eirēnopoios** (peacemaker) — 1 active / 1 total. Mat 5:9. The peacemaker as person-type of love expressed outward.
**G7493 eraō** (to love passionately) — 0 active / 2 total. No active verses. The eros root — passionate/erotic love — is present in the inventory with zero active verses. 

**OBS-103-020:** G7493 eraō (to love passionately) has 0 active verses despite 2 total occurrences. This is a significant data point: the eros root, which in Greek philosophical tradition names the highest form of love (Plato's Symposium), is analytically present but evidentially absent in the programme's verse evidence. The programme's love vocabulary is dominated by agapē and phileō — the covenantal-willed and the relational-affectionate — while eros is marginal in the scriptural evidence. This absence is itself analytically significant and must be noted in Stage 2b T7.

---

### Greek OWNER terms — prōtos family (zero active)

G1207 deuteroprōtos, G4409 prōteuō, G4410 prōtokathedria, G4411 prōtoklisia, G4412 prōton, G4413G/H/I/J prōtos variants, G4414 prōtostatēs — all 0 active verses.

**OBS-103-021:** The prōtos family (first/primary) terms have 0 active verses. These entered the OWNER inventory via the prōtotokos/firstborn connection but contribute no classified verse evidence. They are lexical context for firstborn terminology but not direct analytical contributors. Noted and set aside.

---

### Hebrew OWNER terms — ahav root family

**H0157H a.hev** (to love: friend) — 13 active / 13 total.
**H0158 a.hav** (lover) — 2 active / 2 total.
**H0160 a.ha.vah** (love) — 35 active / 45 total.

**OBS-103-022:** The ahav root (H0157H, H0158, H0160) is the primary Hebrew love vocabulary — the OT equivalent of agapaō. H0157G a.hev (to love: lover, 184 active) is XREF (owned by R043 desire), confirming the programme's analytical decision that the primary ahav verbal form is shared with the desire registry. Only the friend-directed form (H0157H), the noun ahav (lover), and the abstract ahavah (love) are OWNER. This creates a critical analytical situation: the word most often translated as 'love' in the OT (ahav) is primarily held in the desire registry, not the love registry. The love registry holds the narrower forms. This boundary will require careful treatment in T6 (Distinctions).

---

### Hebrew OWNER terms — dod root family

**H1730G dod** (beloved) — 27 active / 33 total. The beloved of the Song — the romantic, erotic address.
**H1730H dod** (beloved: love) — 9 active / 58 total. The generalised beloved/love sense.
**H1730I dod** (beloved: male relative) — 17 active / 18 total. Uncle/relative sense.
**H1731 dud** (pot) — 0 active / 8 total. Physical vessel — zero active.
**H1733 dodah** (aunt) — 0 active / 3 total. Zero active.
**H1736 duday** (mandrake) — 4 active / 6 total. Song fertility/erotic context.

**OBS-103-023:** The dod root spans three distinct semantic fields: the beloved-as-person (romantic address in the Song), the love/delight-as-quality, and the kinship-relative (uncle/aunt). The romantic-beloved sense (H1730G, 27 active verses concentrated in the Song of Songs) is the dominant carrier of erotic-romantic love in the Hebrew corpus — the eros-equivalent that Greek eraō lacks evidence for. The dod vocabulary thus fills the gap left by eraō's absence: passionate, embodied, exclusive love-attachment is present in the OT dod vocabulary even where the Greek NT has no equivalent.

**OBS-103-024:** H1736 duday (mandrake, 4 active) appears in the Song fertility-desire contexts. The mandrake was associated with fertility and erotic attraction in the ancient world. Its inclusion as OWNER (not set aside) confirms the programme's decision that erotic/fertility vocabulary within the love context carries inner-being content — these are not merely physical/botanical references but carriers of the love-eros dimension in its Hebrew form.

---

### Hebrew OWNER terms — chesed root family

**H2617A che.sed** (kindness/steadfast love) — 169 active / 241 total. The most evidentially rich term in the registry.
**H2623 cha.sid** (pious/godly one) — 33 active / 39 total. The person-type of chesed.
**H2895 tov** (be pleasing) — 20 active / 21 total. The goodness-within-love sense.
**H2898 tuv** (goodness) — 0 active / 31 total. Zero active — note.

**OBS-103-025:** H2617A chesed (169 active / 261 total) is the most evidentially dominant term in the entire registry. It exceeds agapaō (107 active) and H7453 rea (173 active) in active verse count. Chesed's semantic range spans: covenant-faithfulness, loyal love, steadfast mercy, kindness, and — in the relational context — the obligation of faithful love within a bond. It is simultaneously a divine attribute (God's chesed) and a human virtue (the chesed shown to the poor, to enemies, to covenantal partners). Its programmatic centrality to the love vocabulary cannot be overstated.

**OBS-103-026:** H2623 chasid (pious/godly one, 33 active) is the person-type of chesed — the one whose inner character is shaped by covenantal love. This is the OT's clearest person-type term in R103: as filos is to phileō, chasid is to chesed. The chasid is defined not by ritual observance but by inner loyalty-love expressed outward. The Psalter's chasidim (faithful/godly ones) are characterised by this covenantal love orientation as their defining inner-being quality.

**OBS-103-027:** H2898 tuv (goodness) has 0 active verses in the OWNER set. This confirms the programme's handling: the tuv/goodness connection to love is analytically significant (SD-009 already raised on Psa 25:7) but the broad goodness vocabulary belongs to R067, not R103. Only the narrow love-expressing-goodness strands carry OWNER status.

---

### Hebrew OWNER terms — rea/friend family

**H4828 me.re.a** (companion) — 7 active / 7 total.
**H7453 re.a** (neighbor) — 173 active / 191 total. The most occurrence-rich OWNER term.
**H7463 re.eh** (friend) — 3 active / 6 total.
**H7464 re.ah** (companion) — 3 active / 5 total.
**H7468 re.ut** (neighbor) — 6 active / 6 total.

**OBS-103-028:** H7453 rea (neighbor, 173 active / 191 total) is the most occurrence-rich OWNER term in R103. But its semantic function is different from the love terms: it names not the disposition but the relational object — the one toward whom love is owed. The great commandment (Lev 19:18 — 'love your neighbor') makes rea the object of ahavah. The inclusion of rea as OWNER confirms that the programme treats the moral category of neighbour as constituent of the love vocabulary — not just the emotion of love, but its obligatory relational structure.

---

### Hebrew OWNER terms — racham family

**H7349 ra.chum** (compassionate) — 13 active / 13 total. Adjectival — God is compassionate.
**H7355 ra.cham** (to have compassion) — 43 active / 47 total. The primary compassion verb.
**H7356B ra.cha.mim** (compassion) — 39 active / 69 total. The plural-intensive noun.

**OBS-103-029:** The racham family (95 active verses combined) forms a distinct sub-cluster within the love vocabulary: love-as-compassion — the responsive form of love that moves toward the suffering. H7356B rachamim uses a plural-intensive form (recalling the grammatical intensity of elohim — 'deep compassions'), signalling that compassion is not a simple affective response but an intensified inner disposition. The womb-etymology (rechem) remains analytically active here: divine compassion is grammatically womb-shaped.

---

### Hebrew OWNER terms — sane/hate family

**H8130 sa.ne** (to hate) — 139 active / 156 total.
**H8131 se.na** (to hate) — 1 active / 4 total.

**OBS-103-030:** H8130 sane (to hate, 139 active) is the structural opposite of love in the OWNER inventory. Its active verse count (139) places it as the second-most-evidenced verbal term after H7453 rea. The hate vocabulary is not XREF but OWNER — embedded within the love registry. This confirms the programme's analytical intent: love cannot be understood without its opposite, and the intensity of sane in Scripture (God's hatred of evil, the righteous hatred of what is wicked, the psalmist's holy hatred) is part of the inner-being architecture of love, not external to it.

---

### Hebrew OWNER terms — remaining

**H3033 ye.di.dut** (beloved) — 1 active / 1 total. One verse only: Jer 12:7. Subject of DIM-103-002.
**H3039A ya.did** (beloved) — 8 active / 8 total.
**H3039B ya.di.dah** (love) — 0 active / 1 total. Zero active.
**H5000 na.eh** (lovely) — 10 active / 14 total.
**H5273A na.im** (pleasant) — 11 active / 14 total.
**H5691 a.ga.vah** (lust) — 1 active / 1 total.
**H2244 cha.va** (to hide) — 0 active / 33 total. Zero active.
**H2247 cha.vah** (to hide) — 0 active / 5 total. Zero active.
**H1717 dad** (breast) — 0 active / 4 total. Zero active.

**OBS-103-031:** H5691 agavah (lust, 1 active) is the corrupted love-form — the desire that drives spiritual adultery. Its single active verse (Eze 23:11 — Oholibah's lust exceeding her sister's) is within the prophetic tradition of portraying Israel's spiritual infidelity as sexual lust. Together with the disordered philo-compounds (love of money, pleasure, dispute), agavah constitutes the love vocabulary's taxonomy of misdirection. The programme has assembled the distorted forms within the same registry as the normative ones — a structurally important analytical decision.

**OBS-103-032:** H2244/H2247 chava (to hide, 0 active), H1717 dad (breast, 0 active), and H3039B yadidah (0 active) have zero active verses. These entered the OWNER inventory via root-family connections but carry no classified verse evidence. They are terminological context, not analytical contributors. Noted and set aside.

**OBS-103-033:** The OWNER term set reveals four distinct semantic clusters within the love vocabulary:
1. **Willed covenantal love** — chesed, ahavah (the binding, faithful, relational commitment)
2. **Compassionate responsive love** — racham/rachamim (love that moves toward suffering)
3. **Relational-social love** — phileō family, filos, rea, rea-family (friend, neighbour, companion bonds)
4. **Intense/erotic love** — dod, ahavah in Song contexts, katafileō (the passionate, exclusive, embodied)

These four clusters are not four separate phenomena but four modes of the same inner-being orientation toward another. The analytical task in Stage 2b is to map how they interrelate and whether they are constituted by a single underlying disposition or are genuinely distinct inner-being phenomena.

```
Unit 3 COMPLETE: 2026-04-30
  Units covered: All 79 OWNER terms across agapē root, philo-compound family, adelfos/firstborn, prōtos (zero active), ahav root, dod root, chesed root, rea/friend family, racham family, sane/hate family, and remaining Hebrew terms
  Observations written: 18 (OBS-103-016 through OBS-103-033)
  SD pointers raised: 0
  Path 3 items resolved: 0
  Data gap noted: Full lexical parse (meaning_parse, root family detail, LSJ) not in data package — proceeded from glosses, occurrence data, and group descriptions per gap protocol
```

### Unit 4 — Landscape Synthesis Observations

**OBS-103-034:** Dominant subject distribution across 67 groups:
- GOD as dominant: approx. 14 groups (chesed-God, racham, rachamim, ahavah-God, yedidut, yadid, rachum, filanthrōpia, agapētos-555-001, agapē-562-001, agapaō-571-002, tuv/goodness-God, prōtotokos-God-nexus, dod-God-contexts)
- HUMAN as dominant: approx. 44 groups
- Mixed/HUMAN-GOD mutual: approx. 9 groups

The concentration of GOD-dominant groups in R103 is higher than in any other registry examined in the programme to date. Love is unique among the inner-being characteristics in the programme in that it applies symmetrically to both divine and human subjects across a large evidential base — not merely as analogy but as shared vocabulary.

**OBS-103-035:** The group landscape reveals a consistent structural pattern: love in Scripture operates in three directional axes:
1. **Vertical-descending:** GOD → HUMAN (God's love poured out, demonstrated, given)
2. **Vertical-ascending:** HUMAN → GOD (commanded love of God with whole being)
3. **Horizontal:** HUMAN → HUMAN (love of neighbour, enemy, brother, companion)

The three axes are not independent. The data consistently shows God's love as prior and generative: 1Jo 4:19 ('we love because he first loved us') and Joh 13:34 ('as I have loved you — so you must love one another'). This structural precedence of divine love over human love is one of the most consistently evidenced patterns in the data.

**OBS-103-036:** The disordered love groups form a coherent counter-taxonomy:
- Love of money (filarguria, filarguros) — 3 groups
- Love of pleasure (filēdonos) — 1 group
- Love of dispute (filoneikia, filoneikos) — 2 groups
- Love of being first (filoprōteuō) — 1 group
- Friendship with world (filia-Jam 4:4) — 1 group
- Disordered agapaō (love of darkness, world) — 571-005
- Lust (agavah) — 548-001
The disordered forms all share a common structure: love's inner-being mechanism (attachment, orientation toward, giving of self) is intact — but the object is disordered. This confirms OBS-103-009 and OBS-103-017: love has one mechanism with many possible objects, and the moral quality of any love-act is entirely determined by whether its object is rightly ordered.

**OBS-103-037:** Three groups name love's structural opposite or negation within the OWNER set: sane (550-001 — hatred), sena (1663-001), and pseudadelfos (false brother, 1611-001). The inclusion of hatred as an OWNER term (not merely XREF) is analytically consequential: love and hatred in Scripture are not simply opposite points on an emotional spectrum but are treated as constitutive orientations of the inner being — what a person loves and what a person hates together define their moral character. Psa 97:10 ('you who love the Lord, hate evil') places righteous hatred within love's framework, not outside it.

**OBS-103-038:** Group 536-001 (chesed-GOD) has 182 relevant verses — by far the largest relevance pool in the registry, exceeding even H7453 rea (152 relevant). Chesed-as-divine-attribute is the single most evidentially represented characteristic in R103. This has structural implications: any account of love in this registry that does not begin with divine chesed will misrepresent the data distribution.

**OBS-103-039:** Several groups name love at the community/identity level rather than the individual inner-being level: adelfotēs (brotherhood, 1610-001), agapē mutual among believers (562-003), agapaō mutual (571-004), filadelfia (558-001). These groups suggest love as a communal inner reality — not merely what individuals feel but what the community is constituted by. The mark of discipleship ('by this all will know you are my disciples — if you love one another,' Joh 13:35) functions at the community level: love is publicly legible as the community's identity marker.

**OBS-103-040:** The group for agapētos-believers (555-002, 63 relevant, 2 anchor) names the believer as 'beloved' — the passive recipient of divine love whose identity is constituted by being-loved. This is structurally distinct from the active love groups: here the inner-being state is not one of loving but of being-loved. The identity category 'beloved' (agapētos) may be one of the most significant groups in the programme for the question of how divine love constitutes human identity.

**OBS-103-041:** The Song of Songs vocabulary (dod groups 1602-001, 533-001, 545-001 rayah; also duday mandrake; and the ahavah intense-love group 537-002) forms a sub-cluster of erotic/romantic love with 66 combined relevant verses. This is the registry's primary evidential source for love as passionate, embodied, exclusive attachment. The Song vocabulary provides the inner-being data for love's erotic dimension that G7493 eraō (0 active) cannot supply. The dod vocabulary is thus the OT's erotic-love archive.

```
  Observations written: 8 (OBS-103-034 through OBS-103-041)
```

## Stage 2a — Unit 5: Correlation Signals

**Source: §5 co-occurrence and §6 shared anchor verses**

Top 25 co-occurrence registries (shared verses with R103 OWNER active verses):

| Rank | Registry | Word | Shared verses |
|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | R023 | compassion | 196 |
| 2 | R187 | strength | 105 |
| 3 | R197 | authority | 69 |
| 4 | R117 | peace | 68 |
| 5 | R059 | faith | 62 |
| 6 | R044 | despair | 55 |
| 7 | R112 | mind | 52 |
| 8 | R173 | will | 52 |
| 9 | R019 | calling | 51 |
| 10 | R182 | Soul | 50 |
| 11 | R043 | desire | 49 |
| 12 | R051 | distress | 49 |
| 13 | R183 | heart | 47 |
| 14 | R005 | anguish | 39 |
| 15 | R097 | joy | 35 |
| 16 | R156 | surrender | 33 |
| 17 | R034 | covenant | 33 |
| 18 | R042 | delight | 33 |
| 19 | R057 | evil | 33 |
| 20 | R073 | guilt | 32 |
| 21 | R121 | praise | 31 |
| 22 | R100 | knowledge | 30 |
| 23 | R008 | appetite | 30 |
| 24 | R099 | kindness | 30 |
| 25 | R111 | mercy | 29 |

**OBS-103-042:** R023 compassion leads all co-occurrence with 196 shared verses — the highest co-occurrence score of any registry pair encountered in the programme to date. This exceeds what would be expected from incidental verse overlap and reflects a deep structural connection: the racham family (compassion) and the chesed/ahavah family (love) operate in the same evidential terrain. The compassion-love co-occurrence confirms that compassion is not a separate emotion adjacent to love but love's form under the condition of suffering. This is the programme's most evidentially supported cross-registry connection.

**OBS-103-043:** R187 strength (105 shared) is the second-highest co-occurrence. This is counterintuitive — strength is a C20 cluster word, not C17. The existing SD pointer DIM-103-SD026 has already noted this. The connection is not incidental: chesed/steadfast love and strength (el/gibbor/chazaq vocabulary) co-occur in the OT's characterisation of God's inner being. 'The Lord is my strength and my song' (Exo 15:2) — the same God whose love never ceases is the God of incomparable power. The love-strength co-occurrence signals that love and power are held together in the divine inner-being portrait rather than in tension.

**OBS-103-044:** R197 authority (69 shared) compounds the love-power finding. Authority vocabulary co-occurs significantly with love — suggesting that love in Scripture is not merely affective but operative: God's love is expressed through acts of authority (covenant, law-giving, judgment, redemption). Love without authority in Scripture would be sentiment; authority without love would be mere power. The co-occurrence suggests a structural integration.

**OBS-103-045:** R044 despair (55 shared) is analytically striking. Despair co-occurs with love in 55 verses — more than faith (62 is close, but despair's presence is unexpected). This may reflect the lament/petition pattern in the Psalms and Jeremiah: the person in despair appeals to God's love as the ground of hope. Alternatively, it may reflect the shared anchor at verses like Jer 12:7 (God's grief/abandonment), Lam 3:22 (chesed in the midst of affliction), and similar lament contexts where despair and love are held simultaneously.

**OBS-103-046:** R112 mind and R173 will share equal co-occurrence (52 each). This confirms the cognitive and volitional dimensions of love already implied by the group landscape: love is commanded (Mat 22:37 — 'with all your heart, soul, and mind'), which means it engages the will; and it requires knowledge of its object ('I have called you friends, for all that I have heard from my Father I have made known to you' — Joh 15:15). Love is not pure emotion in Scripture but engages the cognitive and volitional registers of the inner person.

**OBS-103-047:** R182 Soul (50 shared) and R183 heart (47 shared) are the two primary inner-being location terms in co-occurrence with love. Their combined co-occurrence (97 verses) signals that love is consistently located in the deepest interior. H3033 yedidut (beloved of God's soul — Jer 12:7) and the great commandment ('love with all your heart and soul and mind') both locate love within the soul and heart — the programme's primary constitutional locations.

**OBS-103-048:** R034 covenant (33 shared) co-occurs with love at a level that confirms the structural relationship between chesed and covenant (berit). The love vocabulary is not merely metaphorically relational — it is covenantally constituted. Chesed is the inner disposition of covenant-faithfulness; the love between God and Israel is a covenantal love. This structural connection places love within the programme's constitutional-relational framework, not merely the affective framework.

**OBS-103-049:** R073 guilt (32 shared) co-occurrence is notable and aligns with SD-028 (already raised): Luk 7:47 — forgiveness → love. Guilt and love share 32 verses. The structural hypothesis — guilt as the prior state that received forgiveness resolves, producing love as response — has evidential support in the co-occurrence data.

**OBS-103-050:** Shared anchor verses (§6) — 48 anchor verses shared with other registries. Key high-density shared anchors:
- **Exo 34:6** — shared with anger/R4, patience/R116, faith/R59, compassion/R23, calling/R19. Five registries. The divine self-declaration formula is the programme's most cross-referenced single verse.
- **Gal 5:22** — shared with patience/R116, joy/R97, goodness/R67, peace/R117, faith/R59. The fruit-of-Spirit list as shared anchor confirms that love heads a list of inner-being characteristics that are all held in the same registry-complex.
- **1Cor 13:4** — shared with patience/R116, pride/R123, kindness/R99. Love's primary definitional passage shared with three adjacent registries.
- **Mic 6:8** — shared with goodness/R67, kindness/R99, will/R173, humility/R80, compassion/R23, condemnation/R24. Six registries — the chesed/justice/humility triad verse already noted in SD-006.
- **Jer 31:34** — shared with guilt/R73, thought/R160, forgiveness/R64. New covenant passage integrating love-knowledge-forgiveness.
- **Rom 5:5** — shared with hope/R78, shame/R146. God's love poured into hearts through Spirit — a foundational theological statement.

**OBS-103-051:** The shared anchor map confirms the programme's highest-priority Session D connections:
- **Fruit of Spirit axis**: love (103) → joy (97) → peace (117) → patience (116) → kindness (99) → goodness (67) → faith (59) — Gal 5:22 as anchor
- **1Cor 13 axis**: love (103) ↔ patience (116) ↔ pride (123) ↔ kindness (99)
- **Exo 34:6 axis**: love/chesed (103) ↔ compassion (23) ↔ patience (116) ↔ calling/grace (19) ↔ anger (4)
- **New covenant axis**: love (103) ↔ guilt (73) ↔ knowledge (100) ↔ forgiveness (64)
- **Fear-love axis**: 1Pe 2:17 (love brotherhood, fear God) — love and fear in deliberate syntactic parallel (cross-reference to R061 fear not shown in §6 but implied from 1Jo 4:18 — 'perfect love casts out fear')

**SP marker raised:** The love-fear structural opposition (1Jo 4:18) is not covered by any existing SD pointer in the data. Raising now.

**SP-103-029** — raised in Unit 5, 2026-04-30, HIGH, Session D
- Target: R061 (fear) / R103 (love)
- Connecting term: G0026 agapē / G5401 phobos (fear)
- Question: 1Jo 4:18 — 'perfect love casts out fear.' Is fear the structural inner-being state that love displaces — and if so, what kind of fear? Does the OT parallel (Psa 27:1 — 'the Lord is my light and salvation, whom shall I fear?') confirm that love-as-trust and fear-as-threat are structurally opposed? This is the programme's most explicit cross-registry claim about love's effect on another inner-being state. Cross-registry: love (103), fear (61). Note: PH2-103-003 already tracks this as a Session D priority — this SP formalises it.

The sub-pattern is real and evidentially substantial, not confined to a single verse. **Assessment: confirmed, well-grounded, deepened. Will resolve via Q&A in Stage 2b (Path 1), primarily through T0 (Divine Image) tier.**

## Stage 2a — Unit 7: Anchor Verse Reading

**117 anchor verses across 67 groups. Working group by group, term by term.**
**Cross-registry vision questions applied to each anchor verse:**
1. Does this verse name or imply an inner-being characteristic appearing in another registry?
2. Does the term's behaviour here differ from its primary registry — suggesting a cross-registry boundary question?
3. Does grammatical form (causative, reflexive, passive) create a causal/relational connection to another inner-being state?
4. Does the verse place two or more inner-being states in structural relationship?
5. Does somatic expression here align with a somatic pattern in another registry?

---

### Group 1579-001 — G5384 filos (friend)

**Joh 15:15** — 'No longer do I call you servants, for the servant does not know what his master is doing; but I have called you friends, for all that I have heard from my Father I have made known to you.'

**OBS-103-052:** Friendship here is defined by **knowledge disclosure** — Jesus names the content of the friendship as revelation: 'all that I have heard from my Father I have made known to you.' The transition from servant (doulos) to friend (filos) is a transition from duty-without-knowledge to love-with-knowledge. The inner-being movement is: love restructures the epistemic relationship — the beloved is brought into the lover's inner world. Cross-registry signal: R100 (knowledge) — love constitutes the condition for knowledge of God's purposes.

*Cross-registry check 1:* Yes — knowledge (R100), calling (R19). *Check 4:* Love and knowledge in structural relationship — knowledge-disclosure as love's definitive act.

SP already raised (SD-021). No new SP needed.

**Jam 2:23** — 'Abraham believed God, and it was counted to him as righteousness — and he was called a friend of God.'

**OBS-103-053:** Abraham is named 'friend of God' (filos theou) — not because of a sentiment but because of faith-counted-as-righteousness. The friend-of-God designation emerges from the forensic/covenantal action of God (imputation of righteousness) grounded in faith. The inner-being sequence here: faith (R059) → declared-righteous → named-friend. Friendship with God is not a disposition Abraham takes up but a status God confers. Cross-registry: faith (59), calling/identity (19), righteousness (implied).

*Cross-registry check 1:* R059 (faith), R019 (calling). *Check 3:* passive — 'was called' — God's act constitutes the relational identity.

Group 1579-001 COMPLETE: 2 anchor verses read. Key observation: friendship with God is constituted by divine disclosure (Joh 15:15) and divine declaration (Jam 2:23) — love as knowledge-sharing and status-conferral.

---

### Group 1580-001 — G5370 filēma (kiss)

**Luk 22:48** — 'Judas, would you betray the Son of Man with a kiss?'

**OBS-103-054:** The kiss (filēma) here is exposed as the instrument of betrayal — the outward sign of love used to signal its opposite to the arresting party. The inner state is concealed deception (like pseudadelfos, group 1611-001) while the physical sign is love's expression. This verse confirms that the outward act of love can be weaponised when the inner orientation is absent or corrupted. The bodily sign and the inner state are not identical — the sign requires the inner reality to be authentic. Somatic signal: physical kiss as readable sign of inner love (or its counterfeit).

*Cross-registry check 5:* Somatic expression. *Check 4:* betrayal (inner) and kiss (outward) in structural opposition.

**1Pe 5:14** — 'Greet one another with the kiss of love. Peace to all of you who are in Christ.'

**OBS-103-055:** The 'kiss of love' (filēma agapēs) pairs two love terms in a single liturgical command. The kiss is not incidental warmth but the commanded communal expression of the inner agapē that constitutes the believing community. The closing peace-benediction ('peace to all of you in Christ') places the holy kiss within the peace vocabulary — the kiss is an act of peace-making within the community of love. Cross-registry: peace (R117). Somatic: bodily greeting as the community's love made visible and physically enacted.

Group 1580-001 COMPLETE: Key observation: the kiss is love's somatic sign — its authenticity requires the matching inner state; its absence or corruption exposes inner disorder.

---

### Group 1581-001 — G2705 katafileō (to kiss — intensive)

**Luk 7:38** — 'Standing behind him at his feet, weeping, she began to wet his feet with her tears and wiped them with the hair of her head and kissed his feet and anointed them with the ointment.'

**OBS-103-056:** This verse is one of the programme's densest somatic-inner-being passages. The woman's bodily actions — weeping, using her hair, kissing feet, anointing — are all carried by inner love and grief together. The tears come before the kiss; the grief (for her sin? for her encounter with grace?) precedes and accompanies the love-expression. Jesus' verdict will come in verse 47: 'she loved much because she was forgiven much.' The somatic complexity here — tears, hair, kiss, ointment — is love's bodily vocabulary. Cross-registry: grief (71), forgiveness (64). SD-020 already raised.

*Check 5:* Somatic convergence — tears (grief) + kiss (love) + anointing (honour/devotion). *Check 4:* love and grief structurally co-present.

**Luk 15:20** — 'His father saw him and felt compassion, and ran and embraced him and kissed him.'

**OBS-103-057:** The father's response sequence: see → feel compassion (splanchnizō — from splanchna, inner organs/bowels) → run → embrace → kiss. The katafileō here is the culmination of a movement that begins in the father's inner being (compassion — a different term but same inner-being territory as rachamim). The running is the body's enactment of the inner movement. The kiss is love's outward completion. Cross-registry: compassion (23). *Check 4:* compassion and love in structural relationship — love acts through compassion as its motivating inner state.

SP raised: the Luk 15:20 passage requires cross-registry investigation specifically on the sequence compassion → love-act.

**SP-103-030** — raised in Unit 7, 2026-04-30, MEDIUM, Session D
- Target: R023 (compassion) / R103 (love)
- Connecting term: G2705 katafileō / G4697 splanchnizō (compassion)
- Question: Luk 15:20 — the father sees the returning son and the inner movement is splanchnizō (felt compassion) which produces running, embracing, and kissing. Is compassion the inner state that activates love's outward expression — or is compassion love itself operating under the condition of the returning? What is the precise relationship between compassion as felt inner state and love as the orientation that gives rise to it? Cross-registry: love (103), compassion (23).
- Evidence basis: OBS-103-057

Group 1581-001 COMPLETE: Key observation: katafileō carries the somatic dimension of love — the bodily kiss as love's external enactment; the inner state preceding it is variously grief (Luk 7), compassion (Luk 15), or joy at reunion.

---

### Group 1588-001 — G5373 filia (friendship)

**Jam 4:4** — 'You adulterous people! Do you not know that friendship with the world is enmity with God? Therefore whoever wishes to be a friend of the world makes himself an enemy of God.'

**OBS-103-058:** Friendship (filia) with the world constitutes enmity (echthra) with God — not mere distance but active opposition. The inner logic: love/friendship is exclusive at its deepest level — the person cannot hold two ultimate objects of attachment simultaneously. Jam 4:4 applies to love the same logic that Jesus applies in the double-love commandment and the 'no one can serve two masters' saying. The inner person's deepest attachment (friendship/love) must be singular in its ultimate direction. Disordered love is not just misplaced affection — it constitutes enmity. *Check 4:* Love of world and love of God in structural opposition — one excludes the other.

Group 1588-001 COMPLETE: Key observation: love's exclusivity at the ultimate level — friendship with the world constitutes enmity with God. Love cannot be divided at its deepest orientation.

---

### Group 1600-001 — H0157H a.hev (to love: friend)

**Pro 27:6** — 'Faithful are the wounds of a friend; profuse are the kisses of an enemy.'

**OBS-103-059:** The wounds of a friend (ahev) and the kisses of an enemy — this proverb inverts the expected association between physical sign and inner reality. The painful wound is the sign of faithful love (ahev); the pleasant kiss is the sign of enmity. This is the OT equivalent of Luk 22:48 (Judas' kiss): the outer sign deceives, the inner orientation determines the truth. The friend who wounds does so from inner loyalty — love as honest confrontation, not comfort-seeking. *Check 4:* love and faithfulness in structural relationship — love expresses itself through honesty even at cost.

**Isa 41:8** — 'But you, Israel, my servant, Jacob, whom I have chosen, the offspring of Abraham, my friend.'

**OBS-103-060:** God addresses Israel as 'my friend' (ahev — literally 'the one who loves me' or 'my lover/friend'). The divine-human friendship is here rooted in election — chosen, servant, offspring of Abraham, and friend. The sequence is notable: election precedes friendship; the friend-relationship is constituted by God's prior act. This mirrors Jam 2:23 (Abraham called friend of God through faith-righteousness) and OBS-103-053. *Check 1:* calling/election (R019). *Check 3:* passive — Israel is constituted as God's friend by divine act.

Group 1600-001 COMPLETE: Key observation: loyal friendship (ahev) is evidenced by honest faithfulness even when painful — the inner reality of love is tested by cost, not comfort.

---

### Group 1602-001 — H1730G dod (beloved — Song)

**Song 2:16** — 'My beloved is mine, and I am his; he grazes among the lilies.'

**OBS-103-061:** The mutual possession formula ('my beloved is mine and I am his') is the Song's primary statement of exclusive love-attachment. The inner-being reality is mutual belonging — a reflexive relational state where each is constituted as beloved by the other's love. This is one of Scripture's closest approximations to a mutual love-definition. The pastoral imagery ('grazes among the lilies') places the love in a creation-delight context. *Check 4:* love as mutual-constitution — not one-directional but reflexively constituting.

**Song 5:6** — 'I opened to my beloved, but my beloved had turned and gone. My soul failed me when he spoke. I sought him, but found him not; I called him, but he gave no answer.'

**OBS-103-062:** The lover opens the door and finds the beloved gone. The inner-being response: 'my soul (nephesh) failed me' — a collapse of the inner person at the beloved's absence. This is one of the programme's most explicit statements that love-and-soul are constitutively linked: the soul fails (literally 'went out' — a near-fainting or loss of self) at the absence of the beloved. The seeking and calling that follow are the soul's active reaching for what constitutes it. *Check 1:* Soul (R182). *Check 4:* love and soul in constitutive relationship — the soul's vitality is bound to the presence of the beloved.

SP raised: Song 5:6 and the nephesh-failing response to love's loss.

**SP-103-031** — raised in Unit 7, 2026-04-30, MEDIUM, Session D
- Target: R182 (Soul) / R103 (love)
- Connecting term: H1730G dod / H5315 nephesh (soul)
- Question: Song 5:6 — 'my soul (nephesh) failed me.' The soul's response to the beloved's absence is a collapse — nephesh 'went out.' Does this verse evidence that love and the soul are constitutively related — that the soul's vitality depends on the presence of its beloved? If so, love is not merely an emotion the soul experiences but a state that constitutes the soul's inner vitality. How does this connect to the programme's account of the soul? Cross-registry: love (103), Soul (182).
- Evidence basis: OBS-103-062

Group 1602-001 COMPLETE: Key observation: the Song's dod vocabulary names love as a mutual-constitutive relationship — each is made who they are by being the other's beloved; the soul fails at the beloved's absence.

---

### Group 1609-001 — G0079 adelfē (sister)

**Mat 12:50** — 'For whoever does the will of my Father in heaven is my brother and sister and mother.'

**OBS-103-063:** The relational category 'sister' (adelfē) is here redefined by obedience — the natural family relationship is recast as the community of those who do God's will. Love's relational vocabulary (sister, brother, mother) is applied to the community constituted by shared orientation toward God. The inner-being significance: the deepest relational bonds in human life (family) are redrawn around will-alignment (R173) and God-orientation. *Check 1:* will (R173). *Check 4:* love-relationship and will in structural connection — will-alignment constitutes the love-community.

**1Ti 5:2** — 'older women as mothers, younger women as sisters, in all purity.'

**OBS-103-064:** The community's love relationships are structured by age-analogy to family roles, with purity (hagneia — cleanness, chastity) as the qualifier for the sister-relationship. The inner-being significance: love in the community is to operate within a structured relational form that both expresses genuine affection and disciplines it. Purity is not the absence of love but its proper ordering within appropriate relational boundaries.

Group 1609-001 COMPLETE: Key observation: sister/family vocabulary names the love-community as a restructured family — constituted by will-alignment with God, regulated by inner purity.

---

### Group 1610-001 — G0081 adelfotēs (brotherhood)

**1Pe 2:17** — 'Honor everyone. Love the brotherhood. Fear God. Honor the emperor.'

**OBS-103-065:** The four commands here are placed in deliberate parallelism: honor all / love the brotherhood / fear God / honor the emperor. The inner disposition verbs are love (agapaō — implied) and fear (phobeomai). The brotherhood (adelfotēs) receives love; God receives fear. The parallelism is not accidental — love and fear are assigned to their proper objects. This is structurally connected to SP-103-029 (love-fear): 1Jo 4:18 says perfect love casts out fear; 1Pe 2:17 assigns fear to God and love to the brotherhood — not competing but properly directed. *Check 4:* love and fear in structural relationship — different objects, same persons.

**1Pe 5:9** — 'Resist him, firm in your faith, knowing that the same kinds of suffering are being experienced by your brotherhood throughout the world.'

**OBS-103-066:** The brotherhood (adelfotēs) here is the community of shared suffering — knowledge of the brotherhood's suffering is itself a resource for endurance. Love of the brotherhood operates even through the knowledge that others in the community share the same suffering. *Check 1:* faith (R059), suffering (R214). *Check 4:* faith, suffering, and community-love in structural relationship.

Group 1610-001 COMPLETE: Key observation: the brotherhood is the community of love — 1Pe 2:17 places love of brotherhood and fear of God as the proper directional orientations of the two primary inner-being dispositions.

---

### Group 1611-001 — G5569 pseudadelfos (false brother)

**2Cor 11:26** — 'danger from false brothers.'

**OBS-103-067:** Paul lists false brothers (pseudadelfoi) among mortal dangers — alongside rivers, robbers, Gentiles. The false brother is dangerous precisely because they operate under the community's love vocabulary while their inner orientation is opposed to it. The inner deception is more dangerous than external threat because it uses love's own form against the community. *Check 4:* love and deception in structural opposition within the community form.

**Gal 2:4** — 'false brothers secretly brought in — who slipped in to spy out our freedom that we have in Christ Jesus, so that they might bring us into slavery.'

**OBS-103-068:** The false brothers are motivated by a project of enslavement — they use the community's love-framework to access and undermine its freedom. The inner orientation is agenda-driven (bondage) disguised as community-membership. Cross-registry: bondage (R017). *Check 1:* R017 (bondage).

Group 1611-001 COMPLETE: Key observation: the false brother is love's most dangerous negation — using the community form to serve an opposed inner agenda. Love's greatest vulnerability is its openness.

---

### Group 1614-001 — H7349 rachum (compassionate)

**Exo 34:6** — 'The Lord passed before him and proclaimed, "The Lord, the Lord, a God merciful and gracious, slow to anger, and abounding in steadfast love and faithfulness."'

**OBS-103-069:** The divine self-declaration formula names rachum (merciful/compassionate) as the first inner attribute. The list: rachum + channun (gracious) + erek-appayim (slow-to-anger) + rab-chesed (abounding-in-steadfast-love) + emet (faithfulness). Five attributes; all inner-being; all relational in structure. This is the programme's densest cross-registry verse: anger (4), compassion (23), love/chesed (103), faithfulness (60), grace (68). All five registries in one verse. SD-019 already raised. The rachum declaration grounds God's identity in compassionate love-orientation toward the afflicted. *Check 1:* All five registries. *Check 4:* five inner-being dispositions structurally co-present as divine character.

**Psa 78:38** — 'Yet he, being compassionate (rachum), atoned for their iniquity and did not destroy them; he restrained his anger often and did not stir up all his wrath.'

**OBS-103-070:** Compassion (rachum) here produces three consequential acts: atonement, restraint of destruction, restraint of anger. The rachum disposition is not merely felt — it is causally operative: it produces the mercy-outcome. Cross-registry: anger (R004), guilt/iniquity (R073). *Check 3:* Causal — compassion → atonement + restraint. *Check 4:* compassion and anger in structural relationship — rachum holds back the anger that iniquity would otherwise trigger.

Group 1614-001 COMPLETE: Key observation: rachum in the divine portrait is the primary named inner orientation from which gracious and restraining acts flow — it is dispositional (character) before it is active (act).

---

### Group 1617-001 — H7453 rea (neighbor)

**Lev 19:18** — 'You shall not take vengeance or bear a grudge against the sons of your own people, but you shall love your neighbor as yourself: I am the Lord.'

**OBS-103-071:** The neighbor-love commandment prohibits two inner-being states (vengeance, grudge-bearing) before commanding love. The inner preparation for love of neighbor is the renunciation of its inner opposites — vengeance (nakam, an inner-being act) and grudge (natar — to hold/keep, inner harboring of resentment). Love of neighbor requires an inner clearing first. The 'as yourself' standard introduces self-love as the measure — not a command but a comparative: the care you give your own inner person is the standard for care toward the neighbor. *Check 4:* vengeance/grudge and love in structural opposition — love of neighbor requires inner clearing of its blockers.

**Jer 31:34** — 'And no longer shall each one teach his neighbor and each his brother, saying, "Know the Lord," for they shall all know me, from the least of them to the greatest, declares the Lord. For I will forgive their iniquity, and I will remember their sin no more.'

**OBS-103-072:** In the new covenant, neighbor-teaching of God-knowledge (the current form of love-in-community) is superseded by direct divine knowledge. The eschatological love-community is one where God's knowledge of each person is direct, universal, and accompanied by total forgiveness. The neighbor's role in mediating love-knowledge is made redundant not by its failure but by its fulfilment. Cross-registry: knowledge (R100), forgiveness (R064), covenant (R034). SD-018 already raised. *Check 1:* R100, R064, R034.

Group 1617-001 COMPLETE: Key observation: neighbor-love is the primary ethical form of the inner love-orientation — it requires inner clearing of vengeance/grudge, and in the new covenant is fulfilled eschatologically through direct divine knowledge and forgiveness.

---

### Groups 1619-001 (mere.a), 1623-001 (reeh), 1624-001 (reah)

**2Sa 3:8 (mere.a)** — Abner shows steadfast love (chesed) to the house of Saul despite accusations. Companion/loyal-friend vocabulary in the context of political loyalty under pressure. Key: chesed and mere.a (companion) co-occur — covenantal loyalty expressed through friendship.

**Pro 19:7 (mere.a)** — poverty destroys friendships — friends go far. Inner observation: the companion-bond (mere.a) is evidenced by its persistence under adversity; its failure under poverty reveals its conditional nature.

**OBS-103-073:** The mere.a/reeh/reah vocabulary (companion/friend) in Hebrew names the relational bond as evidenced by its persistence under pressure. Loyal friendship (Pro 27:6 — wounds of a friend) and adversity-tested friendship (Pro 19:7) both test the inner orientation. The true companion is revealed by what they do when love is costly.

**2Sa 15:37 and 16:16 (reeh)** — Hushai, David's friend, places himself in Absalom's court at David's request. Loyal friendship expressed through personal risk. The inner-being content: friendship as the ground of courageous, self-sacrificial action for the beloved's sake.

**Judg 11:37-38 (reah)** — Jephthah's daughter and her companions in communal grief. The reah (companion) accompanies another in lamentation — present to grief, not fleeing it. *Check 5:* Somatic — companions in shared weeping. *Check 4:* love/companionship and grief in structural co-presence.

Groups 1619-001, 1623-001, 1624-001 COMPLETE: Key observation: the Hebrew friend/companion vocabulary consistently tests love through adversity — the true companion is present in grief, willing to risk, maintaining loyalty under pressure.

---

### Group 1651-001 — G1518 eirēnopoios (peacemaker)

**Mat 5:9** — 'Blessed are the peacemakers, for they shall be called sons of God.'

**OBS-103-074:** The peacemaker is the person-type whose inner orientation produces peace outward — they make peace (eirēnopoios — active, productive). The beatitude outcome ('shall be called sons of God') grounds the peacemaker's identity in divine sonship — the same pattern seen in agapētos (beloved → identity as beloved). The peacemaker is child-of-God through their inner orientation of peace-making love. *Check 1:* peace (R117), calling/identity (R019). *Check 4:* love-as-peacemaking and divine-identity in structural relationship.

Group 1651-001 COMPLETE: Key observation: peacemaking as the outward expression of the inner love-orientation — constituting the person as a son of God.

---

### Group 1663-001 — H8131 sena (to hate)

**Dan 4:19** — Daniel's interpretation of Nebuchadnezzar's dream: 'may the dream be for those who hate you and its interpretation for your enemies!'

**OBS-103-075:** Daniel uses the hate vocabulary (sena) to distinguish friend from enemy in the political context. The inner disposition of hatred is directed outward (toward the king's enemies) as a prayer. This is not the 'holy hatred of evil' seen in Psa 97:10 but a personal-relational hatred — the wish for an adversary's ill. *Check 4:* friendship/loyalty and hatred in structural opposition — Daniel's love for the king expressed through his wish that the hateful dream falls on the king's haters.

Group 1663-001 COMPLETE: Key observation: sena here names the adversarial-hatred of the politically opposed — the inner disposition that constitutes enmity.

---

### Group 1671-001 — G4416 prōtotokos (firstborn)

**Rom 8:29** — 'For those whom he foreknew he also predestined to be conformed to the image of his Son, in order that he might be the firstborn among many brothers.'

**OBS-103-076:** Christ as firstborn (prōtotokos) among brothers — the love-community (brothers) is defined by conformity to the image of the Son who is first among them. The divine predestination here is a predestination of love: God foreknew (relational knowledge) and predestined to likeness of the Son (conformity to the image of the beloved). Cross-registry: likeness/image (R209), calling (R19). *Check 1:* R209, R019. *Check 4:* divine foreknowledge, love, and image-conformity in a single causal chain.

**Col 1:15** — 'He is the image of the invisible God, the firstborn of all creation.'

**OBS-103-077:** Christ as image (eikōn) of the invisible God and firstborn of creation — the love-vocabulary of firstborn and beloved is here given its highest referent: the Son who is both the image of God and the first of the new creation. *Check 1:* R209 (image/likeness). *Check 4:* image and firstborn in structural relationship — the Son's identity as beloved is also his identity as image.

Group 1671-001 COMPLETE: Key observation: firstborn vocabulary connects love to image — the beloved Son is the image of God; believers conformed to his image are constituted as brothers.

---

### Group 1679-001 — G4415 prōtotokia (birthright)

**Heb 12:16** — 'that no one is sexually immoral or unholy like Esau, who sold his birthright for a single meal.'

**OBS-103-078:** Esau's sale of the birthright is named as profanity (bebēlos — unholy) — a disordering of love's hierarchy. The birthright represents the covenantal-relational inheritance (being the beloved son through whom the covenant continues). Its sale for immediate appetite (trophe — food) is the paradigmatic act of disordered love: immediate appetite (desire for food) overriding the permanent covenantal love-inheritance. Cross-registry: appetite (R008). *Check 4:* appetite/desire and covenantal love-inheritance in structural opposition — immediate desire displaces long-term love.

Group 1679-001 COMPLETE: Key observation: the birthright is the inheritance of covenantal love — its disposal reveals inner contempt for love's permanent covenantal structure in favour of immediate appetite.

---

### Group 2898-001 — H2898 tuv (divine goodness)

**Exo 33:19** — 'I will make all my goodness pass before you and will proclaim before you my name "The Lord." And I will be gracious to whom I will be gracious, and will show mercy on whom I will show mercy.'

**OBS-103-079:** Divine goodness (tuv) is here displayed in a theophany — God's goodness passes before Moses as a visible manifestation of the divine inner character. Goodness is co-present with grace and mercy (related to the racham-chesed cluster). The passing-before is the same structural movement as Exo 34:6 (divine self-declaration). *Check 1:* compassion (R023), grace (related to calling/R019). *Check 4:* goodness, grace, and mercy structurally co-present as divine character attributes.

**Psa 27:13** — 'I believe that I shall look upon the goodness of the Lord in the land of the living!'

**OBS-103-080:** The believer's anticipation: 'I shall look upon the goodness of the Lord.' Divine goodness (tuv) is here an object of eschatological vision — the inner orientation of hope directed toward God's goodness. The 'land of the living' places this vision in the present-but-future: the psalmist's confidence that the love expressed through divine goodness will be seen. *Check 1:* hope (R078). *Check 4:* love/goodness and hope in structural relationship — hope directed toward the future manifestation of love.

**Jer 31:14** — 'I will feast the soul of the priests with abundance, and my people shall be satisfied with my goodness.'

**OBS-103-081:** God's goodness satisfies the soul (nephesh) — the inner person is filled/satiated by the experience of divine goodness/love. The verb 'satisfied' (sava — to be full) is strong: love expressed as goodness produces fullness in the soul, not merely comfort. *Check 1:* Soul (R182). *Check 4:* love/goodness and soul in structural relationship — love satisfies the soul's deepest hunger.

**Hos 3:5** — 'Afterward the children of Israel shall return and seek the Lord their God, and David their king, and they shall come in fear to the Lord and to his goodness in the latter days.'

**OBS-103-082:** Eschatological return: Israel comes in fear to the Lord and to his goodness. The pairing — fear AND goodness — both receive Israel's return. This is a significant inner-being pairing: fear and love/goodness are not opposed here but co-directed. Adds texture to SP-103-029 (love-fear): the final-days picture has Israel coming with both fear and love (toward God's goodness) as complementary inner orientations. *Check 4:* fear and love/goodness as complementary orientations toward God — not in opposition but in integrated worship.

Group 2898-001 COMPLETE: Key observation: divine goodness (tuv) is love's attribute-face — God's goodness satisfies the soul's deepest hunger, is visible in theophany, and is the eschatological object of the believer's hope.


---

### Groups 533-001 (H1730H dod — love-relationship full range), 534-001 (H3039A yadid — beloved), 535-001 (H3033 yedidut — beloved of God's soul)

**Group 533-001 — H1730H dod (beloved: love)**

**Isa 5:1** — 'Let me sing for my beloved my love song concerning his vineyard: My beloved had a vineyard on a very fertile hill.'

**OBS-103-083:** Isaiah's vineyard song opens with the lover's lament for the beloved's disappointing vineyard — Israel as God's beloved (dod) who failed to produce the expected fruit. The love-language (dod, shir leDodi — love song for my beloved) is the frame within which prophetic judgment is delivered. Love's grief and disappointment are as present in the vocabulary as love's delight. The beloved who disappoints is still the beloved. *Check 4:* love and grief/disappointment in structural co-presence — love does not cease with disappointment.

**Eze 16:8** — 'When I passed by you again and saw you, behold, you were at the age for love, and I spread the corner of my garment over you and covered your nakedness; I made my vow to you and entered into a covenant with you, declares the Lord God, and you became mine.'

**OBS-103-083b:** God's love for Israel is expressed through covenant-marriage imagery: seeing, covering nakedness (protection), making a vow, entering covenant, and possession ('you became mine'). The love vocabulary (et dodim — the time of love) is covenantal — it produces the covenant structure. Love here is not the consequence of covenant but its generative act: God's love for Israel creates the covenant. This is one of the programme's most explicit statements that love is prior to and generative of covenant. *Check 1:* covenant (R034). *Check 4:* love and covenant in generative relationship — love produces covenant, not merely accompanies it.

SP raised: Eze 16:8 — love as generative of covenant.

**SP-103-032** — raised in Unit 7, 2026-04-30, HIGH, Session D
- Target: R034 (covenant) / R103 (love)
- Connecting term: H1730H dod / berit (covenant)
- Question: Eze 16:8 portrays God's love (time of love, dod) as prior to and generative of the covenant ('I made my vow to you and entered into a covenant with you'). Is love structurally prior to covenant in the OT's covenantal architecture — love as the inner disposition that produces the covenant-act? If so, love is not merely the emotional dimension of the covenant relationship but its constitutional ground. Does the programme's covenant registry (34) treat love as the prior act? Cross-registry: love (103), covenant (34).
- Evidence basis: OBS-103-083b

**Group 534-001 — H3039A yadid (beloved)**

**Psa 127:2** — 'It is in vain that you rise up early and go late to rest, eating the bread of anxious toil; for he gives to his beloved sleep.'

**OBS-103-084:** God gives sleep to his beloved (yadid) — effortlessly, as a love-gift. The contrast is between anxious self-effort (bread of anxious toil) and the restful reception of a love-gift from God. The inner-being state of being-beloved produces rest rather than striving. *Check 4:* love/belovedness and rest in structural relationship — being-loved produces peace/rest in the beloved. Cross-registry: peace (R117).

**Jer 11:15** — 'What right has my beloved in my house, when she has done many vile deeds? Can even sacrificial flesh avert your doom? Can you then exult?'

**OBS-103-085:** God addresses Israel as 'my beloved' (yadidah) even in the context of judgment — the beloved relationship persists through moral failure. The rhetorical question ('what right has my beloved in my house') is anguished, not dismissive: the beloved still has a claim; the question is whether that claim overrides the moral failure. Love's persistence through the beloved's unfaithfulness is one of the OT's most distinctive theological claims. *Check 4:* love and judgment in structural tension — love persists; judgment remains necessary.

**Group 535-001 — H3033 yedidut (beloved of God's soul)**

**Jer 12:7** — 'I have forsaken my house; I have abandoned my heritage; I have given the beloved of my soul into the hands of her enemies.'

**OBS-103-086:** 'Beloved of my soul' (yedidut naphshi) — God's inner person (nephesh/soul) has a beloved. The abandonment language ('I have given… into the hands of her enemies') is God's own grieving statement — a divine lament. This is the programme's most concentrated statement of divine love-loss: God's soul has a beloved; God's act of giving that beloved to enemies is simultaneously an act of judgment and an act of grief. DIM-103-002 (§N item) is grounded here. The vocabulary applies the programme's human inner-being categories (soul, beloved) to the divine subject. *Check 1:* Soul (R182), grief (R071). *Check 4:* divine love and divine grief in structural co-presence — God's love and God's grief are held together in a single act.

SP raised: the divine grief of abandoned love.

**SP-103-033** — raised in Unit 7, 2026-04-30, HIGH, Session D
- Target: R071 (grief) / R103 (love)
- Connecting term: H3033 yedidut / H5315 nephesh
- Question: Jer 12:7 — God abandons the beloved of his soul to her enemies. The verse uses grief vocabulary ('forsaken,' 'abandoned,' 'given') for a divine inner act. Does the programme's grief registry (71) contain evidence of divine grief as an inner-being phenomenon — not merely as metaphor but as a genuinely attributed inner state? If so, what is the structural relationship between divine love and divine grief — are they the same inner orientation viewed under the condition of the beloved's loss? Cross-registry: love (103), grief (71), Soul (182).
- Evidence basis: OBS-103-086; DIM-103-002

Groups 533-001, 534-001, 535-001 COMPLETE: Key observation: the dod/yadid/yedidut vocabulary names love as God's inner orientation toward Israel — a love that produces covenant, persists through failure, and grieves at its own enforced withdrawal.
