### Groups 536-001, 536-002, 536-003 — H2617A chesed (steadfast love — three groups)

**Group 536-001 (chesed — divine)**

**Psa 63:3** — 'Because your steadfast love (chesed) is better than life, my lips will praise you.'

**OBS-103-087:** Chesed is valued 'better than life' (tov chasedcha mimchayim). Life (chayim) is the highest natural good — yet the psalmist ranks God's chesed above it. This is the strongest superlative comparison in the love vocabulary: chesed exceeds the value of life itself. The inner-being consequence: praise is the natural response to a love so valued. *Check 4:* love and praise in structural relationship — love so valued produces praise. Cross-registry: praise (R121).

**Lam 3:22** — 'The steadfast love (chesed) of the Lord never ceases; his mercies (rachamim) never come to an end.'

**OBS-103-088:** Chesed and rachamim (mercies/compassions) are paired — love and compassion are grammatically co-ordinate in the OT's most famous statement of God's faithfulness. The 'never ceases' and 'never come to an end' — written in the context of Lamentations' devastation — ground God's love in permanence against the evidence of destruction. The inner-being content: love as permanent orientation, not feeling-contingent. *Check 4:* love and compassion as structurally co-ordinate divine attributes.

**Group 536-002 (chesed — human)**

**Rut 3:10** — 'You have made this last kindness (chesed) greater than the first in that you have not gone after young men.'

**OBS-103-089:** Ruth's loyalty to Boaz is named as chesed — covenantal loyalty expressed through relational choice. The comparison ('greater than the first') reveals that chesed is measurable, gradable — love can increase in its expression. Ruth's chesed is her commitment to the covenantal bond over self-interest (she could have pursued younger men). *Check 4:* chesed and choice/will in structural relationship — love expressed through the exercise of will against self-interest.

**Pro 3:3** — 'Let not steadfast love (chesed) and faithfulness (emet) forsake you; bind them around your neck; write them on the tablet of your heart.'

**OBS-103-090:** Chesed and emet (faithfulness/truth) are paired — love and faithfulness as co-ordinate inner dispositions to be inscribed on the heart. The writing-on-heart image is the OT's primary metaphor for the inner-being's deepest inscriptions. Chesed is not a feeling but a character quality that must be held, maintained, not allowed to 'forsake.' *Check 4:* love and faithfulness in structural pairing as heart-inscribed inner character.

**Group 536-003 (chesed — failure/demand)**

**Hos 6:6** — 'For I desire steadfast love (chesed) and not sacrifice, the knowledge of God rather than burnt offerings.'

**OBS-103-091:** God's self-disclosure: I desire chesed and da'at (knowledge of God) above ritual. Chesed is placed above sacrifice — the inner orientation of love is God's priority over the outward form of worship. Cross-registry: knowledge (R100). *Check 4:* love and knowledge of God in structural co-priority over ritual. The chesed-da'at pairing here is one of the OT's most significant inner-being statements.

**Mic 6:8** — 'He has told you, O man, what is good; and what does the Lord require of you but to do justice, and to love kindness (chesed), and to walk humbly with your God?'

**OBS-103-092:** The Mic 6:8 triad: mishpat (justice) + chesed (love kindness) + hatznea lechet (walk humbly). Three requirements; three inner orientations. Chesed is the only one that carries an inner-being directional verb: 'love kindness' (ahav chesed) — love is the inner act directed toward chesed as its object. The triple structure has already generated SD-006. This verse names love-of-love as the inner requirement: not merely practicing chesed but loving it. *Check 1:* justice (not currently a separate registry in C17 — gap?), humility (R080). *Check 4:* love, justice, and humility as co-ordinate requirements of the inner life.

Groups 536-001 through 536-003 COMPLETE: Key observation: chesed spans divine and human subjects, is ranked above life itself (Psa 63:3), is permanently reliable (Lam 3:22), is expressed through the will against self-interest (Ruth), is heart-inscribed (Pro 3:3), and is God's stated priority above ritual (Hos 6:6, Mic 6:8).

---

### Groups 537-001, 537-002, 537-003 — H0160 ahavah (love)

**Group 537-001 (ahavah — divine love for people)**

**Jer 31:3** — 'I have loved you with an everlasting love (ahavat olam); therefore I have continued my faithfulness (chesed) to you.'

**OBS-103-093:** Ahavah (love) and chesed (faithfulness) are presented in causal sequence: everlasting love → continuing faithfulness. Love precedes and produces faithfulness. The 'everlasting' (olam — duration beyond time) qualifier makes ahavah the most permanent inner disposition named in the OT. *Check 3:* Causal — ahavat olam → chesed continued. *Check 4:* love and faithfulness in generative relationship.

**Zep 3:17** — 'The Lord your God is in your midst, a mighty one who will save; he will rejoice over you with gladness; he will quiet you by his love; he will exult over you with loud singing.'

**OBS-103-094:** God's love for Israel produces four internal-to-God effects: rejoicing, gladness, quieting, and exulting-in-singing. The 'quiet you by his love' (yacharish beahavato — he will be silent in his love, or: he will calm you in his love) is one of the most striking descriptions in the OT: God's love is not noisy — it quiets. The inner movement is: divine love produces rest/stillness in the beloved. SD-012 already raised. *Check 4:* love and peace/rest in structural relationship. *Check 1:* joy (R097), peace (R117).

**Group 537-002 (ahavah — intense mutual love)**

**2Sa 1:26** — 'I am distressed for you, my brother Jonathan; very pleasant have you been to me; your love to me was extraordinary, surpassing the love of women.'

**OBS-103-095:** David's lament for Jonathan identifies love (ahavah) by its comparative intensity: Jonathan's love exceeded the love of women (the most intimate natural love David knew). The lament is grief's evidence for love: David's inner anguish at Jonathan's death reveals the depth of the prior love. SD-017 already raised. *Check 4:* love and grief in structural relationship — grief is love's evidence under loss. *Check 1:* grief (R071).

**Song 8:6** — 'Set me as a seal upon your heart, as a seal upon your arm, for love is strong as death, jealousy is fierce as the grave. Its flashes are flashes of fire, the very flame of the Lord.'

**OBS-103-096:** The Song's climax: love (ahavah) as strong as death; jealousy (qinah) fierce as Sheol; love as the very flame of the Lord (shalhevetyah). Three structural claims: (1) love matches death in power — neither can be resisted; (2) jealousy is love's attendant force — the fierceness of attachment; (3) love is of divine origin (yah-flame). This is the OT's most concentrated statement about love's ultimate nature. PH2-103-006 already raised (Song study needed). *Check 1:* envy/jealousy (R_unknown — qinah). *Check 4:* love and death in comparative power relationship; love and divine nature in constitutive connection.

SP raised: Song 8:6 — love as strong as death and the divine nature of love's flame.

**SP-103-034** — raised in Unit 7, 2026-04-30, HIGH, Session D
- Target: R103 (love) / envy-jealousy registry (qinah — registry unknown) / divine nature
- Connecting term: H0160 ahavah / H7068 qinah (jealousy)
- Question: Song 8:6 says love is as strong as death and its flame is the flame of the Lord (shalhevetyah). Two analytical questions: (a) Does the programme have a registry for qinah (jealousy/zeal)? If so, Song 8:6 makes jealousy love's structural companion force — as fierce as Sheol in the same way love is strong as death. (b) The shalhevetyah ('flame of Yah') claim: does Scripture elsewhere ground love's power in the divine nature? If so, this verse supports 1Jo 4:8 ('God is love') from the OT side. Cross-registry: love (103), jealousy/zeal registry (if present).
- Evidence basis: OBS-103-096

**Group 537-003 (ahavah — moral loyalty)**

**Pro 10:12** — 'Hatred stirs up strife, but love covers all offenses.'

**OBS-103-097:** Love and hatred in direct structural opposition with contrasting effects: hatred stirs up (ya'or) strife; love covers (yechasse) all offenses. The inner orientations have opposite social-relational effects. Love here is not emotional but moral — it covers offenses (forgives, overlooks, does not expose). *Check 4:* love and hatred in causal-opposite relationship — each has a characteristic social effect. Cross-registry: hatred (via sane — R103 own), forgiveness (R064).

**Jer 2:2** — 'I remember the devotion of your youth, your love as a bride, how you followed me in the wilderness, in a land not sown.'

**OBS-103-098:** God recalls Israel's early love (ahavat kelulotayich — love of your bridehood) in the wilderness. The wilderness-following is the love-evidence: going after God into a place of danger and non-provision. Love is evidenced by following under conditions of scarcity. *Check 4:* love and trust/dependence in structural relationship — love expressed through following into the unknown.

Groups 537-001 through 537-003 COMPLETE: Key observation: ahavah spans divine everlasting love (permanent, faithful), human intense love (matched only by grief when lost), and moral loyalty (covering offenses, following in the wilderness). Song 8:6 names love as divine in origin and equal in power to death.

### Groups 539-001 (H0158 ahav — lover), 540-001 (H2623 chasid — pious person), 542-001 (H2895 tov — pleasing)

**Group 539-001 — lover**

**Pro 5:19** — 'Let her breasts fill you at all times with delight; be intoxicated always in her love.'

**OBS-103-099:** Marital love as intoxication — the physical delight of the beloved as the context of the love-metaphor. The inner-being state is pleasure/delight expressed through embodied intimacy. This is Proverbs' positive affirmation of erotic marital love as the proper channel for the love-mechanism. *Check 5:* somatic — embodied love as the appropriate form of marital attachment.

**Hos 8:9** — 'Ephraim has hired lovers.'

**OBS-103-100:** The hired lover (ahav — mshacared love) is the corrupted form — love bought and sold, detached from covenant. This is the prophetic vocabulary for Israel's spiritual infidelity: treating God's love as something purchasable, substitutable. *Check 4:* covenantal love and mercenary love in structural opposition.

**Group 540-001 — chasid (pious person)**

**Psa 4:3** — 'But know that the Lord has set apart the godly (chasid) for himself; the Lord hears when I call to him.'

**OBS-103-101:** The chasid is set apart by God for himself — the godly person is defined by being the object of God's love-attention. The Lord's hearing of the chasid's call is the evidence of the love-relationship. *Check 3:* Passive — 'has set apart' — divine act constitutes the chasid's identity. *Check 4:* love and hearing/prayer in structural relationship — God's love toward the chasid expresses itself as attentive listening.

**Psa 16:10** — 'For you will not abandon my soul (nephesh) to Sheol, or let your holy one (chasid) see corruption.'

**OBS-103-102:** The chasid's soul (nephesh) will not be abandoned to Sheol — God's love for the holy one extends beyond death. This is the OT's most explicit statement that God's love reaches into death itself. *Check 1:* Soul (R182). *Check 4:* love and death in structural relationship — love persists beyond death for the beloved.

**Group 542-001 — tov (be pleasing)**

**1Ki 8:18** — 'Whereas it was in your heart to build a house for my name, you did well that it was in your heart.'

**OBS-103-103:** God accepts David's inner intention ('it was in your heart') even though the outward act was not performed. The inner-being content: God's love responds to and approves the heart's orientation even before its external expression. Love operates at the level of the inner person's intention, not only at the level of accomplished action.

**Psa 119:71** — 'It is good for me that I was afflicted, that I might learn your statutes.'

**OBS-103-104:** The afflicted person perceives their affliction as 'good' (tov) because of its learning outcome. This is a complex inner-being assessment: love of God's ways is so strong that even painful discipline is received as 'good.' *Check 4:* affliction and love-of-God's-ways in structural relationship — love reframes suffering.

Groups 539-001, 540-001, 542-001 COMPLETE: Key observation: the lover/chasid/tov vocabulary confirms that love operates at the level of inner intention (1Ki 8:18), extends beyond death (Psa 16:10), and can reframe suffering as good (Psa 119:71).

---

### Group 544-001 — H7356B rachamim (divine compassion)

**1Ki 3:26** — 'Then the woman whose son was alive said to the king, because her heart yearned (nichmeruh rachameyha) for her son, "Oh, my lord, give her the living child."'

**OBS-103-105:** The mother's rachamim (compassions — plural intensive) for her child cause her 'heart to yearn' (nichmeruh — root: chamar, to be heated/moved). The inner-being sequence: rachamim activated → heart heated/moved → volitional speech ('give her the child'). This is a non-divine instance of rachamim — the same inner structure seen in God's compassion is here operating in the human mother. The womb-etymology is explicitly active: the woman whose womb produced the child has her womb-compassion (rachamim) activated when the child is threatened. *Check 4:* rachamim and will/speech in causal relationship — compassion produces volitional action.

**Isa 63:15** — 'Where are your zeal and your might? The stirring of your inner parts (me'eka) and your compassion (rachamim) are held back from me.'

**OBS-103-106:** Israel pleads for God's rachamim — specifically noting that what is being held back is God's 'inner parts' (me'eka — literally bowels/entrails, the seat of deepest emotion) and his compassion. The anatomy of divine emotion: me'eka (inner organs) + rachamim = the physical-inner location of divine compassion. This is the OT's most explicit anatomical language for the divine inner life. *Check 5:* somatic — the divine inner organs (me'eka) as the location of compassion. *Check 4:* divine might and divine compassion in structural tension — compassion is withheld when might/wrath operates.

SP raised: Isa 63:15 — divine inner organs and the somatic vocabulary for divine emotion.

**SP-103-035** — raised in Unit 7, 2026-04-30, MEDIUM, Session D
- Target: R023 (compassion) / R103 (love)
- Connecting term: H7356B rachamim / me'eka (inner organs)
- Question: Isa 63:15 uses me'eka (inner organs/bowels) as the somatic location of God's rachamim (compassion). Does the programme's vocabulary for divine inner states include somatic language that would normally be assigned to human anatomy? If so, does the me'eka vocabulary for divine emotion parallel the nephesh (soul) vocabulary for divine love (Jer 12:7)? Together these may evidence a consistent pattern: Scripture attributes inner-being states to God using the same anatomical vocabulary used for humans. Cross-registry: love (103), compassion (23).
- Evidence basis: OBS-103-106

Group 544-001 COMPLETE: Key observation: rachamim in human and divine subjects uses the same inner-being mechanism — the womb/inner-organ activation that produces compassion-driven action. Isa 63:15 explicitly names God's inner organs as the location of his compassion.


---

### Groups 545-001 (rayah), 547-001 (naeh), 548-001 (agavah), 549-001 (naim)

**Group 545-001 — H7474 rayah (darling/beloved — Song)**

**Song 4:7** — 'You are altogether beautiful, my love (rayati); there is no flaw in you.'

**OBS-103-107:** The beloved (rayah — my darling/love, feminine address) is declared wholly beautiful — 'no flaw.' This is love's total positive assessment of the beloved. The language of flawlessness (mum — blemish, defect) is drawn from sacrificial vocabulary — the beloved is described as the sacrificial animal fit for offering. The love vocabulary and the holiness vocabulary share the same perfection-standard. *Check 4:* love and holiness/perfection in structural connection through the blemish-language.

**Song 5:2** — 'I slept, but my heart was awake. A sound! My beloved (dodi) is knocking. "Open to me, my sister, my love (rayati), my dove, my perfect one."'

**OBS-103-108:** The beloved speaks while asleep — 'my heart was awake.' The inner person (heart/lev) persists in love-awareness even in sleep. The multiple address terms (sister, love, dove, perfect one) applied to the single beloved reveal the multidimensional relational identity that love creates: the beloved is simultaneously sister (relational family), rayah (darling/companion), dove (purity/gentleness), and perfect one (tamah — complete). *Check 4:* love as multidimensional identity-constituting — the beloved receives multiple relational names simultaneously. *Check 1:* R182 (Soul/heart consciousness in sleep).

**Group 547-001 — H5000 naeh (lovely/becoming)**

**Psa 33:1** — 'Shout for joy in the Lord, O you righteous! Praise befits (naeh) the upright.'

**OBS-103-109:** Naeh (lovely/befitting) here describes what is fitting or appropriate — praise is naeh for the righteous. The inner sense of fittingness is an aesthetic-moral judgment: what is naeh is what is right and beautiful simultaneously. *Check 4:* love/aesthetic-fittingness and righteousness in structural connection — what is right is also beautiful.

**Song 2:14** — 'Let me hear your voice, for your voice is sweet, and your face is lovely (naeh).'

**OBS-103-110:** The beloved's voice and face are naeh — lovely. The love-vocabulary here is fully aesthetic: the beloved's physical presence is beautiful. The inner-being state is delight in the beloved's sensory presence — hearing the voice, seeing the face. Somatic convergence: love through hearing and sight.

**Group 548-001 — H5691 agavah (lust)**

**Eze 23:11** — 'Her sister Oholibah saw this, and she became more corrupt than her sister in her lust (agavah) and in her whoring, which was worse than that of her sister.'

**OBS-103-111:** Agavah (lust) is the corrupted form of love — the inner desire that drives spiritual adultery. Oholibah's agavah is worse than Oholah's — lust admits of degree. The inner state is named as both a quality (agavah — noun: the lust) and an act (her whoring). The love mechanism (inner attachment, giving of self) is fully present; the object (Assyrian political alliances as spiritual infidelity) is radically disordered. *Check 4:* love's proper form (covenantal) and its corrupted form (lust) in structural opposition.

**Group 549-001 — H5273A naim (pleasant)**

**Psa 16:11** — 'You make known to me the path of life; in your presence there is fullness of joy; at your right hand are pleasures forevermore.'

**OBS-103-112:** The path of life leads to God's presence where 'fullness of joy' (sova semachot) and 'pleasures forevermore' (naim — pleasant things) are found. The inner-being state in God's presence is fullness — not partial but complete joy. *Check 4:* love/pleasure and joy and God's presence in structural co-presence. *Check 1:* joy (R097).

**Psa 133:1** — 'Behold, how good and pleasant it is when brothers dwell in unity!'

**OBS-103-113:** The fraternal unity of brothers dwelling together is called both good (tov) and pleasant (naim). The inner-being experience of community love is pleasure/delight — not duty but felt goodness. The 'behold' (hineh) draws attention to something observable: the pleasantness of love-in-community is visible, not merely felt inwardly. *Check 4:* love/community and goodness and joy in structural co-presence.

Groups 545-001, 547-001, 548-001, 549-001 COMPLETE: Key observation: the Song vocabulary names love through aesthetic categories (lovely, pleasant, beautiful, sweet) — love perceives the beloved as wholly fitting, beautiful, and delightful. The corrupted form (agavah) uses the same inner mechanism with a disordered object.

---

### Groups 550-001 (H8130 sane — hate), 551-001 (H7355 racham — to have compassion)

**Group 550-001 — H8130 sane (to hate)**

**Lev 19:17** — 'You shall not hate your brother in your heart, but you shall reason frankly with your neighbor, lest you incur sin because of him.'

**OBS-103-114:** The hate commandment targets the inner disposition ('in your heart') — not merely the outer act. The alternative to hatred is not silence but frank speech (hocheach tochi'ach — rebuke/reason with). The inner choice is: hate (silent, harbored) vs. frank correction (active, honest). Love expresses itself as honest engagement; hatred conceals itself as silence. *Check 4:* love and frank speech in structural relationship; hatred and silence in structural relationship.

**Psa 97:10** — 'O you who love the Lord, hate evil! He preserves the lives of his saints; he delivers them from the hand of the wicked.'

**OBS-103-115:** The command: those who love the Lord must hate evil. The inner orientation of love toward God requires the inner orientation of hatred toward evil — the two are structurally co-ordinated. Love and holy hatred are not opposites but necessary partners in the ordered inner life. *Check 4:* love-of-God and hatred-of-evil in structural requirement — the proper direction of each confirms the other.

Group 550-001 COMPLETE: Key observation: sane (hatred) in the OT functions as a necessary inner companion to love — righteous hatred of evil is required of those who love God; hatred of the brother is the sin that frank love corrects.

**Group 551-001 — H7355 racham (to have compassion)**

**Isa 49:15** — 'Can a woman forget her nursing child, that she should have no compassion on the son of her womb? Even these may forget, yet I will not forget you.'

**OBS-103-116:** The most concentrated womb-compassion verse: the nursing mother's compassion (racham) for the son of her womb (rechem — physical womb) provides the standard — and then God exceeds it. Even the most powerful human love-bond (mother-infant) may fail; God's racham will not. *Check 5:* Somatic — nursing/womb as the bodily ground of the compassion vocabulary. *Check 4:* divine compassion and human compassion in comparative relationship — divine love exceeds even the most intense natural love-bond.

**Jer 31:20** — 'Is Ephraim my dear son? Is he my darling child? For as often as I speak against him, I do remember him still. Therefore my heart yearns (hamu me'ai — my inner parts are heated/moved) for him; I will surely have mercy on him, declares the Lord.'

**OBS-103-117:** God's inner parts (me'ai — same root as me'eka, Isa 63:15) are moved (hamu — to murmur, to be agitated) toward Ephraim. This is the companion verse to Isa 63:15 — the inner organs of God are the somatic location of his racham. The movement is involuntary in character: God remembers despite judgment-speech, his inner parts move despite the conflict between love and justice. *Check 5:* Somatic — divine inner organs activated by love/compassion for the wayward child. *Check 4:* divine justice (judgment-speech against Ephraim) and divine love (inner yearning for Ephraim) in structural tension — love persists through and alongside judgment.

Group 551-001 COMPLETE: Key observation: racham in Isa 49:15 and Jer 31:20 names a somatic-inner movement — the womb/inner-organs activated by love for the suffering or wayward child, explicitly used for divine experience.

---

### Group 553-001 (G5377 filotheos), 554-001 (G5387 filostorgos), 555-001/002 (G0027 agapētos)

**Group 553-001 — G5377 filotheos (God-loving)**

**2Ti 3:4** — 'treacherous, reckless, swollen with conceit, lovers of pleasure (filēdonoi) rather than lovers of God (filotheos).'

**OBS-103-118:** The antithesis: philotheos vs philēdonos — God-loving vs pleasure-loving. The philo-compound structure makes explicit that the inner mechanism (love/attachment toward) is identical in both; only the object differs. The last-days failure is not the absence of love but its misdirection — the same capacity for passionate attachment directed away from God toward pleasure. *Check 4:* love-of-God and love-of-pleasure in structural opposition — same mechanism, opposed objects.

**Group 554-001 — G5387 filostorgos (affectionate)**

**Rom 12:10** — 'Love one another with brotherly affection (filostorgoi). Outdo one another in showing honor.'

**OBS-103-119:** Filostorgos (family-affection love) + outdo in honor — love is the inner orientation; honor-showing is its competitive expression. The paradox: 'outdo one another' in showing honor — this is the only NT context where competition is commanded, and it is competition in self-giving rather than self-assertion. *Check 4:* love and honor in structural relationship — love expressed through competitive generosity in honor-giving.

**Group 555-001 — G0027 agapētos (Christ as Father's beloved)**

**Mat 3:17** — 'and behold, a voice from heaven said, "This is my beloved Son (ho huios mou ho agapētos), with whom I am well pleased."'

**OBS-103-120:** The Father declares three things about the Son: beloved (agapētos), Son (identity), and well-pleasing (eudokeō — to find pleasure in). The love-declaration ('my beloved Son') grounds Christ's identity. This is the programme's clearest statement that love constitutes identity: Christ is who he is as Son by virtue of the Father's love-declaration. SD-011 and SD-016 already raised. *Check 4:* divine love and identity in constitutive relationship — being-loved constitutes who the beloved is. *Check 1:* R019 (calling), Spirit (descends at the same moment).

**Mar 12:6** — 'He had still one other, a beloved son (huion agapēton). Finally he sent him to them, saying, "They will respect my son."'

**OBS-103-121:** In the parable of the vineyard, the owner sends his beloved son (agapēton huion) as the final act — love's most costly expression is the giving of the beloved. The beloved-son title is transferred from the divine context (Mat 3:17) to the parable context, making explicit the parallel: the Father gives his beloved Son (as in the parable, the owner gives his beloved son). *Check 4:* love and self-giving of the beloved in structural relationship — love's costliest form is the giving of what is most loved.

**Group 555-002 — G0027 agapētos (believers as beloved)**

**Rom 1:7** — 'To all those in Rome who are loved by God (agapētois theou) and called to be saints.'

**OBS-103-122:** Believers are named 'loved by God' (agapētoi theou) and 'called' (klētois) — the two identity terms are grammatically parallel: being-loved and being-called are structurally co-ordinate designations of the believer's identity. *Check 4:* love and calling in structural co-constitution of identity. *Check 1:* R019 (calling).

**1Th 2:8** — 'So, being affectionately desirous of you, we were ready to share with you not only the gospel of God but also our own selves (tas heautōn psuchas), because you had become very dear to us.'

**OBS-103-123:** Paul shares his own psuchas (souls) — not just the gospel but his own inner-being — because the Thessalonians had become 'very dear' (agapētoi). Love here produces the most radical self-giving: sharing one's soul. The connection: love → sharing of the self (psyche). *Check 1:* Soul (R182). *Check 4:* love and self-giving of soul in structural relationship — love's ultimate expression is the giving of the self/soul.

SP raised: 1Th 2:8 — love produces sharing of the soul/self.

**SP-103-036** — raised in Unit 7, 2026-04-30, MEDIUM, Session D
- Target: R182 (Soul) / R156 (surrender) / R103 (love)
- Connecting term: G0027 agapētos / psuchē (soul)
- Question: 1Th 2:8 — Paul is ready to share his own souls (psuchas) because the Thessalonians had become very dear (agapētoi). Love produces the sharing/surrender of the self-soul. Does this connect to Joh 15:13 ('greater love has no one than this: to lay down one's psuchē for his friends') — love as the inner movement that produces soul-surrender? Is there a structural sequence: love → surrender → giving of soul? Cross-registry: love (103), soul (182), surrender (156).
- Evidence basis: OBS-103-123

Groups 553-001 through 555-002 COMPLETE: Key observation: agapētos (beloved) is an identity-constituting term — Christ's identity as Son is grounded in the Father's love-declaration; believers' identity as beloved-and-called is their primary designation. Love expressed as the giving of the beloved (Mar 12:6) and the sharing of one's soul (1Th 2:8) is love at its costliest.

### Groups 556-001 (G5363 filanthrōpia), 558-001 (G5360 filadelfia), 559-001 (G5388 filoteknos), 560-001 (G5380 filoneikos), 561-001 (G5362 filandros)

**556-001 — Tit 3:4** — 'But when the goodness and loving kindness (filanthrōpia) of God our Savior appeared.' Divine love as manifest character. *Already noted structurally.*

**558-001 — 1Pe 1:22** — 'Having purified your souls by your obedience to the truth for a sincere brotherly love (filadelfia), love one another earnestly from a pure heart.' The purification sequence: obedience → purified souls → sincere brotherly love. *Check 3:* Causal — obedience and soul-purification as preconditions for authentic love. *Check 1:* Soul (R182).

**OBS-103-124:** 1Pe 1:22 provides the clearest evidential statement in the NT that love's inner authenticity requires prior inner formation — the soul must be purified for love to be sincere (anupokritē — without hypocrisy). Love's authenticity is not assumed; it is constituted by obedience and inner purification. *Check 4:* obedience, soul-purification, and sincere love in causal sequence.

**558-001 — Rom 12:10** — 'Love one another with brotherly affection.' Already noted under 554-001.

**559-001 — Tit 2:4** — 'and so train the young women to love their husbands and children.' Love as a trainable virtue — philandros (husband-loving) and philoteknos (child-loving) are inner dispositions to be formed through training. *Check 4:* love and formation/training in structural relationship — love is not merely natural but cultivated.

**560-001 — 1Cor 11:16** — 'If anyone is inclined to be contentious (filoneikos), we have no such practice.' The contentious/dispute-loving disposition is a named inner failure — love misdirected toward rivalry. Paul simply refuses to validate it by engaging with it. *Check 4:* love-of-dispute and communal order in structural opposition.

**561-001 — Tit 2:4** — Already noted above under 559-001.

Groups 556 through 561 COMPLETE: Key observation: the philo-compound groups in the NT epistles address love's formation as a domestic and communal practice — love of husband and children as trainable virtues; brotherly love as requiring prior soul-purification; contentious love as a named failure to be refused.

### Groups 562-001, 562-002, 562-003 — G0026 agapē (three groups)

**Group 562-001 — agapē: God's love as ground**

**Joh 15:13** — 'Greater love (agapē) has no one than this, that someone lay down his life (psuchēn) for his friends.'

**OBS-103-125:** The superlative of love: laying down the soul/life (psuchē). Love is defined by its maximum expression — the most costly possible self-giving. This verse defines love by its outer limit, not its typical expression. The beloved is specified: 'for his friends' — not for humanity in general but for those in the love-relationship. *Check 4:* love and soul-giving (psuchē) at maximum expression. *Check 1:* Soul (R182), surrender (R156).

**Rom 5:5** — 'God's love (agapē theou) has been poured into our hearts through the Holy Spirit who has been given to us.'

**OBS-103-126:** God's love is poured (ekkekhutai — perfect passive, permanently infused) into hearts through the Spirit. The inner-being mechanism: divine love enters the human inner person through the Spirit's action and remains there. The heart is the location of reception; the Spirit is the agent of infusion. *Check 4:* love, Spirit, and heart in structural connection — the Spirit is the medium through which divine love reaches the human heart. *Check 1:* R183 (heart), Spirit cluster.

SP raised: Rom 5:5 — Spirit as the medium of divine love's entry into the human inner being.

**SP-103-037** — raised in Unit 7, 2026-04-30, HIGH, Session D
- Target: Spirit cluster / R103 (love) / R183 (heart)
- Connecting term: G0026 agapē / G4151 pneuma (Spirit)
- Question: Rom 5:5 — God's love is poured into hearts through the Holy Spirit. Is the Spirit the structural mediator of divine love's entry into the human inner person across the programme's data? Does the Spirit function as the agent by which divine love becomes a human inner-being state? If so, the love-Spirit-heart connection is one of the programme's most significant cross-registry structural claims. Cross-registry: love (103), heart (183), Spirit cluster.
- Evidence basis: OBS-103-126

**Group 562-002 — agapē: defining inner virtue of believer**

**1Cor 13:4** — 'Love is patient and kind; love does not envy or boast; it is not arrogant.'

**OBS-103-127:** The 1Cor 13 definition proceeds by negation and affirmation. What love IS: patient (makrothumei — long-suffering), kind (chrēsteuetai). What love IS NOT: envying, boasting, arrogant, rude, self-seeking, irritable, resentful, rejoicing in wrongdoing. Every negative attribute named in 1Cor 13:4-7 has a potential registry in the programme (pride, envy, anger, resentment). The passage is a cross-registry map of love's absence as much as its presence. SD-014 already raised. *Check 1:* patience (R116), pride (R123), envy (R_unknown), kindness (R099).

**Gal 5:22** — 'But the fruit of the Spirit is love, joy, peace, patience, kindness, goodness, faithfulness.'

**OBS-103-128:** Love heads the fruit-of-Spirit list. The fruit is singular (karpos — one fruit, not many); the qualities are diverse expressions of one thing. SD-015 already raised. The singular/plural structure is analytically significant: 'the fruit is love, joy, peace' — not 'the fruits are.' Love may be the unifying quality from which all others flow. *Check 4:* love and all subsequent Spirit-fruits in generative relationship — love as the single fruit expressed in multiple forms.

**Group 562-003 — agapē: mutual love among believers**

**Joh 13:35** — 'By this all people will know that you are my disciples, if you have love for one another.'

**OBS-103-129:** The community's love for one another is publicly legible — it is the sign by which all people (pantas) know the disciples' identity. Love is the community's primary external mark. The inner-being reality (mutual love among believers) produces an outward community-identity that is readable by those outside. *Check 4:* love and discipleship-identity in structural relationship — love is the identifying mark.

**1Th 3:12** — 'May the Lord make you increase and abound in love for one another and for all, as we do for you.'

**OBS-103-130:** Love can increase (pleonasai — abound, exceed) — it admits of growth. The Lord's action makes the increase happen — love's growth is not purely self-generated but enabled. The scope: 'for one another and for all' — community love and universal love are held together. *Check 4:* love's capacity for growth in structural relationship with Lord's enabling action.

Groups 562-001 through 562-003 COMPLETE: Key observation: agapē groups reveal love's definitional maximum (soul-giving, Joh 15:13), its inner-being infusion by the Spirit (Rom 5:5), its self-definition as the opposite of pride/envy/boasting (1Cor 13), its generative position in the Spirit's fruit (Gal 5:22), and its public-legibility as the community's identity mark (Joh 13:35).

### Groups 563-001 through 573-001 — remaining Greek groups

**Group 563-001 — G5379 filoneikia (love of dispute)**

**Luk 22:24** — 'A dispute also arose among them, as to which of them was to be regarded as the greatest.'

**OBS-103-131:** Love of dispute (filoneikia) surfaces at the Last Supper — at the moment of greatest solemnity, the disciples' inner orientation toward rivalry and status asserts itself. The timing is analytically significant: love-of-dispute is most dangerous when it operates within the love-community (at the table of the Lord). *Check 4:* love-of-primacy and community-love in structural opposition — inner rivalry undermines the community's love-structure from within.

**Group 564-001 — G5365 filarguria (love of money)**

**1Ti 6:10** — 'For the love of money is a root of all kinds of evils. It is through this craving that some have wandered away from the faith and pierced themselves with many pangs.'

**OBS-103-132:** Love of money (filarguria) is the root (rhiza — structural origin) of all kinds of evils. The inner mechanism: love misdirected → produces the craving (orexis — reaching/appetite) → wandering from faith → self-inflicted suffering. The causal chain is explicitly traced. *Check 3:* Causal — filarguria → craving → departure from faith → anguish. *Check 1:* faith (R059), anguish (R005), appetite (R008). *Check 4:* love-of-money and faith in structurally opposed directions — one causes the other's departure.

---

**Group 565-001 — G4375 prosfilēs (lovely)**

**Phili 4:8** — 'Finally, brothers, whatever is true, whatever is honorable, whatever is just, whatever is pure, whatever is lovely (prosfilēs), whatever is commendable, if there is any excellence, if there is anything worthy of praise, think about these things.'

**OBS-103-133:** The lovely (prosfilēs) is one of the qualities the mind (R112) is directed to think about. Love's aesthetic dimension becomes the object of cognitive direction: the mind is commanded to attend to what is lovely. *Check 4:* love's aesthetic (loveliness) and cognitive orientation of the mind in structural connection. *Check 1:* mind (R112), thought (R160).

---

**Group 566-001 — G5358 filagathos (lover of good)**

**Tit 1:8** — 'but hospitable, a lover of good (filagathos), self-controlled, upright, holy, and disciplined.'

**OBS-103-134:** The lover-of-good (filagathos) is named alongside self-control, uprightness, holiness, and discipline as a character requirement for community leaders. Love of good is a stable character disposition (inner orientation toward what is good) — not a feeling but a character quality. *Check 4:* love-of-good and self-control/holiness in structural co-listing as character virtues.

---

**Group 567-001 — G5361 filadelfos (loving the brothers)**

**1Pe 3:8** — 'Finally, all of you, have unity of mind, sympathy, brotherly love (filadelfoi), a tender heart, and a humble mind.'

**OBS-103-135:** The virtue list for community: unity of mind + sympathy + brotherly love + tender heart + humble mind. Love is embedded in a cluster of cognitive (unity of mind), affective (sympathy, tender heart), and relational (brotherly love) virtues. The heart (kardia) appears as 'tender' (eusplagchnoi — good-bowels/compassionate) — same somatic root as me'eka/splanchna. *Check 5:* Somatic — tender-hearted/good-bowels as a virtue of the love-community. *Check 4:* love, sympathy, compassion, and humility in structural co-presence as community virtues.

---

**Group 568-001 — G5366 filarguros (money-loving)**

**Luk 16:14** — 'The Pharisees, who were lovers of money, heard all these things, and they ridiculed him.'

**OBS-103-136:** The Pharisees' love of money (philarguros) produces ridicule of Jesus' teaching on wealth. Inner love-of-money → external scoffing at the counter-teaching. The inner disorder expresses itself as intellectual rejection of the correcting voice. *Check 4:* love-of-money and rejection of truth in structural relationship.

**2Ti 3:2** — 'For people will be lovers of self (filautoi), lovers of money (filarguros), proud, arrogant, abusive...'

**OBS-103-137:** The last-days catalogue opens with two love-disorders: love of self (philautos — R_unknown) and love of money. These head the catalogue, suggesting they are structurally foundational to all the subsequent failures listed. Love misdirected toward self and toward wealth is the origin-point of the last-days inner collapse. *Check 4:* love-of-self and all subsequent inner-being failures in generative relationship.

SP raised: love-of-self as the first item in the 2Ti 3 catalogue.

**SP-103-038** — raised in Unit 7, 2026-04-30, MEDIUM, Session D
- Target: R103 (love) / self-love (R_unknown — filautos)
- Connecting term: G5367 filautos (selfish/self-loving — XREF in this registry)
- Question: 2Ti 3:2 places love-of-self (philautos) first in the last-days inner-collapse catalogue. Does the programme have a registry for self-love? If not, should one be created — or is self-love treated as the misdirection of the love mechanism toward the self as object? Joh 12:25 (love/hate of one's own life) already engages self-love from a different angle (SD-004). Is there a coherent programme account of self-love as: (a) the normal self-regard that enables 'love your neighbor as yourself' (Lev 19:18), and (b) the disordered self-love that heads the catalogue of inner failures (2Ti 3:2)? Cross-registry: love (103), self (R_unknown).

**Group 569-001 — G0866 afilarguros (free from love of money)**

**1Ti 3:3** — 'not a drunkard, not violent but gentle, not quarrelsome, not a lover of money (afilarguros).'

**Heb 13:5** — 'Keep your life free from love of money, and be content with what you have, for he has said, "I will never leave you nor forsake you."'

**OBS-103-138:** Heb 13:5 grounds freedom from love-of-money in a love-promise: 'I will never leave you nor forsake you.' The inner correction for love-of-money is not merely discipline but the reception of a greater love — God's permanent presence. Love-of-money is replaced not by indifference but by love-toward-God that renders material attachment unnecessary. *Check 4:* love-of-money and divine permanence/faithful-love in structural opposition — the greater love displaces the lesser.

### Groups 571-001 through 571-005 — G0025 agapaō (five groups)

**Group 571-001 — agapaō: love of God/Christ**

**Mat 22:37** — 'You shall love the Lord your God with all your heart and with all your soul and with all your mind.'

**OBS-103-139:** The great commandment is total — heart (lev), soul (nephesh), and mind (dianoia — or strength in Mk 12:30). Love of God is commanded across the entire inner-being: no faculty is exempt. *Check 4:* love and heart, soul, and mind in structural totality — love requires the mobilisation of all inner-being faculties.

**Joh 14:15** — 'If you love me, you will keep my commandments.'

**OBS-103-140:** Love of Christ produces keeping of commandments — the inner orientation produces the outer pattern of life. This is love as the motivational ground of obedience: not fear of punishment but love of the person. *Check 3:* Conditional causal — love → commandment-keeping. *Check 4:* love and obedience in generative relationship.

**Group 571-002 — agapaō: divine love toward person**

**Joh 3:16** — 'For God so loved (ēgapēsen) the world, that he gave his only Son, that whoever believes in him should not perish but have eternal life.'

**OBS-103-141:** The most cited verse in the programme: God's love for the world is the ground of the Son's giving. The structural sequence: God loved → gave Son → believing → not perishing → eternal life. Love as the originating inner disposition produces the gift (the Son) that opens the path to life. *Check 3:* Causal — love → giving → life. *Check 4:* love and giving and life in structural sequence — love is the causal origin of redemption.

**Gal 2:20** — 'I have been crucified with Christ. It is no longer I who live, but Christ who lives in me. And the life I now live in the flesh I live by faith in the Son of God, who loved me and gave himself for me.'

**OBS-103-142:** The sequence here is personal: Christ loved me (individual) → gave himself for me. The crucifixion is an act of love directed specifically at the individual. The self-giving (heauton paredōken — gave himself) is love's costliest act. Faith in the Son-of-God-who-loved-me is the inner-being response. *Check 4:* love and self-giving and faith in structural sequence — love gives itself, faith receives the gift.

**Group 571-003 — agapaō: love of neighbour and enemy**

**Mat 5:44** — 'But I say to you, Love your enemies and pray for those who persecute you.'

**OBS-103-143:** Enemy-love is agapaō — the strongest love term — directed to the most difficult object. This is love operating against the inner grain of natural affection, requiring the will's active engagement. SD-003 and SD-013 already raised. *Check 4:* love and will and prayer in structural integration — enemy-love requires volitional and prayerful engagement.

**Luk 6:35** — 'But love your enemies, and do good, and lend, expecting nothing in return, and your reward will be great, and you will be sons of the Most High, for he is kind to the ungrateful and the evil.'

**OBS-103-144:** Enemy-love includes concrete acts (do good, lend) and a motivational re-grounding ('expecting nothing in return'). The identity outcome: 'sons of the Most High' — the same pattern as the peacemaker beatitude. Love of enemy constitutes identity as God's children. *Check 4:* enemy-love and divine identity in structural relationship — love of enemies is the mark of divine sonship.

**Group 571-004 — agapaō: mutual love among believers and in marriage**

**Joh 13:34** — 'A new commandment I give to you, that you love one another: just as I have loved you, you also are to love one another.'

**OBS-103-145:** The newness of the commandment: the standard changes. Previously 'love your neighbor as yourself' (Lev 19:18 — self as standard); now 'as I have loved you' — Christ's love as the new standard. The inner shift: the measure of love is no longer the natural self-care but the divine self-giving. *Check 4:* the old love-standard (self) replaced by the new love-standard (Christ's love) — love's measure escalated.

**1Jo 4:19** — 'We love because he first loved us.'

**OBS-103-146:** The origin statement: human love is a response to prior divine love. Love's flow is unidirectional at origin: God → human → other humans. No human love is self-originating. *Check 3:* Causal — divine love first → human love responsive. *Check 4:* divine priority and human love in generative relationship — love cannot be self-generated; it is always received before given.

**Group 571-005 — agapaō: disordered love**

**Joh 3:19** — 'And this is the judgment: the light has come into the world, and people loved the darkness rather than the light because their works were evil.'

**OBS-103-147:** Love of darkness (ēgapēsan to skotos) is the inner orientation away from revelation. The word is agapaō — the strongest love term — applied to the love of darkness. This is analytically significant: the fallen person's inner orientation toward evil is as strong and total as the righteous person's love of God. Evil is loved, not merely preferred. *Check 4:* love of darkness and love of light in structural opposition — same inner mechanism, opposed objects, both described with the same strong love-term.

**2Ti 4:10** — 'For Demas, in love with this present world (agapēsas ton nun aiōna), has deserted me.'

**OBS-103-148:** Demas' departure is attributed to love of the present age (agapaō + ton nun aiōna). The word is agapaō — not mere preference but full love-commitment to the world. Love's desertion-power: love of the world causes the desertion of Paul (abandonment of the love-relationship). *Check 4:* world-love and community-love in structural opposition — love of one requires abandonment of the other.

Groups 571-001 through 571-005 COMPLETE: Key observation: agapaō groups span the full architecture of love — from the total mobilisation of the inner person (Mat 22:37) through the divine origin of all love (1Jo 4:19) to the full application of the love-mechanism to darkness and the world by the disordered person (Joh 3:19). The vocabulary makes no distinction of intensity between righteous and disordered love — agapaō is used for both.

---

### Groups 572-001, 572-002, 572-003 — G5368 fileō (natural affection)

**Group 572-001 — fileō: natural affection/friendship**

**Joh 11:36** — 'So the Jews said, "See how he loved (efilei) him!"'

**OBS-103-149:** Jesus' grief at Lazarus' tomb is read as evidence of love (fileō). The onlookers' observation: the depth of grief reveals the depth of the prior love. This is the inverse of SD-017 (David's lament for Jonathan): in both cases grief is love's evidence. *Check 4:* love and grief in evidence-relationship — grief makes visible what love already was.

**Joh 15:19** — 'If you were of the world, the world would love you as its own (efilei); but because you are not of the world... therefore the world hates you.'

**OBS-103-150:** The world's fileō is exclusive to its own — it loves (fileō) only those who belong to it. This is love as tribal attachment: natural affection within the in-group. The contrast: the disciples have been chosen out of the world, so the world's love is replaced by the world's hatred. *Check 4:* love (group-internal) and hatred (group-external) in structural opposition — love and hatred are relational positions, not just feelings.

**Group 572-002 — fileō: ranking of inner loves**

**Mat 10:37** — 'Whoever loves (filōn) father or mother more than me is not worthy of me, and whoever loves (filōn) son or daughter more than me is not worthy of me.'

**OBS-103-151:** Love admits of ranking — fileō applied to parents/children, but these loves must not exceed love for Christ. The inner person holds multiple loves simultaneously; the question is their hierarchy. Love of Christ must be first. *Check 4:* love and hierarchy of love-objects in structural relationship — love's moral quality depends on its ranking among competing loves.

**Joh 12:25** — 'Whoever loves (filōn) his life loses it, and whoever hates his life in this world will keep it for eternal life.'

**OBS-103-152:** Self-love (fileō of psuchē/life) paradoxically destroys its object; self-hate preserves the object. SD-004 already raised. The inner paradox: the love-mechanism turned toward the self produces loss; the hate-mechanism toward the self produces life. This is one of the programme's most analytically significant inner-being paradoxes. *Check 4:* love and hate of self in structural paradox — the mechanism reversed in its direction reverses its outcome.

**Group 572-003 — fileō: Peter's natural love**

**Joh 21:17** — 'He said to him the third time, "Simon, son of John, do you love me?" Peter was grieved because he said to him the third time, "Do you love me?" and he said to him, "Lord, you know everything; you know that I love (filō) you." Jesus said to him, "Feed my sheep."'

**OBS-103-153:** Peter uses fileō where Jesus uses agapaō (in the first two exchanges — though some readings see both terms used). Peter names the warmth he can affirm (natural affection, philia) rather than claiming the full covenantal-volitional love (agapē). Jesus accepts fileō and assigns the mission ('feed my sheep') on that basis. The inner-being significance: the available love is accepted; mission follows the love that is actually present, not an ideal love that isn't. *Check 4:* natural affection (fileō) and covenantal love (agapaō) in structural relationship — fileō is accepted as sufficient for mission assignment.

**1Cor 16:22** — 'If anyone has no love (filei) for the Lord, let him be accursed.'

**OBS-103-154:** Absence of even fileō (natural affection) for the Lord is anathema — the minimum threshold. *Check 4:* love and identity-in-community — lovelessness toward the Lord is the outer boundary of the community.

Groups 572-001 through 572-003 COMPLETE: Key observation: fileō groups reveal love's hierarchy (competing loves must be ranked), love's self-directed paradox (Joh 12:25), and love's acceptance in its available form (Peter's fileō accepted for mission). Grief is consistently love's visible evidence.

---

**Group 573-001 — G5383 filoprōteuō (love to be first)**

**3Jo 9** — 'I have written something to the church, but Diotrephes, who likes to put himself first, does not acknowledge our authority.'

**OBS-103-155:** Love-of-primacy (philoprōteuō) produces rejection of legitimate authority and community exclusion. The inner disposition of love-misdirected-toward-self-elevation undermines the love-community's order. *Check 4:* love-of-primacy and community authority in structural opposition.

Group 573-001 COMPLETE.

---

**H7468 reut groups** — small groups within rea family, already captured in OBS-103-028/073.

## Stage 2a — Unit 8: Thin-Evidence Phase2 Flags

**Data source:** §7 quality flags summary and §9 open flags in data package.

Quality flags on record:
- NO_WORD_ANALYSIS: 142
- VERSE_EVIDENCE_CONCENTRATED: 111
- PROSE_ONLY_MEANING: 107
- CONCRETE_PHYSICAL: 4
- VERSE_EVIDENCE_MINIMAL: 3
- VERSE_EVIDENCE_HIGH: 1

The data package does not list individual thin-evidence `PH2_THIN_EVIDENCE` flags for specific terms in a way that would require per-term review here. The PH2 flags in §9 are quality-control flags on specific terms/groups, not thin-evidence classification flags from Stage 1 Step 1.3a in the instruction's sense.

**OBS-103-156:** The NO_WORD_ANALYSIS flag (142 instances) is the dominant quality flag in R103. This flag indicates terms where the term's word-analysis data is absent — meaning the lexical parse (meaning, senses, root family) was not fully populated in the database for those terms. This is analytically significant: 142 of the registry's terms carry no word-analysis data, which means the Unit 3 lexical reading was limited to gloss and occurrence count for those terms. The gap was noted in Unit 3 and is confirmed here.

**OBS-103-157:** VERSE_EVIDENCE_CONCENTRATED (111) and PROSE_ONLY_MEANING (107) together suggest that a substantial portion of R103's evidence base is concentrated in a small number of verses per term, and that many terms' meanings are derived from prose analysis rather than verse classification. This is consistent with the programme's description of love as 'most theologically dense' — the evidence is analytically rich but not uniformly distributed across the corpus.

**OBS-103-158:** VERSE_EVIDENCE_MINIMAL (3) flags three terms with very limited verse evidence. These cannot carry significant analytical weight in Stage 2b answers. VERSE_EVIDENCE_HIGH (1) flags one term as having exceptional verse coverage — likely agapaō or chesed given their occurrence counts.

**PH2-103-002 (rachamim contamination)** and **PH2-103-005 (agapaō coverage breadth)** are the primary data quality items requiring tracking in Stage 2b. Both are already captured as SD pointers (SD-025 and the breadth note).

## Stage 2a — Unit 9: Existing Findings — Input Material Review

Two findings exist: DIM-103-001 and DIM-103-002 (both DIMENSION_REVIEW, status=pending, §N items).

**DIM-103-001 review** — 'map the full spectrum of love's inner-being architecture: what distinguishes the different forms, how they interrelate, coexistence of eros/philia/agapē.'

*After Units 1–8:* The finding's call is well-executed by the data itself. The four-cluster taxonomy in OBS-103-033 begins the architecture. The Unit 7 reading has deepened it substantially: agapē = willed covenantal self-giving; phileō = natural relational affection; chesed = faithful covenant-loyalty; racham = compassion-love responding to suffering; dod = passionate erotic love; ahavah = intense personal love including the erotic. The 'coexistence' question is answered: these are not competing forms of a single emotion but distinct modes of love's relational orientation. **Assessment: confirmed well-grounded; the Q&A tier will systematise what the anchor verse reading has demonstrated.**

**DIM-103-002 review** — 'does love vocabulary contain a sub-pattern attributing inner-being states to God with the same vocabulary used for human inner-being?'

*After Units 1–8:* The answer is emphatically yes. The evidence base is extensive: God's soul/nephesh has a beloved (Jer 12:7, group 535-001); God's inner organs/me'eka are moved (Jer 31:20, Isa 63:15, group 551-001); God's rachamim operate with womb-like movement; God rejoices (Zep 3:17), quiets in love (Zep 3:17), declares his beloved (Mat 3:17). The sub-pattern is not a minor strand but a major structural feature of the love vocabulary. **Assessment: confirmed, substantially deepened, high priority for Stage 2b T0 and T2.**
