## Stage 2b — Second-Tier Q&A Log

**Stage 2b commenced: 2026-04-30**
**Source material:** OBS-103-001 through OBS-103-158 (Stage 2a observations)
**Catalogue:** v2 — 189 prompts across T0–T7 + 14 Love Extensions
**Tier sequence:** T0 → T1 → T2 → T3 → T4 → T5 → T6 → T7 → Love Extensions

---

#### Tier 0 — Divine Image and Created Design — 12 prompts


**Q&A-001 | T0.1.1**
- Tier: T0 — Divine Image and Created Design
- Component: T0.1 — Divine Nature Reflected
- Prompt: 1 — What does the verse evidence reveal about the nature or character of God that this characteristic reflects or images?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: The verse evidence reveals that love is not merely an attribute God exercises but a characterisation of what God is. The divine self-declaration formula at Exo 34:6 (OBS-103-069) names rachum (compassionate) + chesed (steadfast love) as the first two inner attributes God proclaims of himself — love leads the divine self-portrait. Jer 31:3 names God's love as 'everlasting' (ahavat olam) — a qualifier that exceeds any human love-form (OBS-103-093). Song 8:6 names love's flame as 'the very flame of the Lord' (shalhevetyah) — grounding love's intensity in the divine nature itself (OBS-103-096). The data culminates in the NT claim (1Jo 4:8 — God is love), carried in the registry as PH2-103-004 and evidenced structurally by the entire divine love vocabulary across the data. The characteristic being imaged in the human person is therefore not a quality God has alongside others but God's own constitutive being-as-love.
- Anchor verses: Exo 34:6, Jer 31:3, Song 8:6, 1Jo 4:8 (via flag), Mat 3:17
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-002 | T0.1.2**
- Tier: T0 — Divine Image and Created Design
- Component: T0.1 — Divine Nature Reflected
- Prompt: 2 — Does Scripture explicitly attribute this characteristic to God — and if so, what does that attribution reveal about its significance in the human person?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Scripture attributes love to God across both testaments and with unprecedented density in R103 — 14+ GOD-dominant groups (OBS-103-034). The attribution operates at three levels: (a) love as God's relational disposition toward persons (chesed-GOD group 536-001; agapaō-GOD group 571-002; rachamim-GOD group 544-001); (b) love as God's inner-being experience — God's soul has a beloved (Jer 12:7, OBS-103-086), God's inner organs move with compassion (Jer 31:20, Isa 63:15, OBS-103-106, OBS-103-117), God grieves the withdrawal of his love; (c) love as what God is ontologically (1Jo 4:8 — held via PH2-103-004). The significance for the human person: because love is constitutive of God's being, it is the primary characteristic through which the human person bears the divine image. A human person who loves is not merely imitating a divine behaviour but reflecting the divine nature. The love-capacity is the image-capacity.
- Anchor verses: Jer 12:7, Jer 31:20, Exo 34:6, Joh 3:16, 1Jo 4:19
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-003 | T0.1.3**
- Tier: T0 — Divine Image and Created Design
- Component: T0.1 — Divine Nature Reflected
- Prompt: 3 — Where Scripture is silent about God's possession of this characteristic, note this explicitly.
- Disposition: NOT APPLICABLE
- Status tag: N
- Rationale: Scripture is not silent — love is attributed to God with greater evidential density in R103 than any other characteristic in the programme. The closing condition of this prompt ('where Scripture is silent') does not apply here. The closing condition is relevant for characteristics the programme does not attribute to God; it does not apply to love.
- Anchor verses: N/A
- Finding type: N/A

**Q&A-004 | T0.2.1**
- Tier: T0 — Divine Image and Created Design
- Component: T0.2 — Created Purpose
- Prompt: 1 — What does the verse evidence suggest about the purpose this characteristic serves in the human person as created — what does it equip the person to be, do, or become?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: The verse evidence points to love as the characteristic that equips the human person to participate in the relational structure of divine life — to enter and sustain the three directional axes identified in OBS-103-035 (vertical-descending, vertical-ascending, horizontal). Love of God with all heart, soul, and mind (Mat 22:37, OBS-103-139) equips the person to respond to the divine love that constitutes them. Love of neighbour (Lev 19:18, OBS-103-071) equips the person to bear the image of God toward other persons. Love in community (Joh 13:34, OBS-103-145) equips the person to live within the relational structure that constitutes the community of God's people. Together: love equips the person to be the image-bearer — to reflect God's own love outward in every relational direction. The great commandment (love God, love neighbour) implies that love is the purpose-function of the human person as created: the person is made to love, and love is what the person most fundamentally is for.
- Anchor verses: Mat 22:37, Lev 19:18, Joh 13:34, 1Jo 4:19
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-005 | T0.2.2**
- Tier: T0 — Divine Image and Created Design
- Component: T0.2 — Created Purpose
- Prompt: 2 — Does the evidence indicate whether this characteristic is part of the original created design, a response to the fallen condition, or both?
- Disposition: PARTIALLY ANSWERED
- Status tag: P
- Notation: *Gap identified*
- Answer: The evidence strongly implies love is part of original created design — the great commandment assumes love as the constitutive purpose of the human person, not as a remedial response. Song of Songs presents love (ahavah, dod) in a creation-delight context without reference to sin or fall — erotic love as given, not remedial. The divine self-declaration (Exo 34:6) attributes love to God prior to and independent of the fall. However, the data also shows love operating distinctively in response to the fallen condition: agapē of enemies (Mat 5:44, OBS-103-143) presupposes enemies exist; racham/compassion (OBS-103-029) responds to suffering that is post-fall in character; forgiveness-love (Luk 7:47, OBS-103-020 via SD pointer) presupposes guilt. The data does not contain an explicit statement that love existed in creation before the fall — the gap in pre-fall love evidence is noted. Both dimensions appear present but the evidence is stronger for love as created design than as purely remedial response.
- Anchor verses: Song 2:16, Exo 34:6, Mat 5:44, Luk 7:47
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE
- Stage 2b note: Pre-fall love evidence is a genuine gap in the data package. Not directly addressable from verse evidence on hand.

**Q&A-006 | T0.2.3**
- Tier: T0 — Divine Image and Created Design
- Component: T0.2 — Created Purpose
- Prompt: 3 — Is there evidence that this characteristic is oriented toward a future fullness — something the person is moving toward, not only what they currently are?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Yes, and clearly. Jer 31:34 (OBS-103-072) presents the new covenant as the eschatological fulfilment of love's neighbour-mediated form — in the final state, neighbour-teaching of God-knowledge is superseded by direct divine knowledge. The new covenant is love's eschatological completion, not its abolition. Psa 27:13 (OBS-103-080) — 'I shall look upon the goodness of the Lord in the land of the living' — names future vision of God's love/goodness as the orientation of hope. 1Th 3:12 (OBS-103-130) — 'may the Lord make you increase and abound in love' — treats love as a growing reality, moving toward greater fullness. 1Jo 4:18 (via SP-103-029) implies that perfect love casts out fear — 'perfect love' is an eschatological state toward which current love moves. The trajectory is from love-as-now to love-as-perfected: love is eschatologically oriented.
- Anchor verses: Jer 31:34, Psa 27:13, 1Th 3:12, Song 8:6
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-007 | T0.3.1**
- Tier: T0 — Divine Image and Created Design
- Component: T0.3 — Image-Bearer Expression
- Prompt: 1 — In what way does this characteristic express the divine image in the human person — what aspect of being made in God's likeness does it instantiate?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Love expresses the divine image in the human person through structural mirroring: the same relational orientations attributed to God (love toward persons, compassion toward the suffering, faithful loyalty within bonds) are commanded of and available to the human person. The mirroring is not analogical but participatory in the data: 1Jo 4:19 ('we love because he first loved us') presents human love as flowing from and enabled by divine love — the same love, not merely an imitation. Rom 8:29 (OBS-103-076) — predestination to conformity with the image of the Son — makes love-conformity the goal of the divine image-restoration project. Joh 13:34 ('as I have loved you, so you must love one another') makes the divine love the model and measure of the human love that bears the image. The aspect of likeness instantiated: love as relational-orientation-toward-persons is the primary mode in which the human person resembles and participates in the divine being.
- Anchor verses: 1Jo 4:19, Joh 13:34, Rom 8:29, Gal 2:20
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-008 | T0.3.2**
- Tier: T0 — Divine Image and Created Design
- Component: T0.3 — Image-Bearer Expression
- Prompt: 2 — Does the evidence suggest that this characteristic is shared between God and the human person, or is it exclusively a creaturely analogue to something in God?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: The evidence strongly suggests love is shared, not merely analogical. The vocabulary is explicitly common: God's nephesh has a beloved using the same term as the human person's beloved (OBS-103-086); God's inner organs (me'eka) are moved using somatic vocabulary parallel to the human compassion-response (OBS-103-106, OBS-103-117); agapē is the term both for God's love toward persons and the commanded love of person toward God and others. The LXX use of agapē to translate chesed bridges the Testaments — the same vocabulary governs both divine and human love. DIM-103-002 (§N item) is precisely this question and is confirmed: the love vocabulary of R103 consistently attributes inner-being states to God with the same vocabulary used for human inner-being. This is not analogy but shared characteristic — love is the one characteristic in the programme where divine and human possession is most evidentially co-extensive.
- Anchor verses: Jer 12:7, Jer 31:20, 1Jo 4:19, Exo 34:6, Joh 13:34
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE
- Stage 2b note: This Q&A resolves DIM-103-002 (§N item). DIM-103-002 lifecycle: resolved_qa via Q&A-008.

**Q&A-009 | T0.3.3**
- Tier: T0 — Divine Image and Created Design
- Component: T0.3 — Image-Bearer Expression
- Prompt: 3 — What does the presence or absence of this characteristic in a person reveal about the condition of the divine image in that person?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: The data provides an unusually direct answer. Joh 13:35 (OBS-103-129) — 'by this all people will know that you are my disciples, if you have love for one another' — makes love the externally legible mark of the divine image in the community. 1Jo 4:8 (via flag) — 'whoever does not love does not know God, for God is love' — states that lovelessness constitutes non-knowledge of God. The absence of love is not merely a moral deficiency; it is an epistemic and ontological condition: the person who does not love does not know God and therefore does not bear the divine image in its proper operation. Conversely, the presence of love — particularly love of enemies (Mat 5:44-45, OBS-103-144) — constitutes identity as a son/daughter of God. Love is thus the diagnostic marker of the divine image's condition: present and active = image bearing; absent or disordered = image distorted.
- Anchor verses: Joh 13:35, Mat 5:44-45, 1Jo 4:8 (via flag)
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-010 | T0.4.1**
- Tier: T0 — Divine Image and Created Design
- Component: T0.4 — Typological Significance
- Prompt: 1 — Does Scripture use this characteristic typologically — deploying it to point toward or participate in a reality beyond the immediate?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Yes — extensively. The dod vocabulary of the Song is the most concentrated typological deployment: human eros/marital love functions as the vehicle for God's love for Israel (Isa 5:1 OBS-103-083; Eze 16:8 OBS-103-083b) and in the prophetic-allegorical tradition as the figure of divine-human covenantal love. God's love for Israel is called 'the time of love' (Eze 16:8) using marital vocabulary. The father-son love (Mat 3:17, OBS-103-120) functions typologically: the Father's love for the Son at baptism is simultaneously the origin-point from which all love flows (SD-016) and the pattern of divine-to-human love in redemption. The parable of the prodigal son (Luk 15:20, OBS-103-057) deploys parental love typologically — the father's running, embracing, and kissing figure God's reception of the returning sinner. Typological use runs in both directions (OT human love → divine love type; NT divine love → human love pattern).
- Anchor verses: Eze 16:8, Mat 3:17, Luk 15:20, Isa 5:1
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-011 | T0.4.2**
- Tier: T0 — Divine Image and Created Design
- Component: T0.4 — Typological Significance
- Prompt: 2 — If typological use is present, what is the direction of the typology?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: The evidence shows both directions operating but with a clear asymmetry. In the OT prophetic tradition: human marital/parental love → divine covenantal love (the human type points toward and is fulfilled in the divine). In the NT: divine love → human love (the divine instance establishes the pattern for the human: 'as I have loved you' — Joh 13:34; 'we love because he first loved us' — 1Jo 4:19). The asymmetry is that in the NT the direction inverts: the human type has served its purpose; the divine original now directly constitutes the human instance. The love-structure of the inner being therefore participates in a typological movement across the canon: created human love → figures divine love → divine love in Christ becomes the source and standard of human love in the new covenant.
- Anchor verses: Joh 13:34, 1Jo 4:19, Eze 16:8, Jer 31:3
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-012 | T0.4.3**
- Tier: T0 — Divine Image and Created Design
- Component: T0.4 — Typological Significance
- Prompt: 3 — If no typological use is evidenced, note this explicitly.
- Disposition: NOT APPLICABLE
- Status tag: N
- Rationale: Typological use is extensively evidenced (Q&A-010, Q&A-011). Closing condition does not apply.
- Anchor verses: N/A
- Finding type: N/A


#### Tier 1 — Definition — 24 prompts

**Q&A-013 | T1.1.1**
- Tier: T1 — Definition
- Component: T1.1 — Name and Naming
- Prompt: 1 — What is this characteristic called in the programme — and what does the name itself signal about its essential nature?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: The characteristic is called 'love' — a name that in English collapses a vocabulary of multiple Hebrew and Greek terms into a single referent. The name signals an orientation outward: love is always toward something or someone; it cannot be self-contained. Even the word's grammar in Scripture consistently requires a direct object (love of God, love of neighbour, love of enemy, love of money). The name also signals relational constitution: the one who loves is partly constituted by who and what they love. The programme's description note ('most foundational and most theologically dense word in the entire corpus,' OBS-103-004) signals that the name functions as an organising category for the entire inner-being vocabulary.
- Anchor verses: Mat 22:37, Lev 19:18
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-014 | T1.1.2**
- Tier: T1 — Definition
- Component: T1.1 — Name and Naming
- Prompt: 2 — What do the primary Hebrew and Greek terms reveal at the definitional level — before deeper lexical analysis begins?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: At the definitional level, the primary terms reveal a structured vocabulary rather than a single concept. Hebrew: chesed (covenant-faithfulness, binding loyalty), ahavah (intense personal love including eros), racham/rachamim (compassion — love responding to suffering), dod (beloved, erotic love of the Song). Greek: agapē (willed self-giving love, LXX/NT coinage), phileō (natural affection), philia compounds (love directed toward a specified object). The terms do not all name the same inner state at different intensities — they name structurally distinct modes of love's operation. Chesed is obligatory-covenantal; agapē is volitional-unconditional; phileō is naturally affective; racham is compassion-responsive. At the definitional level, 'love' in this registry is not one thing but a family of related inner orientations sharing the common structure of directed-attachment-to-an-other (OBS-103-033).
- Anchor verses: Psa 63:3, Joh 13:34, Isa 49:15
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-015 | T1.1.3**
- Tier: T1 — Definition
- Component: T1.1 — Name and Naming
- Prompt: 3 — Does the name carry directional, relational, or constitutional implications that orient the enquiry from the outset?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: All three. Directional: love always has a direction — toward God, toward neighbour, toward the beloved, or toward disordered objects (money, pleasure, world). The moral question of love is always the question of its direction (OBS-103-017). Relational: love cannot exist in isolation — it is constitutively relational, requiring at minimum a lover and a beloved. The relational structure is not incidental but essential (OBS-103-035). Constitutional: love operates at the deepest level of the inner person — the great commandment (Mat 22:37) requires 'all your heart and soul and mind,' indicating that love engages the entire constitutional depth of the inner being (OBS-103-139). The enquiry is oriented from the outset toward a characteristic that is simultaneously moral (choice of direction), relational (requires another), and constitutional (engages the whole person).
- Anchor verses: Mat 22:37, Jam 4:4, 1Jo 4:19
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-016 | T1.2.1**
- Tier: T1 — Definition
- Component: T1.2 — Kind
- Prompt: 1 — What kind of inner-being phenomenon does this characteristic appear to be — an act, a disposition, a condition, a quality, or something else?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Love in the data is simultaneously a disposition (stable inner orientation toward), an act (commanded, exercised, expressed — agapaō is consistently verbal), and a condition (one who is loved — agapētos — is in a constitutive relational state). It is not primarily an emotion, though it produces emotional states (joy, grief, rest). The commanded form (Mat 22:37 — 'you shall love') establishes love as an act of the will, not purely a felt state. The dispositional form (chesed as God's defining attribute, OBS-103-025) establishes love as a stable character quality. The received form (agapētos as identity, OBS-103-040) establishes love as a constitutive condition the person exists within. Love is therefore tripartite: disposition + act + condition — inner orientation that produces acts and exists within a condition of being-loved. This is the most structurally complex inner-being phenomenon in the programme.
- Anchor verses: Mat 22:37, Psa 63:3, Rom 1:7, 1Jo 4:19
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-017 | T1.2.2**
- Tier: T1 — Definition
- Component: T1.2 — Kind
- Prompt: 2 — Is this characteristic simple in structure or does it have constituent elements at first encounter?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: Structurally complex from the first encounter. The four-mode taxonomy (OBS-103-033) — willed covenantal, compassionate responsive, relational-social, intense erotic — is the first-level complexity. Beneath that, the common structure: directed attachment toward an object, whose moral quality is entirely determined by the object (OBS-103-009, OBS-103-017). The disordered forms (OBS-103-036) share the same structure as the righteous forms. The three-axis directional structure (OBS-103-035) adds spatial complexity: love operates in three directions simultaneously. The tripartite kind (Q&A-016) adds ontological complexity: disposition, act, and condition. Love appears to be the programme's most structurally composite inner-being characteristic — not simple but architecturally layered.
- Anchor verses: Mat 22:37, 1Cor 13:4, Gal 5:22
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-018 | T1.2.3**
- Tier: T1 — Definition
- Component: T1.2 — Kind
- Prompt: 3 — What is the current best working description of this characteristic — encapsulating its constitutional location, the faculties it primarily engages, and its impact on the person?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Working description: Love is the primary inner-being orientation of the human person — the directed attachment of the whole inner self toward God, persons, and the good, operating as both the deepest constitutional disposition and the foundational act of the will, producing and sustaining all relational bonds. It locates principally at the heart-soul interface (Spirit-Soul classification confirmed). It engages the will (commanded), the cognition (requires knowledge of the beloved), the emotion (produces joy, grief, rest depending on the beloved's presence/absence), and the body (expressed somatically in kiss, embrace, tears). Its impact: it constitutes the person's relational identity (who you love defines who you are), organises all other inner-being characteristics (love of God requires hatred of evil; love of God produces fruit), and is the externally legible mark of the community's identity (Joh 13:35). Its absence is the diagnostic indicator of the divine image's distortion (1Jo 4:8).
- Anchor verses: Mat 22:37, 1Jo 4:19, Joh 13:35, Gal 5:22
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-019 | T1.3.1**
- Tier: T1 — Definition
- Component: T1.3 — Boundary
- Prompt: 1 — What is the structural opposite of this characteristic — the inner-being reality that stands against or excludes it?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: The structural opposite is hatred (sane — H8130, 139 active verses, OWNER term, OBS-103-030). Sane is embedded in R103 as an OWNER term — the programme treats hate as constitutive of the love vocabulary's boundary, not external to it. Lev 19:17 ('you shall not hate your brother in your heart') places hate as the inner alternative to love of neighbour (OBS-103-114). Pro 10:12 ('hatred stirs up strife, love covers all offences,' OBS-103-097) places them as causal-opposite forces with opposed social effects. The secondary structural opposite at the ultimate level is enmity with God: friendship with the world is enmity (echthra) with God (Jam 4:4, OBS-103-058). But hatred is the primary inner-being opposite — it is the same inner mechanism as love (directed orientation) running in the opposed direction.
- Anchor verses: Lev 19:17, Pro 10:12, Jam 4:4
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-020 | T1.3.2**
- Tier: T1 — Definition
- Component: T1.3 — Boundary
- Prompt: 2 — What does this characteristic explicitly exclude or resist?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: 1Cor 13:4-7 provides the programme's most explicit catalogue of what love excludes: envy, boasting, arrogance, rudeness, self-seeking, irritability, resentfulness, rejoicing in wrongdoing (OBS-103-127). The list names love's resistances across moral, relational, and emotional registers. At the structural level, love resists division of ultimate allegiance (Jam 4:4 — cannot love God and world simultaneously, OBS-103-058), resists self-assertion as the primary orientation (love-of-self as the first item in the last-days catalogue, OBS-103-137), and resists the withholding of self (Joh 15:13 — love's maximum is the giving of the soul/life, OBS-103-125). Love also explicitly resists concealment of inner truth from the beloved: Lev 19:17 contrasts hate-as-silence with love-as-frank-correction (OBS-103-114).
- Anchor verses: 1Cor 13:4-7, Jam 4:4, Lev 19:17, Joh 15:13
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-021 | T1.3.3**
- Tier: T1 — Definition
- Component: T1.3 — Boundary
- Prompt: 3 — What is this characteristic not — where does it end and something else begin?
- Disposition: PARTIALLY ANSWERED
- Status tag: P
- Notation: *Gap identified*
- Answer: What love is not, from the data: love is not sentiment — it is commanded (Mat 22:37) and exercised irrespective of feeling (enemy-love, Mat 5:44). Love is not mere natural affection — phileō is insufficient as the full standard; agapē and chesed exceed phileō in obligatory reach. Love is not the same as desire (R043) — the desire registry owns the primary ahav verbal form (H0157G); desire and love share a mechanism but the programme treats them as distinct (OBS-103-010, OBS-103-022). Love is not the same as goodness (R067) — the tov family is XREF; love produces goodness but is not identical with it (OBS-103-014). The precise boundary between love and compassion (R023), kindness (R099), and mercy (R111) cannot be fully drawn from Stage 2a evidence alone — these are the programme's adjacent characteristics whose distinctions require dedicated treatment in Session D. Partial: the internal boundary is evidenced; the inter-registry distinctions are named as gaps deferred to Session D.
- Anchor verses: Mat 5:44, Lev 19:18, Hos 6:6
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE
- Stage 2b note: Boundary with compassion, kindness, mercy — named as gap; Session D treatment required.

**Q&A-022 | T1.4.1**
- Tier: T1 — Definition
- Component: T1.4 — Modes of Operation
- Prompt: 1 — In what distinct ways does this characteristic operate within the inner person?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Four primary modes of operation, each evidenced across the anchor verse corpus:
(1) **Covenantal-dispositional mode** (chesed, agapē): Love as stable inner orientation of faithful loyalty — not feeling-contingent, not revocable by the beloved's failure. God's chesed 'never ceases' (Lam 3:22, OBS-103-088); human chesed is written on the heart as character (Pro 3:3, OBS-103-090). This mode operates at the level of character — the deep stable orientation.
(2) **Compassionate-responsive mode** (racham, splanchnizō): Love that is activated by the beloved's suffering — the inner-organ movement (OBS-103-105, OBS-103-116). This mode responds to need; it is not passive but activated.
(3) **Volitional-costly mode** (agapē — enemy-love, self-giving): Love that operates against the inner grain of natural preference. Mat 5:44 (OBS-103-143), Joh 15:13 (OBS-103-125). This mode requires the will's deliberate engagement to exceed what natural affection would produce.
(4) **Affective-relational mode** (phileō, ahavah-intense, dod): Love as naturally felt warm attachment — the affection for friends, the longing for the beloved. This mode is experienced; it is love in its felt dimension.
The four modes are not always distinguishable in a single verse but are analytically distinct operations of the same inner orientation.
- Anchor verses: Lam 3:22, Isa 49:15, Mat 5:44, Joh 11:36
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-023 | T1.4.2**
- Tier: T1 — Definition
- Component: T1.4 — Modes of Operation
- Prompt: 2 — Does this characteristic operate differently depending on context, direction, or constitutional level?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: Yes — context and direction both shape the mode. Direction: love toward God operates in the volitional-dispositional mode most prominently (commanded; requires the whole person — Mat 22:37, OBS-103-139); love toward the neighbour operates in both the dispositional and the costly-volitional modes; love toward the beloved (marital/erotic) operates in the affective-intense mode (dod, ahavah — Song vocabulary, OBS-103-041); love toward the enemy operates exclusively in the costly-volitional mode (OBS-103-143). Constitutional level: at the spirit/soul boundary (sb_classification confirmed), love appears to have its deepest location at the spirit level (the willed, faithful chesed) and its experiential expression at the soul level (the felt ahavah/phileō). At the heart level (OBS-103-126) love is infused by the Spirit and inscribed as character. The constitutional level shapes how love presents: deep-spirit love is more chesed-like; soul-surface love is more phileō-like.
- Anchor verses: Mat 22:37, Mat 5:44, Song 2:16, Pro 3:3
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-024 | T1.4.3**
- Tier: T1 — Definition
- Component: T1.4 — Modes of Operation
- Prompt: 3 — Does this characteristic have a communicative or speech-based mode of operation — and if so, how does it function?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Yes — evidenced across several groups. Joh 15:15 (OBS-103-052): love's communicative mode is knowledge-disclosure — Jesus names the content of his friendship with the disciples as 'all that I have heard from my Father I have made known to you.' Love shares the inner world of the lover with the beloved. Lev 19:17 (OBS-103-114): frank correction (hocheach tochi'ach — honest rebuke) is love's communicative act, in contrast to hate's silence. The kiss (filēma, katafileō — OBS-103-054, OBS-103-056) is love's somatic-communicative mode — the body's expression of the inner word. The divine declaration ('this is my beloved Son' — Mat 3:17, OBS-103-120) is love's constitutive speech act: the naming of belovedness is itself the conferral of identity. Love therefore has a speech-mode that functions as: disclosure (sharing the inner world), correction (honest engagement), and declaration (constitutive naming).
- Anchor verses: Joh 15:15, Lev 19:17, Mat 3:17, 1Pe 5:14
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-025 | T1.5.1**
- Tier: T1 — Definition
- Component: T1.5 — Immediate Response
- Prompt: 1 — What is the first or most immediate inner-being response to receiving or encountering this characteristic?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: The data evidences three immediate response patterns, each associated with a primary love-encounter type:
(1) **Responsive love** — 1Jo 4:19: the immediate response to receiving divine love is love in return. Love received generates love given — the response is the same characteristic activated in the receiver.
(2) **Rest/stillness** — Zep 3:17 (OBS-103-094): God's love toward Israel produces quieting — the immediate inner response to the experience of being loved is rest, not striving. Psa 127:2 (OBS-103-084): being-beloved produces effortless sleep (rest as divine love-gift).
(3) **Grief as love-evidence** — Joh 11:36 (OBS-103-149), 2Sa 1:26 (OBS-103-095), Joh 21:17 (OBS-103-153): the immediate response to love's loss or to love's cost is grief — the inner collapse or distress that reveals the depth of the prior love. This is not a response to love per se but to love's absence or cost, and it is consistently love's most visible immediate evidence.
- Anchor verses: 1Jo 4:19, Zep 3:17, Psa 127:2, Joh 11:36
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-026 | T1.5.2**
- Tier: T1 — Definition
- Component: T1.5 — Immediate Response
- Prompt: 2 — Is the immediate response consistent across the verse evidence, or does it vary?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: The response varies by the type of love-encounter. When divine love is received: the immediate response is love-in-return (1Jo 4:19) or rest (Zep 3:17, Psa 127:2). When love is expressed at cost (forgiveness-love, enemy-love): the immediate response in the giver is not named directly. When love is lost: the immediate response is grief (Song 5:6, OBS-103-062; 2Sa 1:26, OBS-103-095). When the beloved is encountered: the immediate response is delight and longing (Song 2:16, OBS-103-061; Luk 15:20 — the father's compassion-movement at sight of the returning son, OBS-103-057). The variation is systematic, not random: the type of encounter determines the response type. There is no single invariant immediate response to love — the response depends on the direction of the encounter (giving vs receiving vs losing vs encountering).
- Anchor verses: 1Jo 4:19, Zep 3:17, Song 5:6, Luk 15:20
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-027 | T1.5.3**
- Tier: T1 — Definition
- Component: T1.5 — Immediate Response
- Prompt: 3 — Where the verse evidence is silent on immediate response, note this explicitly.
- Disposition: NOT APPLICABLE
- Status tag: N
- Rationale: The verse evidence is not silent on immediate response — Q&A-025 and Q&A-026 document three evidenced response patterns. Closing condition does not apply.
- Finding type: N/A

**Q&A-028 | T1.6.1**
- Tier: T1 — Definition
- Component: T1.6 — Sustained Effect
- Prompt: 1 — What does this characteristic produce in the inner being over time?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: The verse evidence identifies several sustained effects of love in the inner being:
(1) **Character formation** — Pro 3:3 (OBS-103-090): chesed written on the heart over time becomes character. 1Pe 1:22 (OBS-103-124): purified souls move toward sincere brotherly love — love as the goal of sustained inner formation.
(2) **Joy and fullness** — Psa 16:11 (OBS-103-112): in God's presence (sustained love-relationship) there is fullness of joy and pleasures forevermore. The sustained love-relationship with God produces an abiding experiential fullness.
(3) **Growth** — 1Th 3:12 (OBS-103-130): love can increase and abound over time. Love is not static but grows under the Lord's enabling.
(4) **Community cohesion** — Joh 13:35 (OBS-103-129): sustained mutual love becomes the externally legible identity of the community — a sustained social effect rather than a momentary one.
(5) **Obedience pattern** — Joh 14:15 (OBS-103-140): sustained love of Christ produces a sustained pattern of commandment-keeping. The inner orientation produces an enduring behavioural pattern.
- Anchor verses: Pro 3:3, 1Pe 1:22, Psa 16:11, 1Th 3:12, Joh 14:15
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-029 | T1.6.2**
- Tier: T1 — Definition
- Component: T1.6 — Sustained Effect
- Prompt: 2 — What states, qualities, capacities, or orientations does sustained exposure to or possession of this characteristic establish?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: From the data: sustained possession of love establishes — (a) **identity as beloved** (agapētos — the one constituted by divine love, OBS-103-040, OBS-103-122): sustained divine love toward the person establishes the identity of being-loved; (b) **relational capacity** — sustained love of neighbour establishes the inner orientation of fairness, care, and honesty that Lev 19 describes (OBS-103-071); (c) **community legibility** — the community constituted by mutual love becomes publicly readable (Joh 13:35, OBS-103-129); (d) **faith-pattern** — sustained love of God produces sustained commandment-keeping (Joh 14:15, OBS-103-140); (e) **soul-satisfaction** — sustained experience of God's goodness/love satisfies the soul's deepest hunger (Jer 31:14, OBS-103-081). The overarching capacity established: the person becomes capable of giving what they have received — sustained reception of divine love equips the person to love others.
- Anchor verses: Joh 13:35, Rom 1:7, Joh 14:15, Jer 31:14
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-030 | T1.6.3**
- Tier: T1 — Definition
- Component: T1.6 — Sustained Effect
- Prompt: 3 — Does the sustained effect differ from the immediate response — and if so, how?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: Yes — the distinction is clear. The immediate response to love is primarily experiential: rest/stillness (Zep 3:17), responsive love (1Jo 4:19), or grief (Song 5:6). The sustained effect is primarily constitutional and communal: character formation (Pro 3:3), identity-establishment (agapētos), community legibility (Joh 13:35), and soul-satisfaction (Jer 31:14). The immediate response is felt; the sustained effect is what the person becomes and what the community is constituted as. This distinction maps onto the programme's spirit-soul boundary: the immediate response operates at the soul-affective level; the sustained effect operates at the spirit-character level and the relational-community level.
- Anchor verses: Zep 3:17, Pro 3:3, Joh 13:35, Jer 31:14
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-031 | T1.7.1**
- Tier: T1 — Definition
- Component: T1.7 — Conditions of Reception
- Prompt: 1 — What inner conditions or orientations enable genuine reception of this characteristic?
- Disposition: PARTIALLY ANSWERED
- Status tag: P
- Notation: *Gap identified*
- Answer: From the data: (a) **obedience** — 1Pe 1:22 (OBS-103-124): soul-purification through obedience enables sincere love. The purified soul is the condition for authentic love. (b) **faith** — Jam 2:23 (OBS-103-053): Abraham's faith is what constitutes him as 'friend of God.' Faith as the inner condition through which love-relationship with God becomes possible. (c) **openness / not loving the darkness** — Joh 3:19 (OBS-103-147): those who love darkness cannot receive the light. The inner orientation away from evil is the negative condition for receiving love. (d) **being the returning prodigal** — Luk 15:20 (OBS-103-057): the son's return (movement toward the father) is the condition for the father's embrace. Some movement toward the source of love appears to be a condition for its reception. Gap: the data does not contain an explicit systematic account of reception-conditions. The conditions above are inferred from contexts where love is given and received. The gap is noted.
- Anchor verses: 1Pe 1:22, Jam 2:23, Joh 3:19, Luk 15:20
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-032 | T1.7.2**
- Tier: T1 — Definition
- Component: T1.7 — Conditions of Reception
- Prompt: 2 — What inner conditions block, distort, or prevent reception?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: The data names several inner blockers: (a) **love of darkness** — Joh 3:19 (OBS-103-147): the inner orientation toward darkness is the condition that prevents reception of love-as-light. The person who loves the darkness does not receive the light; the blocker is the prior love-commitment to a wrong object. (b) **love of money** — 1Ti 6:10 (OBS-103-132): love of money causes departure from faith — the love of a wrong object displaces the reception of divine love. (c) **pride/self-seeking** — 1Cor 13:4-7 (OBS-103-127): love of self expressed as arrogance and self-seeking is explicitly named as what love is not — the self-orientation blocks the other-orientation that genuine love requires. (d) **false-brotherhood orientation** — Gal 2:4 (OBS-103-068): the concealed inner agenda of the false brother prevents genuine love-reception within the community. The pattern: all inner blockers are disordered loves — prior commitments to wrong objects that displace the capacity for rightly directed love.
- Anchor verses: Joh 3:19, 1Ti 6:10, 1Cor 13:4-7, Gal 2:4
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-033 | T1.7.3**
- Tier: T1 — Definition
- Component: T1.7 — Conditions of Reception
- Prompt: 3 — What is the inner-being state of the person who encounters this characteristic but does not receive it?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: The data provides several instances: (a) Joh 3:19 (OBS-103-147) — the person who encounters light-as-love and does not receive it 'loved the darkness' — the inner state is commitment to the alternative; the non-reception is an inner-being act of love misdirected. (b) Luk 16:14 (OBS-103-136) — the Pharisees who were money-lovers ridiculed Jesus' teaching; their inner state is intellectual rejection grounded in love-of-money. (c) 2Ti 4:10 (OBS-103-148) — Demas, in love with the present world, deserts: the non-reception of love-community is an act of love toward the world instead. The pattern is consistent: the person who does not receive love is not loveless — they are loving the wrong thing. Lovelessness in the sense of having no love-capacity does not appear in the data; what appears is love misdirected.
- Anchor verses: Joh 3:19, Luk 16:14, 2Ti 4:10
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-034 | T1.8.1**
- Tier: T1 — Definition
- Component: T1.8 — Dimension Classification
- Prompt: 1 — What is the primary inner-being dimension of this characteristic from the programme's dimension vocabulary?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Consistent with prior analysis*
- Answer: Primary dimension: **Relational Disposition**. This is the confirmed Dimension Review result (v1.9, 2026-04-09) and is well-supported by the data. Love is fundamentally orientation-toward-another — the directed attachment of the inner person toward an object. The relational structure is constitutive, not incidental: love cannot exist without a direction and an object (OBS-103-015, OBS-103-035). The Dimension Review classification is confirmed as well-grounded by the full anchor verse reading in Stage 2a.
- Anchor verses: Mat 22:37, 1Jo 4:19, Joh 13:34
- Finding type: N/A

**Q&A-035 | T1.8.2**
- Tier: T1 — Definition
- Component: T1.8 — Dimension Classification
- Prompt: 2 — What evidence from the verse evidence supports this classification?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Consistent with prior analysis*
- Answer: The Relational Disposition classification is supported by: (a) the consistent directional structure of the vocabulary — love always has an object toward which it is oriented (OBS-103-017); (b) the three-axis relational architecture (GOD → HUMAN, HUMAN → GOD, HUMAN → HUMAN, OBS-103-035); (c) the 14+ GOD-dominant groups naming divine love as relational orientation (OBS-103-034); (d) the person-type terms (filos, chasid, agapētos) that name the relational identity constituted by love (OBS-103-018, OBS-103-026, OBS-103-040); (e) the group descriptions which consistently describe love as 'inner orientation toward' or 'relational disposition' in their language.
- Anchor verses: Mat 22:37, Lev 19:18, 1Jo 4:19, Joh 13:35
- Finding type: N/A

**Q&A-036 | T1.8.3**
- Tier: T1 — Definition
- Component: T1.8 — Dimension Classification
- Prompt: 3 — Does this characteristic carry secondary dimensions — and if so, what are they, and do they compete with the primary classification?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: Secondary dimensions evidenced: (a) **Moral Character** — chesed written on the heart (Pro 3:3, OBS-103-090), chasid as the person of covenant-character (OBS-103-026), love-of-good (filagathos) as a character disposition (OBS-103-134). Love as stable character (not just act) carries Moral Character alongside Relational Disposition. (b) **Emotion-Positive** — the affective-relational modes (phileō, ahavah-intense, dod) carry positive emotional content: delight, joy, longing (OBS-103-061, OBS-103-112). (c) **Volition** — enemy-love (Mat 5:44) and the ranking of loves (Mat 10:37) are explicitly volitional — choices against natural preference. These secondary dimensions do not compete with Relational Disposition; they describe the faculties through which love's relational orientation is expressed. The primary dimension correctly captures the constitutive structure; the secondary dimensions capture the modes.
- Anchor verses: Pro 3:3, Joh 11:36, Mat 5:44, Mat 10:37
- Finding type: N/A


#### Tier 2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries — 31 prompts

**Q&A-037 | T2.1.1**
- Tier: T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries
- Component: T2.1 — Spirit-Level Location
- Prompt: 1 — Is this characteristic explicitly located at the spirit level in the verse evidence?
- Disposition: PARTIALLY ANSWERED
- Status tag: P
- Notation: *Gap identified*
- Answer: Not explicitly by name in the verse evidence — the spirit vocabulary (ruach/pneuma) is not directly paired with love in the anchor verses in a way that names love as a spirit-level phenomenon. However, the sb_classification of 'Spirit-Soul Interface' (OBS-103-002) reflects a programme decision, not merely a verse label. The strongest spirit-adjacent evidence: Gal 5:22 names love as the fruit of the Spirit (pneuma) — the Spirit's fruit, not the human spirit directly, but love is produced by the Spirit's operation (OBS-103-128). Rom 5:5 names God's love as poured into hearts through the Holy Spirit (OBS-103-126) — the Spirit is the agent of love's infusion into the inner person. These are Spirit-sourced locations for love, though not explicit spirit-level location statements in the anatomical sense. Gap: no verse explicitly says 'love is in the spirit/ruach of the person.'
- Anchor verses: Gal 5:22, Rom 5:5
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-038 | T2.1.2**
- Tier: T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries
- Component: T2.1 — Spirit-Level Location
- Prompt: 2 — Does the evidence indicate that this characteristic originates in or is primarily a spirit-level phenomenon?
- Disposition: PARTIALLY ANSWERED
- Status tag: P
- Notation: *Gap identified*
- Answer: The Spirit-infusion evidence (Rom 5:5, OBS-103-126; Gal 5:22, OBS-103-128) points toward spirit-level origin in the sense of divine-Spirit origination — love's origin is the Holy Spirit's action, not the human spirit's generation. The commanded form ('you shall love' — Mat 22:37) places love at the will level, which in the programme's framework operates at or near the spirit boundary. Chesed as covenantal faithfulness — the mode that persists regardless of feeling — has a spirit-character quality: it operates at the deepest stable-disposition level rather than the feeling-fluctuating soul level. The sb_classification 'Spirit-Soul Interface' captures this: love has its deepest origin and most stable form at the spirit level but is also experienced at the soul level. The evidence implies spirit-level origin without explicitly naming it.
- Anchor verses: Rom 5:5, Gal 5:22, Mat 22:37
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-039 | T2.1.3**
- Tier: T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries
- Component: T2.1 — Spirit-Level Location
- Prompt: 3 — What does spirit-level location reveal about the nature and depth of this characteristic?
- Disposition: PARTIALLY ANSWERED
- Status tag: P
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: If spirit-level location is confirmed (the inference from Q&A-038, if not explicitly stated), it would reveal that: (a) love is the deepest possible inner-being orientation — not surface emotion but foundational directedness; (b) love cannot be fully explained by the soul's affective fluctuations — chesed persists through feeling-states (Lam 3:22, OBS-103-088); (c) love is constitutionally prior to the acts and emotions it produces. The Spirit-Soul Interface classification implies that love occupies the junction between the deepest dispositional level (spirit) and the experiential level (soul), which is consistent with it being simultaneously commanded (spirit/will) and felt (soul/affect). The partial status reflects that this is an inferred rather than explicitly evidenced constitutional location.
- Anchor verses: Lam 3:22, Pro 3:3, Mat 22:37
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE
- Stage 2b note: Spirit-level location is inferred from Spirit-as-source and from love's will-engagement character. Not explicitly named. Gap for Session D investigation.

**Q&A-040 | T2.1.4**
- Tier: T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries
- Component: T2.1 — Spirit-Level Location
- Prompt: 4 — If the evidence is silent on spirit-level location, note this explicitly.
- Disposition: NOT APPLICABLE
- Status tag: N
- Rationale: The evidence is not wholly silent — Q&A-037 through Q&A-039 identify Spirit-sourced location and spirit-implied characteristics. The closing condition ('if silent') does not fully apply. Partial evidence addressed above.
- Finding type: N/A

**Q&A-041 | T2.2.1**
- Tier: T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries
- Component: T2.2 — Soul-Level Location
- Prompt: 1 — Is this characteristic identified in the verse evidence as a soul-level phenomenon?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Yes — and with unusual density. Mat 22:37 ('love the Lord your God with all your heart and with all your soul and with all your mind') explicitly names the soul (nephesh/psuchē) as one of the constitutional locations of love — love is commanded as a soul-act. Song 5:6 ('my soul failed me') locates love's absence at the soul level — the soul's vitality collapses when the beloved departs (OBS-103-062, SP-103-031). Jer 12:7 ('the beloved of my soul') attributes a nephesh to God with a beloved located in it (OBS-103-086) — the soul as the seat of love's deepest attachment. Joh 15:13 ('lay down his psuchē for his friends') makes love's maximum expression a soul-act — the giving of the soul itself. 1Th 2:8 ('ready to share our own souls') repeats this pattern (OBS-103-123). The soul is one of love's primary constitutional locations.
- Anchor verses: Mat 22:37, Song 5:6, Jer 12:7, Joh 15:13, 1Th 2:8
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-042 | T2.2.2**
- Tier: T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries
- Component: T2.2 — Soul-Level Location
- Prompt: 2 — What does soul-level location reveal about this characteristic's place in the innermost personal experience?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Soul-level location reveals: (a) love's experiential depth — the soul is the seat of the person's felt inner life; love at the soul level is not intellectual assent but the deepest experiential attachment; (b) love's constitutive function for the soul — Song 5:6 (OBS-103-062) shows the soul failing at the beloved's absence: the soul's vitality is partly constituted by the love-object's presence. Love is not merely something the soul does; it is part of what the soul is sustained by; (c) love as the soul's highest risk — because the soul is invested in love, the loss of the beloved is the soul's most acute suffering. Grief is the soul-evidence of love (OBS-103-062, OBS-103-095). This is the constitutive-love finding: love and soul are not independent. The soul that loves is partly constituted by its love-object.
- Anchor verses: Song 5:6, Jer 12:7, Mat 22:37, 1Th 2:8
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-043 | T2.2.3**
- Tier: T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries
- Component: T2.2 — Soul-Level Location
- Prompt: 3 — If the evidence is silent on soul-level location, note this explicitly.
- Disposition: NOT APPLICABLE
- Status tag: N
- Rationale: Evidence is not silent — Q&A-041 and Q&A-042 document extensive soul-level love evidence. Closing condition does not apply.
- Finding type: N/A

**Q&A-044 | T2.3.1**
- Tier: T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries
- Component: T2.3 — Heart
- Prompt: 1 — Does the verse evidence locate this characteristic in the heart?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Yes — prominently. Mat 22:37 ('love with all your heart' — lev) names the heart as the first constitutional location of love. Pro 3:3 ('write them on the tablet of your heart' — OBS-103-090) places chesed/faithfulness as heart-inscriptions — love's dispositional form is written into the heart. Rom 5:5 ('God's love poured into our hearts through the Holy Spirit,' OBS-103-126) names the heart as the location of divine love's reception and indwelling. 1Ki 8:18 (OBS-103-103) — God accepts David's inner intention because 'it was in your heart' — love expressed as heart-intention is accepted even before outward act. Song 5:2 (OBS-103-108) — 'my heart was awake' while asleep — the heart persists in love-awareness even in sleep. The heart is love's primary named constitutional location in the data.
- Anchor verses: Mat 22:37, Pro 3:3, Rom 5:5, Song 5:2
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-045 | T2.3.2**
- Tier: T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries
- Component: T2.3 — Heart
- Prompt: 2 — What does heart-location reveal — what aspect of the heart's integrating function does this characteristic engage?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Heart-location reveals love's engagement with all four of the heart's functions: (a) **knowing** — the heart that loves also knows (Joh 15:15 — friendship constituted by knowledge-disclosure, OBS-103-052; Hos 6:6 — God desires knowledge of God alongside chesed, OBS-103-091); (b) **willing** — the heart is the seat of intention, and love is commanded at the heart level (Mat 22:37; 1Ki 8:18 — 'it was in your heart to build'); (c) **feeling** — Song 5:2 ('my heart was awake') — the heart's affective persistence in love; (d) **moral awareness** — Pro 3:3 (chesed and faithfulness written on the heart as moral character). Love engages the heart's full integrating function — it is not a partial heart-engagement but a total one, consistent with the 'with all your heart' formulation of the commandment.
- Anchor verses: Mat 22:37, Hos 6:6, Song 5:2, Pro 3:3
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-046 | T2.3.3**
- Tier: T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries
- Component: T2.3 — Heart
- Prompt: 3 — If the evidence is silent on heart-location, note this explicitly.
- Disposition: NOT APPLICABLE
- Status tag: N
