**Q&A-047 | T2.4.1**
- Tier: T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries
- Component: T2.4 — Mind
- Prompt: 1 — Does the verse evidence locate or engage this characteristic in the mind?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: Yes — the great commandment includes 'with all your mind' (dianoia — Mat 22:37, OBS-103-139), explicitly locating love at the mind level. Phili 4:8 (OBS-103-133) directs the mind to attend to what is lovely (prosfilēs) — love's aesthetic quality becomes the object of cognitive direction. Joh 15:15 (OBS-103-052) — love constituted by knowledge-disclosure — places the cognitive (knowledge) at the centre of the love-relationship. Hos 6:6 (OBS-103-091) — God desires 'knowledge of God' alongside chesed — the knowledge-love co-priority is a mind-engagement. The mind's engagement is primarily as the organ of knowledge that love opens access to (friendship = mutual knowledge) and as the faculty directed to attend to the lovely.
- Anchor verses: Mat 22:37, Phili 4:8, Joh 15:15, Hos 6:6
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-048 | T2.4.2**
- Tier: T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries
- Component: T2.4 — Mind
- Prompt: 2 — What does mind-engagement reveal about this characteristic's cognitive dimension?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Mind-engagement reveals that love has a genuine cognitive dimension — it is not sub-cognitive. The cognitive dimension operates in three ways: (a) **knowledge as love's medium** — friendship/love constituted by mutual knowledge-sharing (Joh 15:15) means love opens access to the inner world of the other and requires the mind's engagement to receive what is shared; (b) **cognitive direction toward the lovely** — Phili 4:8 makes the mind's attentiveness to what is lovely a cognitive act in service of love's orientation; (c) **knowledge of God as love's fruit** — Hos 6:6 and Jer 31:34 (OBS-103-072) place knowledge of God as the companion of love, with the new covenant completing the knowledge that love currently mediates. Love is cognitively demanding in the biblical data — it requires and produces knowledge.
- Anchor verses: Joh 15:15, Phili 4:8, Hos 6:6, Jer 31:34
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-049 | T2.5.1**
- Tier: T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries
- Component: T2.5 — Will
- Prompt: 1 — Is this characteristic engaged with or dependent on the will?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: Yes — emphatically. The commanded form of love ('you shall love' — Mat 22:37, Lev 19:18) requires the will's exercise — love cannot be merely a spontaneous feeling if it is commanded. Enemy-love (Mat 5:44, OBS-103-143) is the clearest evidence: loving enemies requires volitional engagement against natural preference. The ranking of loves (Mat 10:37, OBS-103-151) requires a deliberate choice-act — placing love of Christ above natural love of family. Ruth's chesed (Rut 3:10, OBS-103-089) — choosing the elderly Boaz over young men — is love expressed through will against self-interest. The will's engagement is not peripheral but central to love in its highest form (agapē, chesed). The affective forms (phileō, dod) may be less volitionally constituted, but the command-forms require the will.
- Anchor verses: Mat 22:37, Mat 5:44, Rut 3:10, Mat 10:37
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-050 | T2.5.2**
- Tier: T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries
- Component: T2.5 — Will
- Prompt: 2 — Does this characteristic produce or require an act of the will, or does it operate without volitional engagement?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: Both operate in the data — love both requires and produces will-acts. It requires the will: enemy-love (Mat 5:44), ranking of loves (Mat 10:37), and Ruth's choice (Rut 3:10) are all volitional love-acts. It produces will-acts: love of Christ produces commandment-keeping (Joh 14:15, OBS-103-140) — the inner orientation generates the volitional pattern of life. The two modes are distinct: love-as-act-of-will (requiring deliberate engagement) vs love-as-generator-of-will (the inner orientation that produces volitional patterns). Both are evidenced. The affective forms (phileō, dod) may operate without explicit volitional initiation, but they too produce will-acts (Peter's fileō generates faithful mission-response, Joh 21:17, OBS-103-153).
- Anchor verses: Mat 5:44, Joh 14:15, Joh 21:17, Rut 3:10
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-051 | T2.6.1**
- Tier: T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries
- Component: T2.6 — Emotion
- Prompt: 1 — Does the verse evidence associate this characteristic with emotional or affective states?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: Extensively. Joy (Psa 16:11, OBS-103-112; Zep 3:17, OBS-103-094); grief (Song 5:6, OBS-103-062; Joh 11:36, OBS-103-149; 2Sa 1:26, OBS-103-095); rest/stillness (Zep 3:17, OBS-103-094; Psa 127:2, OBS-103-084); delight (Song 2:16, OBS-103-061; Pro 5:19, OBS-103-099); compassion-movement (Luk 15:20, OBS-103-057; 1Ki 3:26, OBS-103-105); yearning (Jer 31:20, OBS-103-117); anguish at separation (Song 5:6, OBS-103-062). Love's emotional palette is among the richest in the programme. Love does not suppress emotion — it generates, focuses, and intensifies the inner affective life.
- Anchor verses: Psa 16:11, Zep 3:17, Song 5:6, Joh 11:36
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-052 | T2.6.2**
- Tier: T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries
- Component: T2.6 — Emotion
- Prompt: 2 — What emotional states does this characteristic produce or require?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Produced by love: joy and fullness of pleasure (Psa 16:11, OBS-103-112) — love in the presence of the beloved generates joy. Rest and quieting (Zep 3:17, OBS-103-094) — being loved by God produces inner stillness. Yearning (Jer 31:20, OBS-103-117) — God's love for Ephraim expressed as inner yearning for the wayward. Grief (2Sa 1:26, OBS-103-095; Song 5:6, OBS-103-062) — love under loss produces grief as its evidence. Intoxication/delight (Pro 5:19, OBS-103-099) — erotic love produces a pleasure-state described as intoxication. Required by love: compassion-movement (Luk 15:20, OBS-103-057) — responsive love requires the inner organs to be moved; without the emotional movement, the love-act does not occur. The full range: love produces the most positive (joy, delight, rest) and the most painful (grief, yearning) affective states in the inner-being vocabulary.
- Anchor verses: Psa 16:11, Zep 3:17, 2Sa 1:26, Pro 5:19
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-053 | T2.7.1**
- Tier: T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries
- Component: T2.7 — Conscience
- Prompt: 1 — Does this characteristic engage or affect the conscience?
- Disposition: PARTIALLY ANSWERED
- Status tag: P
- Notation: *Gap identified*
- Answer: Indirect evidence only. The conscience (suneidēsis) does not appear by name in R103's anchor verses. However: Lev 19:17 (OBS-103-114) — the prohibition on hating the brother 'in your heart' and the command to rebuke frankly — implies conscience-engagement: the inner recognition that hate is wrong and that honest love requires action. 2Cor 11:26 (OBS-103-067) and Gal 2:4 (OBS-103-068) — the false brother's concealed inner orientation — implies conscience is involved in the recognition of inner deception. The programme's suneidēsis registry (R026) co-occurs with love at Rom 8:29 (shared anchor). Gap: conscience's specific engagement with love is not explicitly evidenced in R103's anchor corpus. The conscience-love connection is inferred from the moral imperative structure of the love commands.
- Anchor verses: Lev 19:17, Rom 8:29 (via shared anchor)
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-054 | T2.8.1**
- Tier: T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries
- Component: T2.8 — Body — Deposit
- Prompt: 1 — Is there evidence that this characteristic leaves a constitutional deposit in the body — a somatic trace or formation?
- Disposition: PARTIALLY ANSWERED
- Status tag: P
- Notation: *Gap identified*
- Answer: The data provides extensive somatic expression evidence (Unit 7 — kiss, embrace, tears, womb-movement, inner organs) but the question of a lasting somatic deposit is distinct from somatic expression. Evidence relevant to deposit: Pro 3:3 — chesed written on the 'tablet of the heart' — the heart is a somatic location but this is more metaphorical inscription than physiological deposit. The inner organs (me'eka/splanchna) appear as the location of love's compassion-movement — this is a named somatic location but not clearly a lasting deposit. The womb-etymology of rachamim implies a bodily-constitutional rootedness of love. The evidence implies a deep somatic-constitutional rootedness of love without explicitly naming a body deposit. Gap: the precise question of lasting somatic deposit is not directly addressed. Flagging T5.7 dependency per instruction.
- Anchor verses: Pro 3:3, Isa 63:15, 1Ki 3:26
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE
- Stage 2b note: T2.8 partial — somatic expression extensively evidenced; lasting deposit inferred but not explicit. T5.7 to be addressed when reached; if T2.8 remains partial, T5.7 prompts will reflect accordingly.

**Q&A-055 | T2.9.1**
- Tier: T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries
- Component: T2.9 — Integration Across Levels
- Prompt: 1 — How does this characteristic integrate across the spirit-soul-heart-mind-body constitutional structure?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Love is the programme's most fully integrated constitutional characteristic. The integration: at the spirit/will level — love is commanded (Mat 22:37), covenantal (chesed), and willed (enemy-love, Mat 5:44); at the soul level — love is experienced (Song 5:6 — soul failing at beloved's absence), given (Joh 15:13 — soul laid down for friends), and constitutive of identity (nephesh of God has a beloved, Jer 12:7); at the heart level — love is inscribed (Pro 3:3), infused by the Spirit (Rom 5:5), and the seat of love-awareness (Song 5:2); at the mind level — love requires and produces knowledge (Joh 15:15, Hos 6:6), and directs cognitive attention to the lovely (Phili 4:8); at the body level — love is expressed through kiss, embrace, tears, the movement of inner organs (Unit 7 multiple instances). No constitutional level is absent from the love vocabulary. Love is the programme's most constitutionally comprehensive characteristic — it operates at all levels simultaneously.
- Anchor verses: Mat 22:37, Song 5:6, Pro 3:3, Phili 4:8
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-056 | T2.10.1**
- Tier: T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries
- Component: T2.10 — Constitutional Movement
- Prompt: 1 — Does this characteristic move across constitutional levels — from spirit to soul, from soul to body, or across boundaries in other directions?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Yes — the data evidences downward constitutional movement (from spirit-source into soul and body) as the primary direction. Rom 5:5 (OBS-103-126): God's love poured into hearts through the Spirit — movement from divine Spirit into the human heart (spirit → heart). Luk 15:20 (OBS-103-057): compassion (inner movement) → running → embrace → kiss — the inner compassion-love produces bodily movement (soul → body). Lam 3:22 (OBS-103-088) and Pro 3:3 (OBS-103-090): chesed at the character level (spirit) expressed in word and act (soul and body). The movement is consistently from the interior (spirit/heart) outward (soul/affect, then body/act). The inverse — body experience generating love-at-the-spirit-level — is not directly evidenced but may be implied in the somatic kiss-as-love-communication contexts.
- Anchor verses: Rom 5:5, Luk 15:20, Lam 3:22, Pro 3:3
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-057 | T2.10.2**
- Tier: T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries
- Component: T2.10 — Constitutional Movement
- Prompt: 2 — What does the evidence reveal about the sequence or pattern of that movement?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: The pattern from the data: divine love (Spirit-sourced) → enters heart (Rom 5:5) → produces soul-response (rest, joy, grief) → expresses bodily (kiss, embrace, tears, running). The sequence is: reception-at-depth → emergence-in-feeling → expression-in-body. This is the programme's first evidenced downward constitutional movement sequence for any characteristic. The intermediate soul-level is confirmed by OBS-103-041 and OBS-103-062 (Song) — love is experienced at the soul level before it expresses bodily. The body-level expression follows the soul-level experience: grief in the soul produces tears in the body; compassion-movement in the inner organs produces running and embrace. Pattern summary: Spirit origin → heart reception → soul experience → body expression.
- Anchor verses: Rom 5:5, Zep 3:17, Luk 15:20, 1Pe 5:14
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-058 | T2.10.3**
- Tier: T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries
- Component: T2.10 — Constitutional Movement
- Prompt: 3 — If no constitutional movement is evidenced, note this explicitly.
- Disposition: NOT APPLICABLE
- Status tag: N
- Rationale: Constitutional movement is extensively evidenced in Q&A-056 and Q&A-057. Closing condition does not apply.
- Finding type: N/A


**Q&A-059 | T2.4.3**
- Tier: T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries
- Component: T2.4 — Mind
- Prompt: 3 — If the evidence is silent on mind-engagement, note this explicitly.
- Disposition: NOT APPLICABLE
- Status tag: N
- Rationale: Mind-engagement is evidenced in Q&A-047 and Q&A-048. Closing condition does not apply.
- Finding type: N/A

**Q&A-060 | T2.5.3**
- Tier: T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries
- Component: T2.5 — Will
- Prompt: 3 — What does this engagement reveal about the depth of this characteristic's operation?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: Will-engagement reveals that love in the biblical data is not reducible to feeling — it is a chosen orientation that the person actively maintains and directs. Enemy-love (Mat 5:44, OBS-103-143) is the most demanding evidence: love directed against natural antipathy requires the will's deliberate and sustained engagement. This reveals that love has depth precisely at the point where feeling runs out — chesed persists when feeling does not (Lam 3:22, OBS-103-088). The will is love's constitutional ground when affective experience is withdrawn or absent. This is the programme's key distinguishing feature for love versus mere positive feeling: love can sustain itself volitionally when the soul-level affective experience is absent.
- Anchor verses: Mat 5:44, Lam 3:22
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-061 | T2.6.3**
- Tier: T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries
- Component: T2.6 — Emotion
- Prompt: 3 — Is this characteristic primarily emotional, or does the evidence position it differently?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Love is not primarily emotional in the biblical data, though it has a rich emotional dimension. The evidence positions love as primarily dispositional/constitutional — an inner orientation that produces emotional states rather than consisting in them. Chesed is the clearest evidence: it persists without depending on emotional states (Lam 3:22 — 'the steadfast love of the Lord never ceases' despite Israel's devastating judgment). Agapē of enemies (Mat 5:44) operates where positive feeling is absent or where it must overcome negative feeling. The emotional states (joy, grief, rest, yearning) are love's products and evidence, not its constitutive substance. If love were primarily emotional, its commanded form ('you shall love') would be incoherent — emotions cannot be commanded. The commanded form confirms that love's primary operation is dispositional-volitional; the emotional dimension is real but secondary.
- Anchor verses: Lam 3:22, Mat 5:44, Zep 3:17, Joh 11:36
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-062 | T2.7.2**
- Tier: T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries
- Component: T2.7 — Conscience
- Prompt: 2 — What does conscience-engagement (if present) reveal about this characteristic's moral depth?
- Disposition: PARTIALLY ANSWERED
- Status tag: P
- Notation: *Gap identified*
- Answer: The indirect evidence suggests conscience and love operate at the same moral depth but through different mechanisms. The conscience recognises the moral wrongness of hate-in-the-heart (Lev 19:17, OBS-103-114); love is what the conscience directs the person toward as the alternative. If conscience is the inner moral monitor, love is the inner moral orientation — the conscience identifies what violates love; love provides the positive orientation the conscience is protecting. Gap: this relationship is inferred, not directly evidenced in R103's anchor verses.
- Anchor verses: Lev 19:17
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-063 | T2.7.3**
- Tier: T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries
- Component: T2.7 — Conscience
- Prompt: 3 — If the evidence is silent on conscience-engagement, note this explicitly.
- Disposition: PARTIALLY ANSWERED
- Status tag: P
- Notation: *Gap identified*
- Answer: The evidence is not fully silent (see Q&A-053 and Q&A-062) but the direct naming of conscience in connection with love is absent from R103's anchor verse corpus. The co-occurrence of suneidēsis (R026) at the programme level (Rom 8:29 shared anchor) suggests a connection exists; its content is not determinable from the current data. Named gap: conscience-love explicit relationship not directly evidenced; inferred only.
- Anchor verses: Rom 8:29 (shared anchor only)
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-064 | T2.8.2**
- Tier: T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries
- Component: T2.8 — Body — Deposit
- Prompt: 2 — If a body deposit is evidenced, what is its nature and what does it reveal about this characteristic's permanence or constitutional weight?
- Disposition: PARTIALLY ANSWERED
- Status tag: P
- Notation: *Gap identified*
- Answer: The heart-inscription of chesed/faithfulness (Pro 3:3, OBS-103-090) — 'write them on the tablet of your heart' — is the closest evidence to a constitutional body-deposit: the heart-tablet metaphor implies that love's dispositional form is inscribed into the person's constitutional core. If this is treated as a deposit analogy, it reveals: (a) love's dispositional form (chesed) is meant to be a permanent inner-being inscription, not a transient orientation; (b) the heart as the deposit location is the deepest accessible somatic address in the love vocabulary; (c) the 'tablet' language implies durability — written, not merely felt. However, this is metaphorical language whose literal constitutional meaning is uncertain. Partial: the heart-inscription is the best available deposit-candidate in the data.
- Anchor verses: Pro 3:3
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-065 | T2.8.3**
- Tier: T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries
- Component: T2.8 — Body — Deposit
- Prompt: 3 — If no body deposit is evidenced, note this explicitly and flag the T5.7 dependency.
- Disposition: PARTIALLY ANSWERED
- Status tag: P
- Notation: *Gap identified*
- Answer: Body deposit in the explicit sense is not directly evidenced. The heart-inscription (Pro 3:3) is the closest candidate. The inner organs (me'eka/splanchna) are love's somatic location of compassion-movement but represent somatic expression rather than lasting deposit. For T5.7: if the body deposit at T2.8 is treated as absent or uncertain, T5.7 (Deposit Consequence) will receive not-applicable responses for all three prompts per the instruction's rule. This is flagged here. Recommendation: treat T2.8 as 'partially evidenced' (heart-inscription as metaphorical deposit candidate) and process T5.7 accordingly — neither full confirmation nor full N.
- Anchor verses: Pro 3:3
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Stage 2b note — T2 complete.** 31 prompts processed. T2.8 remains partially answered; T5.7 will be addressed when reached. Summary: love occupies all constitutional levels (spirit-implied, soul-explicit, heart-explicit, mind-explicit, body-expressed). The constitutional movement pattern is: Spirit-origin → heart-reception → soul-experience → body-expression.


#### Tier 3 — Inner Faculties — 20 prompts

**Q&A-066 | T3.1.1**
- Tier: T3 — Inner Faculties
- Component: T3.1 — Attention and Perception
- Prompt: 1 — Does this characteristic engage or shape the faculty of attention and perception?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Yes. Phili 4:8 (OBS-103-133) is the clearest evidence: 'whatever is lovely (prosfilēs), think about these things' — love's aesthetic quality becomes the object that the attention-faculty (logizesthe — reckon, take account of) is commanded to attend to. Love shapes what the person notices and regards as worth attending to. Song 5:2 (OBS-103-108): the heart's wakefulness while the person sleeps — the beloved becomes the first object of perception even in the liminal state between sleep and waking. Joh 15:19 (OBS-103-150): the world loves its own — in-group love shapes the perception of who belongs and who is other. Love as a perceptual lens: what is loved becomes salient; what is not loved becomes invisible or threatening.
- Anchor verses: Phili 4:8, Song 5:2, Joh 15:19
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-067 | T3.2.1**
- Tier: T3 — Inner Faculties
- Component: T3.2 — Reason and Judgment
- Prompt: 1 — Does this characteristic engage the faculty of reason and judgment?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: Yes — through the judgment of the love-object's worth and the assessment of love's hierarchy. Mat 10:37 (OBS-103-151) requires a judgment: 'whoever loves father or mother more than me is not worthy of me' — love operates through a comparative judgment of worth among competing objects. The ranking of loves (OBS-103-022 — love as four-mode structure) requires reason to navigate. Jam 4:4 (OBS-103-058): the reasoning that friendship with the world constitutes enmity with God is a logical judgment. Pro 10:12 (OBS-103-097): 'love covers all offences' — the judgment that covering is better than exposing is a reasoned moral assessment. Love requires and shapes the judgment-faculty at the level of determining what and whom to love, in what order, and how.
- Anchor verses: Mat 10:37, Jam 4:4, Pro 10:12
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-068 | T3.3.1**
- Tier: T3 — Inner Faculties
- Component: T3.3 — Memory
- Prompt: 1 — Does this characteristic engage or depend on the faculty of memory?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Yes — and with unusual depth. Jer 2:2 (OBS-103-098): God remembers ('I remember the devotion of your youth') — divine love operates through memory of the prior love-relationship. The remembered love becomes the measure of the present failure ('how you followed me in the wilderness'). Jer 12:7 and Jer 31:20 (OBS-103-086, OBS-103-117): 'I do remember him still' — God's persistent love for Ephraim despite judgment-speech is grounded in divine memory. Lam 3:22 (OBS-103-088): the remembrance of God's chesed ('his mercies never come to an end') is the act of memory that sustains hope in the midst of desolation. Memory functions as love's sustaining faculty: love that cannot remember the beloved cannot maintain itself through absence or failure.
- Anchor verses: Jer 2:2, Jer 31:20, Lam 3:22
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-069 | T3.4.1**
- Tier: T3 — Inner Faculties
- Component: T3.4 — Imagination and Vision
- Prompt: 1 — Does this characteristic engage the faculty of imagination and forward vision?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Yes. Psa 27:13 (OBS-103-080): 'I believe that I shall look upon the goodness of the Lord in the land of the living' — the psalmist's forward vision of God's love/goodness sustains the present inner life. The love-vocabulary consistently generates forward orientation (OBS-103-006, Q&A-006 — eschatological trajectory of love). Jer 31:3 (OBS-103-093): 'I have loved you with an everlasting love' — the everlasting qualifier generates an imagined future of permanent love. Song 2:16 (OBS-103-061): 'my beloved is mine' — the possession formula is also anticipatory: the belovedness extends into the imagined future. Imagination engages as love's visionary faculty — projecting the love-relationship into the future and sustaining the present through that projection.
- Anchor verses: Psa 27:13, Jer 31:3, Song 2:16
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-070 | T3.5.1**
- Tier: T3 — Inner Faculties
- Component: T3.5 — Creativity
- Prompt: 1 — Does this characteristic engage or produce creative expression?
- Disposition: PARTIALLY ANSWERED
- Status tag: P
- Notation: *Gap identified*
- Answer: Indirectly evidenced. The Song of Songs is love's most concentrated creative expression in Scripture — a poem whose entire form (extended metaphor, nature imagery, dialogue structure) is the creative vehicle of love-expression (OBS-103-041). Isa 5:1 (OBS-103-083): 'let me sing for my beloved my love song' — love generating song as creative expression. The kiss vocabulary (kiss = creative somatic expression of love) and the anointing (Luk 7:38, OBS-103-056) are body-as-creative-medium. However, the explicit creativity-faculty engagement (imagination deployed in artistic creation) is not named in the data — the creative dimension is inferred from the Song's form and from the love-song references. Partial: love generates creative expression in the data; explicit creativity-faculty engagement not directly named.
- Anchor verses: Isa 5:1, Song 2:16, Luk 7:38
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-071 | T3.6.1**
- Tier: T3 — Inner Faculties
- Component: T3.6 — Desire and Appetite
- Prompt: 1 — Does this characteristic engage or relate to the faculty of desire and appetite?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: Yes — the desire-love boundary is analytically significant in the data. The dod and ahavah-intense vocabulary occupies the same semantic space as desire (R043 shares the ahav verbal root, OBS-103-022). Song 5:6 (OBS-103-062) — 'my soul failed me' — is desire-like in its intensity: the longing for the absent beloved. The yearning of God's inner parts (Jer 31:20, OBS-103-117) uses the same language-field as desire. Hos 6:6 (OBS-103-091): 'I desire (chaphets) steadfast love' — love becomes the object of God's desire. Heb 12:16 (OBS-103-078): Esau's appetite (trophe — food-desire) displacing love's covenantal inheritance is the paradigmatic desire-love conflict. The desire-faculty is love's closest adjacent faculty — love and desire share a mechanism (orientation toward an object) but are distinguished in the programme by the nature and stability of the commitment.
- Anchor verses: Song 5:6, Hos 6:6, Heb 12:16, Jer 31:20
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-072 | T3.7.1**
- Tier: T3 — Inner Faculties
- Component: T3.7 — Affection and Emotion
- Prompt: 1 — How does this characteristic engage the affective-emotional faculty?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Consistent with prior analysis*
- Answer: Already fully addressed in T2.6 (Q&A-051, Q&A-052, Q&A-061). Love engages the affective faculty as its primary experiential medium — joy, grief, rest, delight, yearning, compassion-movement are love's affective palette. Love is not reducible to affective state (Q&A-061) but the affective faculty is love's most immediate experiential expression. The distinctive feature: love's affective range spans the widest spectrum in the programme — from the deepest joy (Psa 16:11) to the deepest grief (Song 5:6, 2Sa 1:26). Love is the affective faculty's governing characteristic.
- Anchor verses: Psa 16:11, Song 5:6, Zep 3:17
- Finding type: N/A
- Stage 2b note: Cross-reference to T2.6 responses — no additional content beyond T2.6.

**Q&A-073 | T3.8.1**
- Tier: T3 — Inner Faculties
- Component: T3.8 — Moral Sensitivity
- Prompt: 1 — Does this characteristic shape the faculty of moral sensitivity?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Yes — love is the primary shaper of moral sensitivity in the data. Psa 97:10 (OBS-103-115): 'O you who love the Lord, hate evil' — love of God directly produces moral sensitivity to evil (the capacity to hate what is wrong). Lev 19:17 (OBS-103-114): the prohibition on hating the brother in the heart implies that moral sensitivity recognises inner hate as morally significant. 1Cor 13:6 (within OBS-103-127): love 'does not rejoice in wrongdoing' — love shapes the moral sensitivity that recognises wrongdoing as something not to be celebrated. Pro 10:12 (OBS-103-097): love's moral sensitivity distinguishes between hatred-that-stirs-strife and love-that-covers — the faculty that makes this distinction is morally sensitised by love. Love functions as the moral-sensitivity calibrator: it determines what the inner person registers as morally significant and how they register it.
- Anchor verses: Psa 97:10, Lev 19:17, 1Cor 13:6, Pro 10:12
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-074 | T3.9.1**
- Tier: T3 — Inner Faculties
- Component: T3.9 — Conscience (Faculty dimension)
- Prompt: 1 — How does this characteristic relate to conscience as a faculty?
- Disposition: PARTIALLY ANSWERED
- Status tag: P
- Notation: *Gap identified*
- Answer: The conscience-as-faculty relationship to love is addressed at T2.7 (Q&A-053, Q&A-062, Q&A-063). The additional faculty-dimension: the conscience functions as the internal monitor that activates when love's requirements are violated (hating the brother in the heart, Lev 19:17) or when love's form is distorted (false brotherhood, Gal 2:4). Love provides the positive standard; conscience provides the monitoring mechanism. The faculty-relationship: love is the norm; conscience is the norm-enforcer in the inner person. Gap: the direct conscience-love faculty interaction is not named in R103's anchor verses. The relationship is structurally inferred.
- Anchor verses: Lev 19:17, Gal 2:4
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-075 | T3.10.1**
- Tier: T3 — Inner Faculties
- Component: T3.10 — Identity and Self-Understanding
- Prompt: 1 — Does this characteristic engage or constitute the faculty of identity and self-understanding?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: This is one of love's most significant contributions in the data. Belovedness as identity: agapētos (OBS-103-040, OBS-103-122) — the believer's primary identity designation is 'loved by God and called.' Being loved constitutes who the person is; identity is received through the love-relationship, not self-generated. Mat 3:17 (OBS-103-120): the Father's declaration 'this is my beloved Son' constitutes Christ's identity — being named beloved is identity-conferral. Joh 13:35 (OBS-103-129): the community's identity ('my disciples') is constituted by its love for one another — what you love constitutes your community identity. What you love as the individual also constitutes personal identity: the money-lover (OBS-103-132), the God-lover (OBS-103-118), the world-lover (OBS-103-148) — love is the diagnostic identity-marker. Identity in the biblical data is constituted by: (a) being loved (passive — agapētos) and (b) what you love (active — the love-object as identity-definer).
- Anchor verses: Mat 3:17, Joh 13:35, Rom 1:7, 2Ti 3:2-4
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-076 | T3.11.1**
- Tier: T3 — Inner Faculties
- Component: T3.11 — Relational Capacity
- Prompt: 1 — Does this characteristic build, sustain, or restore relational capacity?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: All three — building, sustaining, and restoring — are evidenced. Building: Joh 13:34 (OBS-103-145) — 'as I have loved you, you also are to love one another' — establishes the community as a new relational structure constituted by love. Sustaining: Lam 3:22 (OBS-103-088) — chesed that never ceases sustains the covenant relationship through judgment and desolation. Pro 3:3 (OBS-103-090) — heart-inscription sustains the disposition through circumstances. Restoring: Luk 15:20 (OBS-103-057) — the father's compassion-love restores the broken relationship with the returning son. Luk 7:47 (via SD-020): 'she loved much because she was forgiven much' — restored relationship (through forgiveness) produces love as its fruit. The restoration function: love does not merely sustain what exists but restores what has been broken — this is one of love's most structurally important capacities.
- Anchor verses: Joh 13:34, Lam 3:22, Luk 15:20, Pro 3:3
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE


#### Tier 4 — Relational Interfaces — 22 prompts

**Q&A-077 | T4.1.1**
- Tier: T4 — Relational Interfaces
- Component: T4.1 — God-to-Human Direction
- Prompt: 1 — What does the evidence reveal about how this characteristic flows from God to the human person?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: The God-to-human direction is the programme's most evidentially dense directional axis for any characteristic. Four primary mechanisms: (a) **Covenantal declaration** — God names the love-relationship: 'I have loved you with an everlasting love' (Jer 31:3, OBS-103-093); 'you are the beloved of my soul' (Jer 12:7, OBS-103-086); 'This is my beloved Son' (Mat 3:17, OBS-103-120). The declaration is performative — it constitutes the relationship. (b) **Infusion** — God's love poured into hearts through the Spirit (Rom 5:5, OBS-103-126) — the Spirit as agent of love's transfer from divine to human inner being. (c) **Acts of love** — God gave his Son (Joh 3:16, OBS-103-141); God restores, forgives, compassionates (Lam 3:22, Isa 49:15, Jer 31:20). (d) **Covenantal covering** — Eze 16:8 (OBS-103-083b): God spreads his garment, makes a vow, enters covenant — the love-gift that constitutes the relationship. The overall pattern: divine love moves toward the human person through declaration, infusion, act, and covenant.
- Anchor verses: Jer 31:3, Joh 3:16, Rom 5:5, Eze 16:8
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-078 | T4.1.2**
- Tier: T4 — Relational Interfaces
- Component: T4.1 — God-to-Human Direction
- Prompt: 2 — What does this direction reveal about the nature of this characteristic as a divine gift?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Divine love as gift has two structural features in the data: (a) **Priority** — 1Jo 4:19 ('we love because he first loved us') — divine love precedes all human love; it is not responsive to human merit but prior to it. Jer 31:3 ('with an everlasting love I have loved you') — the love predates the present moment and will outlast it. (b) **Sufficiency** — Heb 13:5 (OBS-103-138): the promise 'I will never leave you nor forsake you' is the ground for freedom from love-of-money — divine love is sufficient to displace the need for material security. The gift of divine love reorders the inner economy: receiving it makes other attachments unnecessary. As gift, divine love is both prior (unconditioned by merit) and sufficient (displacing rival loves by its own fullness).
- Anchor verses: 1Jo 4:19, Jer 31:3, Heb 13:5
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-079 | T4.1.3**
- Tier: T4 — Relational Interfaces
- Component: T4.1 — God-to-Human Direction
- Prompt: 3 — What is the inner-being state of the person as receiver of this characteristic from God?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: The receiver is constituted as agapētos (beloved) — an identity state, not merely a felt experience (OBS-103-040, OBS-103-122). The immediate inner-being state upon receiving divine love: rest/quieting (Zep 3:17, OBS-103-094); fullness and pleasure (Psa 16:11, OBS-103-112); soul-satisfaction (Jer 31:14, OBS-103-081). The sustained inner-being state: security ('I will never leave you' — Heb 13:5), known-ness ('Lord, you know everything — Joh 21:17, OBS-103-153), and free-from-striving (Psa 127:2, OBS-103-084). The person who receives divine love becomes the person who rests in it. The identity-state (beloved) and the experiential state (rest, fullness) are both dimensions of the receiver's inner condition.
- Anchor verses: Zep 3:17, Psa 16:11, Psa 127:2, Rom 1:7
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-080 | T4.2.1**
- Tier: T4 — Relational Interfaces
- Component: T4.2 — Human-to-God Direction
- Prompt: 1 — What does the evidence reveal about how the human person expresses or directs this characteristic toward God?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: Human love toward God is the great commandment's content: love with all heart, soul, and mind (Mat 22:37, OBS-103-139). The data shows love toward God expressed through: (a) **Total mobilisation** — 'with all your heart and soul and mind' — no faculty withheld; (b) **Commandment-keeping** — 'if you love me, you will keep my commandments' (Joh 14:15, OBS-103-140) — love produces the obedience-pattern; (c) **Priority-ranking** — love of God above family love (Mat 10:37, OBS-103-151), above love of the present world (2Ti 4:10, OBS-103-148); (d) **Costly following** — Jer 2:2 (OBS-103-098) — Israel's early love expressed through following God into the wilderness; (e) **Praise** — Psa 63:3 (OBS-103-087): 'because your steadfast love is better than life, my lips will praise you' — love toward God expressed as praise. The human-to-God direction is constituted by total inner mobilisation, life-ordering, and expressive acts.
- Anchor verses: Mat 22:37, Joh 14:15, Psa 63:3, Jer 2:2
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-081 | T4.2.2**
- Tier: T4 — Relational Interfaces
- Component: T4.2 — Human-to-God Direction
- Prompt: 2 — What does this direction reveal about the conditions or capacities required for this characteristic to flow from human to God?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: The condition for human love toward God is prior reception of divine love (1Jo 4:19 — 'we love because he first loved us'). Human love toward God is always responsive, not originating. The capacity required: soul-purification (1Pe 1:22, OBS-103-124) — the inner person must be cleared of the disordering loves that block genuine love toward God. The great commandment ('with all your soul') implies that the soul must be free from divided ultimate attachment to function as love-toward-God. Love of money (1Ti 6:10, OBS-103-132) and love of the world (2Ti 4:10, OBS-103-148) represent the prior conditions that prevent the human-to-God love-flow. The capacity for human love toward God is therefore: received divine love (enabling condition) + soul-purification from rival loves (clearing condition).
- Anchor verses: 1Jo 4:19, 1Pe 1:22, 1Ti 6:10
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-082 | T4.2.3**
- Tier: T4 — Relational Interfaces
- Component: T4.2 — Human-to-God Direction
- Prompt: 3 — What is the inner-being state of the person who directs this characteristic toward God?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: The data gives several descriptions: (a) Psa 63:3 (OBS-103-087): the person who loves God so values chesed above life that praise becomes natural — the inner state is one of valuation so high it reorders the hierarchy of goods; (b) Joh 14:15 (OBS-103-140): the person who loves Christ keeps commandments — the inner state produces a habitual obedience-pattern; (c) 1Pe 2:17 (OBS-103-065): 'love the brotherhood, fear God' — love toward God and fear of God co-exist as the person's dual dispositional orientation toward the divine. Fear is not love's replacement but its companion. The inner state: reverent love, or loving reverence — the integration of love and fear that Hos 3:5 names ('come in fear to the Lord and to his goodness,' OBS-103-082). The person who loves God is also the person who properly fears God.
- Anchor verses: Psa 63:3, Joh 14:15, 1Pe 2:17, Hos 3:5
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-083 | T4.3.1**
- Tier: T4 — Relational Interfaces
- Component: T4.3 — Giving
- Prompt: 1 — What does the evidence reveal about love as something given — expressed outward toward others?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: Love as given outward is the primary ethical direction of the commandment structure: love your neighbour (Lev 19:18), love your enemy (Mat 5:44), love one another (Joh 13:34). The giving of love reaches its maximum in Joh 15:13 (OBS-103-125) — 'greater love has no one than this: that someone lay down his life/soul for his friends.' The gift of the soul is love's outer limit. The giving-forms span: chesed as daily covenantal faithfulness given to the covenant-partner (OBS-103-089); agapē given to the enemy against natural preference (OBS-103-143); phileō given as warmth within the community (OBS-103-119); rachamim given as compassion toward the suffering (OBS-103-105). Love-as-given is the primary ethical form in which the inner orientation is concretely actualised.
- Anchor verses: Joh 15:13, Mat 5:44, Lev 19:18, Rut 3:10
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-084 | T4.4.1**
- Tier: T4 — Relational Interfaces
- Component: T4.4 — Receiving
- Prompt: 1 — What does the evidence reveal about love as something received — received from God or from others?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: Love as received is constitutive of identity (agapētos, OBS-103-040), productive of rest (Zep 3:17, OBS-103-094), and the enabling condition for giving love (1Jo 4:19, OBS-103-146). The reception is: (a) constitutive — being named beloved by God constitutes who the person is; (b) enabling — divine love received is what makes human love possible (1Jo 4:19); (c) experiential — rest, fullness, and joy are the experiential register of received love. Reception of love is not passive — Song 5:2 (OBS-103-108) shows the beloved opening the door; Luk 15:20 (OBS-103-057) shows the son returning. Some movement toward the source appears to be the condition for reception (Q&A-031).
- Anchor verses: 1Jo 4:19, Zep 3:17, Rom 1:7, Luk 15:20
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-085 | T4.4.2**
- Tier: T4 — Relational Interfaces
- Component: T4.4 — Receiving
- Prompt: 2 — What does it mean to truly receive this characteristic versus encountering it without receiving it?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: The data provides a distinction. True reception: 1Jo 4:19 — responsive love flows; the person who receives divine love loves in return. Psa 127:2 (OBS-103-084) — the beloved sleeps — reception produces rest and effortlessness. Jer 31:14 (OBS-103-081) — the soul is satisfied. Non-reception: Joh 3:19 (OBS-103-147) — those who encounter light-love do not receive it because their inner love-commitment runs the other way. The distinguishing feature: genuine reception of love produces love in return (1Jo 4:19) and produces rest/satisfaction (Psa 127:2). Non-reception while encountering: the person continues in the disordered love that blocked reception, unchanged and satisfied with it. The test of reception is: does love-received produce love-outward and rest-inward? If so, reception is genuine. If the person encounters the love-offer but remains oriented toward a rival love-object, reception has not occurred.
- Anchor verses: 1Jo 4:19, Psa 127:2, Joh 3:19
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-086 | T4.4.3**
- Tier: T4 — Relational Interfaces
- Component: T4.4 — Receiving
- Prompt: 3 — What is the inner-being state of the person who encounters this characteristic but does not receive it?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Consistent with prior analysis*
- Answer: Already addressed at T1.7.3 (Q&A-033). The person who does not receive love is not loveless but misdirected — loving a wrong object. The inner state is commitment to the rival love that blocks reception. The person remains internally coherent (in their own economy of loves) but existentially misdirected. No additional evidence beyond Q&A-033.
- Anchor verses: Joh 3:19, 2Ti 4:10, Luk 16:14
- Finding type: N/A

**Q&A-087 | T4.5.1**
- Tier: T4 — Relational Interfaces
- Component: T4.5 — Human-to-Human Direction
- Prompt: 1 — What does the evidence reveal about how this characteristic flows between human persons?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: Human-to-human love is the ethical core of the love commandment. The data shows it operating in five structural relationships: (a) **Neighbour** (H7453 rea — 173 active) — the primary OT ethical form: 'love your neighbour as yourself' (Lev 19:18); (b) **Enemy** (Mat 5:44, OBS-103-143) — the most demanding NT extension — love directed to those who actively oppose the person; (c) **Community of faith** (Joh 13:34, 1Th 3:12) — mutual love as the community's defining practice; (d) **Friendship** (filos, H0157H, dod vocabulary) — personal loyal love; (e) **Family** (filadelfia, filostorgos, filoteknos, filandros) — love within natural and spiritual family structures. The human-to-human direction is the most evidentially diverse — spanning obligation (neighbour-love), choice (friendship), natural bond (family), and cost (enemy-love).
- Anchor verses: Lev 19:18, Mat 5:44, Joh 13:34, Pro 27:6
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-088 | T4.5.2**
- Tier: T4 — Relational Interfaces
- Component: T4.5 — Human-to-Human Direction
- Prompt: 2 — What does the human-to-human direction of this characteristic reveal about the social and relational architecture it creates?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Human-to-human love creates a social architecture with three features: (a) **Restructured family** — Mat 12:50 (OBS-103-063): 'whoever does the will of my Father is my brother and sister and mother' — love redraws the family boundary around shared orientation toward God rather than natural kinship. (b) **Public community mark** — Joh 13:35 (OBS-103-129): mutual love is externally legible as the community's identity. The social architecture of love is publicly readable — it creates a community whose internal reality is visible to outsiders. (c) **Competitive generosity** — Rom 12:10 (OBS-103-119): 'outdo one another in showing honor' — love creates a social order where the competition is in giving rather than taking, in honour-showing rather than honour-claiming. These three features constitute a social architecture that is structurally counter to the natural social patterns of kinship, concealment, and rivalry.
- Anchor verses: Mat 12:50, Joh 13:35, Rom 12:10
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-089 | T4.5.3**
- Tier: T4 — Relational Interfaces
- Component: T4.5 — Human-to-Human Direction
- Prompt: 3 — What conditions or breakdowns of this direction does the evidence name?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: Breakdowns evidenced: (a) **False brotherhood** — Gal 2:4 (OBS-103-068): using the community-love structure to serve a contrary agenda — the most dangerous breakdown because it uses love's form; (b) **Betrayal-kiss** — Luk 22:48 (OBS-103-054): love's somatic sign (kiss) used to indicate enmity — betrayal as the weaponisation of love's language; (c) **Desertion for world-love** — 2Ti 4:10 (OBS-103-148): abandonment of love-community for love of world; (d) **Poverty-caused dissolution** — Pro 19:7 (OBS-103-073): friendship tested by adversity may fail when it was conditional; (e) **Pride-driven rivalry** — Luk 22:24 (OBS-103-131): love-of-primacy at the table of the Lord. Conditions for maintenance: honest engagement (Lev 19:17, frank rebuke), soul-purification (1Pe 1:22), shared suffering (1Pe 5:9). The most dangerous breakdown is false brotherhood — it operates inside the love-structure while working against it.
- Anchor verses: Gal 2:4, Luk 22:48, Pro 19:7, 1Pe 1:22
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-090 | T4.6.1**
- Tier: T4 — Relational Interfaces
- Component: T4.6 — Spiritual Beings
- Prompt: 1 — Does the evidence address this characteristic in relation to spiritual beings (angels, spiritual realities)?
- Disposition: NOT ANSWERED
- Status tag: S
- Notation: *Gap identified*
- Answer: The data does not directly address love in relation to spiritual beings in R103's anchor verse corpus. 1Cor 13:1 ('if I speak in the tongues of angels, but have not love') is implicitly referenced via the 1Cor 13 cluster but is not a named anchor verse. The absence is noted. Gap: love's relationship to angelic beings or spiritual realities is not evidenced in the current data package.
- Anchor verses: none
- Finding type: N/A


#### Tier 5 — Formative and Developmental — 20 prompts

**Q&A-091 | T5.1.1**
- Tier: T5 — Formative and Developmental
- Component: T5.1 — Acquisition and Growth
- Prompt: 1 — Does the evidence address how this characteristic is acquired or cultivated?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Yes — multiple acquisition-pathways: (a) **Reception of divine love** — 1Jo 4:19 (OBS-103-146): human love is acquired by receiving divine love first. The primary acquisition pathway is reception, not self-generation. (b) **Spirit infusion** — Rom 5:5 (OBS-103-126): God's love poured into hearts through the Spirit — the Spirit is the agent of love's acquisition at the heart level. Gal 5:22 — love as the Spirit's fruit — love grows in the person as the Spirit produces it. (c) **Training** — Tit 2:4 (OBS-103-124 context): young women trained to love husbands and children — love as a domestically trainable virtue. (d) **Soul purification through obedience** — 1Pe 1:22 (OBS-103-124): obedience purifies the soul for sincere love. The obedience-pathway cleanses the inner person of what blocks love, enabling authentic love to emerge. (e) **Covenant-formation** — Pro 3:3: chesed written on the heart — love is inscribed through the practices of the covenant life.
- Anchor verses: 1Jo 4:19, Rom 5:5, Tit 2:4, 1Pe 1:22
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-092 | T5.1.2**
- Tier: T5 — Formative and Developmental
- Component: T5.1 — Acquisition and Growth
- Prompt: 2 — Is there evidence for genuine growth or increase in this characteristic?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: Yes — explicitly. 1Th 3:12 (OBS-103-130): 'may the Lord make you increase and abound in love' — love admits of increase; the Lord is the agent of its growth. The prayer-form implies that love's increase is both desirable and possible, dependent on the Lord's action. The degree-language in the data also implies growth: Rut 3:10 — 'you have made this last kindness greater than the first' — chesed measurably greater in a later act than an earlier one. Love is not fixed at a static level but admits of deepening expression and increase over time.
- Anchor verses: 1Th 3:12, Rut 3:10
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-093 | T5.2.1**
- Tier: T5 — Formative and Developmental
- Component: T5.2 — Transformation
- Prompt: 1 — Does this characteristic produce transformation in the person who possesses or exercises it?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Yes. Joh 15:15 (OBS-103-052): the disciples are transformed from servants to friends through Christ's love — a fundamental identity and relational reclassification. 1Pe 1:22 (OBS-103-124): soul-purification as the outcome of the love-formation process — the inner person is changed by the pathway that leads to sincere love. The 1Cor 13 trajectory (OBS-103-127): love's sustained exercise produces a character that does not envy, boast, or seek its own — the moral character is transformed by the practice of love. Luk 7:47 (via SD-020): the woman who loves much has been transformed by forgiveness — the transformation in her produced the love-expression. Love both requires and produces transformation.
- Anchor verses: Joh 15:15, 1Pe 1:22, 1Cor 13:4-7
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-094 | T5.3.1**
- Tier: T5 — Formative and Developmental
- Component: T5.3 — Reversibility
- Prompt: 1 — Is this characteristic reversible — can it be lost or its formation undone?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: The data shows love can be abandoned or displaced, but the covenantal-divine form (chesed, agapē) is presented as permanent. Human love: reversible. 2Ti 4:10 (OBS-103-148): Demas' love of Paul's community abandoned for love of the world — the human love-commitment can be redirected. Mat 10:37 (OBS-103-151) implies love-rankings can be disordered (natural love displacing love of Christ). Joh 21:17: Peter's love was contested but affirmed — the question of love's persistence through failure is the Joh 21 theme. Divine love: irreversible in character. Jer 31:3 (OBS-103-093): 'with an everlasting love' — the qualifier rules out reversibility for the divine instance. Lam 3:22 (OBS-103-088): 'chesed never ceases' — divine chesed is by definition permanent. The distinction: divine love as irreversible; human love as subject to redirection through competing love-allegiances.
- Anchor verses: 2Ti 4:10, Jer 31:3, Lam 3:22, Joh 21:17
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-095 | T5.4.1**
- Tier: T5 — Formative and Developmental
- Component: T5.4 — Mechanism
- Prompt: 1 — What is the mechanism by which this characteristic operates or is produced in the inner being?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: The primary mechanism from the data: divine love received → responsive love generated (1Jo 4:19). The Spirit is the operating agent of this mechanism (Rom 5:5, Gal 5:22) — the Spirit infuses divine love into the heart, which produces the inner reorientation toward love. The soul-purification mechanism (1Pe 1:22): obedience → purification → sincere love — a preparatory clearing that enables love to emerge. The training mechanism (Tit 2:4): repeated practice within the community forms love as a stable disposition. The forgiveness-trigger mechanism (Luk 7:47 — via SD-020): received forgiveness generates love as its fruit. Together: love's mechanism operates at multiple levels — the Spirit as the primary agent, obedience as the clearing condition, practice as the formation pathway, and received forgiveness as a specific love-trigger.
- Anchor verses: 1Jo 4:19, Rom 5:5, 1Pe 1:22, Tit 2:4
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-096 | T5.5.1**
- Tier: T5 — Formative and Developmental
- Component: T5.5 — Eschatological Trajectory
- Prompt: 1 — What is the eschatological trajectory of this characteristic — what is it moving toward?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: The data presents love as eschatologically oriented toward perfection and direct knowledge. Jer 31:34 (OBS-103-072): the new covenant vision — love of neighbour is superseded by direct divine knowledge; the mediated form of love (teaching the neighbour about God) gives way to the direct form. 1Jo 4:18 (via SP-103-029): perfect love casts out fear — 'perfect love' is an eschatological state that eliminates the inner-being disturbance of fear. 1Th 3:12 (OBS-103-130): love abounds toward the Lord's coming — love is moving toward a fullness coinciding with the eschatological event. Psa 16:11 (OBS-103-112): 'pleasures forevermore' at God's right hand — the eschatological fullness of the love-relationship is pleasures without end. The trajectory: love is currently partial (partial knowledge, partial reception) and is moving toward perfection (direct knowledge, perfect love, eternal pleasure in God's presence).
- Anchor verses: Jer 31:34, 1Th 3:12, Psa 16:11
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-097 | T5.6.1**
- Tier: T5 — Formative and Developmental
- Component: T5.6 — Formation Through Others
- Prompt: 1 — Does this characteristic require the presence or action of others for its formation?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: Yes — fundamentally. Love cannot be formed in isolation: it requires a beloved to be directed toward. The community formation of love (Joh 13:34 — 'love one another'; filadelfia cultivated together; training in Tit 2:4 within a community context) is inherently relational. The primary formation-by-others: reception of divine love as the enabling condition (1Jo 4:19) — God's action toward the person is the formative ground. The community of mutual love (1Pe 1:22 — 'sincere brotherly love' developed through shared obedience) is a communal-formation context. Love cannot be a solo formation project — it requires the other's presence, action, and response. The relational structure of love (always toward another) makes community the necessary formation context.
- Anchor verses: Joh 13:34, 1Pe 1:22, 1Jo 4:19
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-098 | T5.7.1**
- Tier: T5 — Formative and Developmental
- Component: T5.7 — Deposit Consequence
- Prompt: 1 — If a body deposit of this characteristic was identified at T2.8, what is the consequence of that deposit for the person?
- Disposition: PARTIALLY ANSWERED
- Status tag: P
- Notation: *Gap identified*
- Answer: T2.8 identified the heart-inscription (Pro 3:3) as a partial deposit-candidate — metaphorical but not fully confirmed as a constitutional body-deposit. If the heart-inscription is treated as a deposit: the consequence is that love becomes a stable constitutional feature of the person rather than a fluctuating state — chesed written on the heart is love that endures through circumstance. The heart-inscription consequence: the person whose heart has love inscribed acts from love habitually, not only when feeling love. This is consistent with the chasid profile (OBS-103-026): the godly person whose inner character is shaped by covenantal love. The inscription makes love a character-quality rather than a feeling-event. Gap: the full body-deposit question remains partially evidenced; this response reflects the heart-inscription's probable consequence if it is a deposit, not a fully confirmed answer.
- Anchor verses: Pro 3:3, Psa 4:3
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-099 | T5.7.2**
- Tier: T5 — Formative and Developmental
- Component: T5.7 — Deposit Consequence
- Prompt: 2 — Does the deposit produce a lasting constitutional change in the person?
- Disposition: PARTIALLY ANSWERED
- Status tag: P
- Notation: *Gap identified*
- Answer: Per the heart-inscription evidence (Pro 3:3, OBS-103-090): the inscription of love on the heart implies a lasting constitutional change — the person whose heart has chesed written into it is a different person constitutionally from the one who merely performs loving acts occasionally. The chasid (OBS-103-026) is defined as a person-type, not merely a person-doing-things — the love-character is constitutive of who they are. However, the evidence for permanent constitutional change in the biological-body sense (as distinct from the character-level) is not directly stated. The character-change appears lasting; the somatic-deposit sense remains uncertain.
- Anchor verses: Pro 3:3, Psa 4:3
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-100 | T5.7.3**
- Tier: T5 — Formative and Developmental
- Component: T5.7 — Deposit Consequence
- Prompt: 3 — If no body deposit was evidenced at T2.8, formally close this component and state N for all three prompts.
- Disposition: NOT APPLICABLE
- Status tag: N
- Rationale: T2.8 returned a partial result (heart-inscription as candidate deposit, not confirmed absent). T5.7 prompts 1 and 2 have been partially answered on that basis. This closing-N prompt does not apply since T2.8 was not a clear negative.
- Finding type: N/A


#### Tier 6 — Structural Relationships — 28 prompts

**Q&A-101 | T6.1.1**
- Tier: T6 — Structural Relationships
- Component: T6.1 — Co-occurrence
- Prompt: 1 — What other characteristics co-occur most frequently with this one in the verse evidence — and what does the pattern reveal?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: Top co-occurrences from §5 data (OBS-103-042 through OBS-103-051):
R023 compassion (196), R187 strength (105), R197 authority (69), R117 peace (68), R059 faith (62), R044 despair (55), R112 mind (52), R173 will (52), R019 calling (51), R182 Soul (50), R043 desire (49), R051 distress (49), R183 heart (47).
The pattern reveals three structural clusters: (a) **Love's relational cluster** — compassion (23), peace (117), kindness (99), mercy (111) — love co-occurs with its closest relational companions within C17, confirming cluster integrity; (b) **Love's constitutional cluster** — soul (182), heart (183), mind (112) — love is present in verses that name the inner constitutional locations; (c) **Love's theological cluster** — faith (59), calling (19), covenant (34) — love co-occurs consistently with the programme's foundational theological vocabulary. The surprise: strength (105) and authority (197) are co-occurrence #2 and #3 — love and power are structurally co-present in the data at high frequency.
- Anchor verses: Exo 34:6, Gal 5:22, Mat 22:37
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-102 | T6.1.2**
- Tier: T6 — Structural Relationships
- Component: T6.1 — Co-occurrence
- Prompt: 2 — Are any co-occurrences surprising or unexpected — and what might they reveal?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Three surprising co-occurrences: (a) **Strength (R187, 105) and authority (R197, 69)** — love and power as the second and third highest co-occurrence registers. This is analytically unexpected — strength and authority are C20 cluster characteristics, not C17. The data suggests that love and power are not merely adjacent but structurally co-present in biblical contexts. The 1Cor 13 framework places love above gifts of power ('tongues of angels, gifts of prophecy') — the comparison implies they occupy the same evidential terrain. SD-026 (already raised) addresses this. (b) **Despair (R044, 55)** — despair appearing in the top 10 co-occurrences with love. The lament/petition pattern (despair crying to love for rescue) generates this co-occurrence. Love and despair are structurally linked as the inner state that appeals to love and the love that responds to despair. (c) **Guilt (R073, 32)** — less surprising given SD-028 (forgiveness-love chain) but notable that guilt appears in the top 25 — love and guilt are structurally related at the verse level through the forgiveness-love causal chain.
- Anchor verses: 1Cor 13:1-3, Lam 3:22, Luk 7:47
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-103 | T6.1.3**
- Tier: T6 — Structural Relationships
- Component: T6.1 — Co-occurrence
- Prompt: 3 — Does the co-occurrence pattern confirm or complicate the primary dimension assignment?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Consistent with prior analysis*
- Answer: The co-occurrence pattern confirms the Relational Disposition primary dimension. Love co-occurs most densely with: compassion (the compassionate form of relational orientation), peace (the relational-outcome), faith (the trust-orientation toward God), calling (identity constituted relationally), and the soul/heart/mind (the constitutional locations of relational experience). This is the pattern expected for a Relational Disposition characteristic. The strength/authority co-occurrence adds texture (love operates in contexts of power) but does not complicate the primary classification — love remains relational disposition even when co-present with power vocabulary.
- Anchor verses: N/A (structural assessment)
- Finding type: N/A

**Q&A-104 | T6.2.1**
- Tier: T6 — Structural Relationships
- Component: T6.2 — Sequential Relationships
- Prompt: 1 — Does the verse evidence place this characteristic in sequential relationship with other inner-being characteristics — does it follow from, lead to, or require others?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: The data is unusually rich in love's sequential relationships. Love as effect (something precedes it): (a) Received divine love → human love (1Jo 4:19, OBS-103-146); (b) Forgiveness received → love expressed (Luk 7:47, via SD-020); (c) Obedience → soul purification → sincere love (1Pe 1:22, OBS-103-124); (d) Spirit infusion → love in heart (Rom 5:5, OBS-103-126). Love as cause (love produces): (e) Love of God → commandment-keeping (Joh 14:15, OBS-103-140); (f) Love → all other Spirit-fruits (Gal 5:22, OBS-103-128 — if love is generative); (g) Love of money → craving → departure from faith → anguish (1Ti 6:10, OBS-103-132 — the disordered sequence); (h) Perfect love → displacement of fear (1Jo 4:18, via SP-103-029). The sequential data reveals love as both deeply downstream of divine action and richly upstream of the ethical and moral life. Love is the programme's most central sequential node.
- Anchor verses: 1Jo 4:19, Joh 14:15, Gal 5:22, 1Ti 6:10
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-105 | T6.2.2**
- Tier: T6 — Structural Relationships
- Component: T6.2 — Sequential Relationships
- Prompt: 2 — Does this characteristic appear to occupy a particular structural position — foundational, mediating, or terminal?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Love appears to occupy a **mediating and generative** position in the programme's sequential architecture. Mediating: it stands between received divine love (prior) and the ethical-moral life (subsequent). It is not the origin (God is the origin) but it is the indispensable middle — without love, no commandment-keeping, no Spirit-fruit, no community-identity. Generative: love heads the fruit-of-Spirit list (Gal 5:22) and defines the measure of all subsequent virtues (1Cor 13:13 — 'the greatest is love'). Love functions as the programme's organising characteristic at the ethical level: it is what the other Spirit-fruits emerge from and what the commandments resolve into. This is consistent with the registry description ('most foundational word') and DIM-103-001's call to map love's governing position relative to other characteristics.
- Anchor verses: Gal 5:22, 1Cor 13:13, 1Jo 4:19, Joh 14:15
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-107 | T6.3.1**
- Tier: T6 — Structural Relationships
- Component: T6.3 — Causal and Constitutive Relationships
- Prompt: 1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic causing or constituting other inner-being states?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Yes — love is causally productive in the data at both the inner-being and the social levels: (a) **Love → joy** (Psa 16:11, OBS-103-112): love-in-God's-presence produces fullness of joy; (b) **Love → rest** (Zep 3:17, OBS-103-094): God's love produces inner quieting; (c) **Love → grief** (Song 5:6, OBS-103-062; 2Sa 1:26, OBS-103-095): love under loss produces grief — love constitutes the grief by making the beloved's absence unbearable; (d) **Love → obedience** (Joh 14:15, OBS-103-140): love of Christ produces commandment-keeping; (e) **Love → praise** (Psa 63:3, OBS-103-087): love expressed as response to chesed-above-life produces praise. Love does not merely accompany these states but appears to constitute or cause them. It is the programme's most causally productive characteristic.
- Anchor verses: Psa 16:11, Zep 3:17, Song 5:6, Joh 14:15
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-108 | T6.3.2**
- Tier: T6 — Structural Relationships
- Component: T6.3 — Causal and Constitutive Relationships
- Prompt: 2 — Is this characteristic a constituent element of another, or does another characteristic constitute part of this one?
- Disposition: PARTIALLY ANSWERED
- Status tag: P
- Notation: *Gap identified*
- Answer: From the data: (a) Love may constitute or generate all Spirit-fruits (Gal 5:22, Q&A-105) — if love is the single fruit of which joy, peace, patience, etc. are expressions, then love partially constitutes those characteristics. (b) Forgiveness may constitute the condition from which love emerges (Luk 7:47 via SD-020) — if 'she loved because she was forgiven much,' forgiveness is constitutive of the love-response. (c) Compassion and love appear to be constitutively related — compassion may be love's form under the condition of the other's suffering (OBS-103-042, OBS-103-057). Gap: the precise constitutive relationships between love and compassion, mercy, kindness cannot be fully determined from Stage 2a evidence alone — these require Session D treatment. Partial: love-as-constituent-of-Spirit-fruits and forgiveness-as-constituent-of-love-response are the best-evidenced claims.
- Anchor verses: Gal 5:22, Luk 7:47, Luk 15:20
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

The term sharing ratio (0.701 — 96 of 137 terms shared, OBS-103-006) is among the highest in the programme. Love shares vocabulary with almost every adjacent registry in C17.

**Q&A-111 | T6.4.2**
- Tier: T6 — Structural Relationships
- Component: T6.4 — Vocabulary and Root Sharing
- Prompt: 2 — Does vocabulary sharing extend to root-level architecture?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Yes — three root-level connections are analytically significant: (a) **Racham root** — spans love (103), compassion (23), and mercy (111) as a unified etymological family. The womb-compassion-love nexus (OBS-103-007, OBS-103-029) is a root-level connection — the same bodily root generates three distinct registry characteristics; (b) **Tov root** — spans love (103) and goodness (67), crossing cluster boundaries (C17 and implied goodness cluster). The goodness-as-love-expression connection (SD-009) is root-level; (c) **Ahav root** — spans love (103) and desire (43). H0157H (friend-ahev, OWNER R103) and H0157G (lover-ahev, OWNER R043 via XREF placement) are the same root, different programme assignments. Root-sharing confirms that the programme's registries are not sealed semantic units but connected through shared etymological architecture.
- Anchor verses: Isa 49:15, Psa 25:7, Hos 6:6

**Q&A-112 | T6.4.3**
- Tier: T6 — Structural Relationships
- Component: T6.4 — Vocabulary and Root Sharing
- Prompt: 3 — What does vocabulary sharing reveal about the conceptual relationship between characteristics?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Vocabulary sharing at this density reveals that love is not a bounded standalone characteristic but the semantic centre of a vocabulary cluster. The characteristics surrounding love (compassion, mercy, kindness, goodness, desire, peace) share vocabulary with it because they are all expressions or dimensions of a common inner-being reality — oriented-attachment-to-the-good-and-to-persons. The registries do not name wholly distinct phenomena; they name distinguishable aspects of a single broadly relational inner-being reality. The practical implication: Session D synthesis for love cannot treat the other C17 characteristics as merely adjacent — they are lexically and conceptually continuous with love. The distinctions drawn in the programme's registry structure are analytical tools, not natural kinds.
- Anchor verses: N/A (structural assessment)
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-113 | T6.5.1**
- Tier: T6 — Structural Relationships
- Component: T6.5 — Distinctions
- Prompt: 1 — Which adjacent characteristic most closely resembles love — and what precisely distinguishes them?
- Disposition: PARTIALLY ANSWERED
- Status tag: P
- Notation: *Gap identified*
- Answer: The closest adjacent characteristic from co-occurrence data is compassion (R023, 196 shared verses). What distinguishes them from the data: compassion is love's responsive form under the condition of the other's suffering — the rachamim/womb-movement is activated by the beloved's need or distress. Love without suffering context does not require the racham-movement; love in the presence of suffering always produces it. Stated differently: compassion is the subset of love that is suffering-triggered; love is the broader orientation of which compassion is one mode (OBS-103-029, OBS-103-042). However: the data does not fully distinguish chesed from compassion at the verse level — both can be present simultaneously (Lam 3:22). The distinction is partial. Gap: the precise boundary between love and compassion requires dedicated Session D analysis of both registries' verse corpora together.
- Anchor verses: Lam 3:22, Isa 49:15, Luk 15:20
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-114 | T6.5.2**
- Tier: T6 — Structural Relationships
- Component: T6.5 — Distinctions
- Prompt: 2 — Where the evidence shows apparent overlap, what is the precise boundary?
- Disposition: PARTIALLY ANSWERED
- Status tag: P
- Notation: *Gap identified*
- Answer: The racham/chesed overlap at Lam 3:22 ('his chesed never ceases, his rachamim never come to an end') is the programme's clearest example of the boundary difficulty — the two terms are paired in parallel without distinction. At the definitional level the boundary is: chesed = covenantal-faithful love (disposition of the covenant partner); rachamim = compassion-love (response to suffering). But at the verse level they co-occur so consistently that their experiential separation is unclear. Gap: the boundary is analytically drawn but evidentially porous. Session D is the appropriate resolution context.
- Anchor verses: Lam 3:22, Exo 34:6
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-115 | T6.5.3**
- Tier: T6 — Structural Relationships
- Component: T6.5 — Distinctions
- Prompt: 3 — Is the distinction between this characteristic and its nearest neighbour one of degree, kind, direction, or constitutional level?
- Disposition: PARTIALLY ANSWERED
- Status tag: P
- Notation: *Gap identified*
- Answer: Between love and compassion: the distinction appears to be one of **trigger** rather than degree, kind, direction, or constitutional level. Both are inner dispositions of orientation toward another (same kind, same direction, similar constitutional level). What differs is the activating condition: compassion is triggered by the other's suffering; love can be present without suffering. This makes them the same characteristic differently activated, rather than different characteristics. This reading is consistent with SD-007 (compassion as love-responding-to-suffering hierarchy). However, the data does not definitively confirm this — it is an analytical interpretation of the co-occurrence and definitional data. Deferred to Session D for resolution.
- Anchor verses: Lam 3:22, Isa 49:15
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

Gal 5:22 (shared with 5 registries) places love as the head of the Spirit-fruit list and all subsequent fruits as co-anchors. These are not random co-occurrences — they are structurally chosen: the programme anchored the most important characteristic-verses at love because love is the conceptual centre from which the adjacent characteristics derive their meaning. The shared anchor pattern confirms love's generative position (Q&A-105): love is what the surrounding characteristics are expressions of, not merely what appears alongside them.
