#### Tier 7 — Evidential and Methodological Foundation — 20 prompts

**Q&A-122 | T7.1.1**
- Tier: T7 — Evidential and Methodological Foundation
- Component: T7.1 — Lexical and Semantic Analysis
- Prompt: 1 — What are the primary Hebrew and Greek terms for this characteristic — and what do their root meanings reveal?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Consistent with prior analysis*
- Answer: Primary Hebrew terms and root meanings: **chesed** (H2617A) — root implies binding loyalty, covenant-fidelity; possibly related to the idea of steadfastness or bending toward; the most theologically laden term in the OT love vocabulary. **ahavah** (H0160) — root ahav (to breathe after, to desire) — implying love as a form of directed longing or desire. **racham** (H7355) / **rachamim** (H7356B) — root rechem (womb) — love as womb-like envelopment and tender compassion; the most somatically grounded root. **dod** (H1730G/H) — root unclear; used for lover/beloved in the Song — the erotic-relational vocabulary. Primary Greek terms: **agapē** (G0026) / **agapaō** (G0025) — of uncertain pre-classical etymology; LXX/NT coinage whose meaning is constituted by Scripture rather than importing a prior secular meaning (OBS-103-016). **phileō** (G5368) / **philia** (G5373) / **filos** (G5384) — root from philos (friend); classical Greek for natural affectionate love. Root meanings together reveal: love spans willed-covenant (chesed), longing-desire (ahavah), somatic-compassion (racham), erotic-beloved (dod), self-giving-willed (agapē), and natural-affection (phileō).
- Anchor verses: Lam 3:22, Song 2:16, Isa 49:15, 1Cor 13:4
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-123 | T7.1.2**
- Tier: T7 — Evidential and Methodological Foundation
- Component: T7.1 — Lexical and Semantic Analysis
- Prompt: 2 — What is the grammatical range of the primary term — and what does that range reveal?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: Taking agapaō/agapē as the primary NT term: **agapaō** (verb, 344 occurrences) — love as an action, exercisable and commandable; the verbal form affirms love's volitional dimension. **agapē** (noun, 133 occurrences) — love as an entity, a reality that can be 'poured into hearts' (Rom 5:5), that 'never fails' (1Cor 13:8), that is the greatest (1Cor 13:13). **agapētos** (adjective/participle, 79 occurrences) — beloved, the passive recipient of love; love as constituting an identity-state in the object. Together: verb + noun + adjective-participle spans the full grammatical range: love as act (verb), love as reality/quality (noun), and love as identity-constitutive state (adjective). This three-part grammatical range confirms Q&A-016's finding that love is simultaneously act, disposition, and condition. For chesed: primarily noun (covenant-quality) with verbal cognate (chasad — to act with chesed) — the noun-primary form confirms love as a stable quality before it is an act.
- Anchor verses: Mat 22:37, 1Cor 13:13, Rom 1:7, Rom 5:5
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-124 | T7.1.3**
- Tier: T7 — Evidential and Methodological Foundation
- Component: T7.1 — Lexical and Semantic Analysis
- Prompt: 3 — What is the semantic range of the primary term — across what breadth of meaning does it operate?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: Agapē's semantic range in the NT evidence: (a) divine love for humanity (Joh 3:16); (b) human love for God (Mat 22:37); (c) mutual love in community (Joh 13:34); (d) love of enemy (Mat 5:44); (e) disordered love (love of darkness — Joh 3:19; love of the world — 2Ti 4:10; love of the pre-eminent position — 3Jo 9). The semantic range spans divine, human-covenantal, communal, and misdirected forms. Chesed's range: divine faithfulness, human loyalty, the person-type (chasid), the failure of chesed (withdrawal, demand). The combined semantic range of the primary terms covers the full moral landscape — from the highest (God's love as his being) to the lowest (love misdirected toward darkness). This breadth is unique in the programme — no other characteristic has primary terms whose semantic range spans from the ontologically highest (divine nature) to the morally inverted (love of darkness).
- Anchor verses: Joh 3:16, Mat 5:44, Joh 3:19, Psa 63:3
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-125 | T7.1.4**
- Tier: T7 — Evidential and Methodological Foundation
- Component: T7.1 — Lexical and Semantic Analysis
- Prompt: 4 — Does the vocabulary distinguish distinct aspects: disposition versus act, received versus given, condition versus quality?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Consistent with prior analysis*
- Answer: Yes — the vocabulary structure itself distinguishes these: **Disposition vs act**: agapē (noun — disposition) vs agapaō (verb — act); chesed (noun — the quality) vs chasad (verb — to act with chesed). **Received vs given**: agapētos (passive — received) vs agapaō (active — given); 'beloved of my soul' (Jer 12:7, received by Israel) vs 'I have loved you' (Jer 31:3, given by God). **Condition vs quality**: the lover-as-identity (chasid as person-type, OBS-103-026; filos as person-type, OBS-103-018) names the quality that has become a stable condition; the act-forms name love as an exercised capacity. The vocabulary is architecturally precise — it distinguishes what love is (quality/disposition), what love does (act), who love comes from (given), who love is directed toward (received), and who love constitutes (condition/identity).
- Anchor verses: Lam 3:22, Jer 12:7, Psa 4:3, Joh 15:13
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-126 | T7.1.5**
- Tier: T7 — Evidential and Methodological Foundation
- Component: T7.1 — Lexical and Semantic Analysis
- Prompt: 5 — Does the vocabulary include a term for the structural opposite or absence of this characteristic?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: Yes — embedded as OWNER. H8130 sane (to hate, 139 active / 156 total) is the structural opposite within the registry (OBS-103-030). H8131 sena (hating, 1 active) is a second form. The hate vocabulary is not XREF but OWNER — the programme treats the structural opposite as constituent of the love vocabulary's boundary (OBS-103-019). Additionally: the philo-compound negative forms (afilarguros — not-money-loving; pseudadelfos — false-brother) name the absence of specific love-forms. The disordered love vocabulary names love's distorted presence rather than its absence. True lovelessness (absence without misdirection) is not prominently named — the data suggests the inner mechanism is always present and always directed at something; the question is always the object, not the presence or absence of love-capacity.
- Anchor verses: Lev 19:17, Psa 97:10, Pro 10:12
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-127 | T7.1.6**
- Tier: T7 — Evidential and Methodological Foundation
- Component: T7.1 — Lexical and Semantic Analysis
- Prompt: 6 — Does the vocabulary include a person-type term — a term for one who habitually possesses or exercises this characteristic?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: Yes — two primary person-type terms: (a) **H2623 chasid** (pious/godly one, 33 active) — the person-type of chesed. The chasid is defined by their inner character of covenantal love toward God (OBS-103-026). (b) **G5384 filos** (friend, 27 active) — the person-type of phileō. The filos is one whose inner orientation of loyal affection has become their defining relational identity (OBS-103-018). Additional person-type compounds: filagathos (lover of good — positive), filarguros (money-lover — negative), filotheos (God-lover), filēdonos (pleasure-lover), filautos (self-lover — via 2Ti 3:2). The philo-compound system generates person-types for each form of love (OBS-103-017). The programme has the richest person-type vocabulary in the programme for any single characteristic — the love-vocabulary directly generates who you are from what you love.
- Anchor verses: Psa 4:3, Joh 15:15, 2Ti 3:2-4
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-128 | T7.1.7**
- Tier: T7 — Evidential and Methodological Foundation
- Component: T7.1 — Lexical and Semantic Analysis
- Prompt: 7 — Does the vocabulary include a supplication or seeking term — a term for the act of seeking this characteristic from another?
- Disposition: PARTIALLY ANSWERED
- Status tag: P
- Notation: *Gap identified*
- Answer: The data contains supplication-for-love contexts but not a dedicated seeking term. Lam 3:22 (OBS-103-088): the community crying out for chesed in the midst of desolation is implicit supplication. The Psalms' consistent 'according to your chesed' (Psa 63:3, Psa 78:38) pattern is love-seeking as petition. Hos 3:5 (OBS-103-082): 'they shall come in fear to the Lord and to his goodness' — movement toward God's love/goodness as a seeking-act. However, a specific lexical term for 'seeking love' is not identified in the current data package. Gap: the seeking-term for love may exist in the broader corpus (the Psalms' petition-for-chesed formulae) but is not captured as a named group or anchor in R103's current structure.
- Anchor verses: Psa 63:3, Lam 3:22, Hos 3:5
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-129 | T7.1.8**
- Tier: T7 — Evidential and Methodological Foundation
- Component: T7.1 — Lexical and Semantic Analysis
- Prompt: 8 — What does the LXX use of the vocabulary reveal about continuity or development of this characteristic across the Testaments?
- Disposition: PARTIALLY ANSWERED
- Status tag: P
- Notation: *Gap identified*
- Answer: The key LXX observation from the data: the LXX translators used agapē/agapaō to translate both ahav and chesed, embedding the Hebrew covenantal sense of steadfast love into the Greek agapē vocabulary. This is historically significant — agapē in the NT carries the weight of the OT chesed through the LXX translation. When the NT says 'God so loved (ēgapēsen)' (Joh 3:16), it uses the term that the LXX used for God's chesed toward Israel. Continuity is established at the lexical level: the NT's agapē is not a new concept but the Hebrew chesed in Greek form. Gap: the NO_WORD_ANALYSIS flag (142 instances, OBS-103-156) limits the depth of LXX-analysis available from the data package. Full LXX lexical analysis is not possible from the current data.
- Anchor verses: Joh 3:16, Lam 3:22, Psa 63:3
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-130 | T7.1.9**
- Tier: T7 — Evidential and Methodological Foundation
- Component: T7.1 — Lexical and Semantic Analysis
- Prompt: 9 — Is there a term newly coined in the NT period for this characteristic?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Yes — agapē itself is effectively a NT-period coinage in its theological-central usage. The word exists rarely in classical Greek but carries no comparable weight; its meaning is constituted by its LXX/NT usage (OBS-103-016). The coinage-significance: the NT needed a word for love that was not pre-loaded with the Platonic eros tradition or the friendship-philia tradition — agapē fills this gap, its meaning entirely constituted by Scripture. This is analytically significant: agapē is the programme's strongest example of a characteristic whose vocabulary definition is wholly internal to the scriptural corpus. What agapē means cannot be determined by reference to classical Greek usage — it must be read from the LXX and NT contexts themselves.
- Anchor verses: Joh 3:16, 1Cor 13:4, 1Jo 4:8 (via flag)
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-131 | T7.1.10**
- Tier: T7 — Evidential and Methodological Foundation
- Component: T7.1 — Lexical and Semantic Analysis
- Prompt: 10 — What does the full vocabulary arc reveal about this characteristic's complete semantic range?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: The full vocabulary arc reveals love as the programme's most semantically comprehensive characteristic. The arc spans: (a) **Ground of being** — 1Jo 4:8 (God is love — the ontological summit); (b) **Covenantal permanence** — chesed (never ceasing, Lam 3:22); (c) **Somatic compassion** — rachamim (womb-like movement, Isa 49:15); (d) **Erotic-intense** — dod, ahavah (Song vocabulary, OBS-103-041); (e) **Natural affection** — phileō (Joh 11:36); (f) **Volitional self-giving** — agapē (enemy-love, soul-laying-down); (g) **Object-directed attachment** — philo-compounds (love of money, God, pleasure, brothers); (h) **Structural opposite** — sane (hatred). The arc is a spectrum from the ontologically highest (divine being) through the morally normative (covenantal chesed, commanded agapē) to the naturally affective (phileō, dod) to the morally disordered (love of darkness, self, money). No characteristic in the programme covers a comparable arc. Love is the vocabulary's outermost circle — encompassing the greatest range of inner-being phenomena under a single governing concept.
- Anchor verses: Song 8:6, Lam 3:22, Isa 49:15, Joh 15:13
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-132 | T7.2.1**
- Tier: T7 — Evidential and Methodological Foundation
- Component: T7.2 — Verse and Literary Interpretation
- Prompt: 1 — What is the function of the primary term within its primary verse?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: Identifying 1Jo 4:8 ('God is love') as the primary theological claim and Joh 15:13 as the primary ethical-definitional verse: In 1Jo 4:8: the predicate nominative construction ('God is love') makes love not merely an attribute of God but an identification — love as God's being. The verb 'is' (estin) establishes identity, not activity. In Joh 15:13: 'greater love has no one than this: that someone lay down his life for his friends' — love is the subject of a comparative superlative; the function is to name the outer limit of love by identifying its maximum expression (soul-giving). The primary term in both cases functions as the frame of reference against which all other love-instances are measured: Joh 15:13 defines love's maximum; 1Jo 4:8 defines love's origin. Together they establish the top and bottom of love's definitional range: what love ultimately is (God's being) and what love ultimately does (gives itself to death for the beloved).
- Anchor verses: Joh 15:13, 1Cor 13:4, Lam 3:22
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-133 | T7.2.2**
- Tier: T7 — Evidential and Methodological Foundation
- Component: T7.2 — Verse and Literary Interpretation
- Prompt: 2 — What literary form carries the primary verse evidence — and what does that form require for responsible interpretation?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: Love's evidence base spans every major literary form: (a) **Wisdom/Proverb** (Pro 10:12, 27:6): requires attention to the comparative and aphoristic structure — proverbs describe patterns, not absolutes; (b) **Psalm** (Psa 63:3, 16:11, 97:10): requires reading as first-person prayer/meditation — the psalmist's inner orientation, not universal dogma; (c) **Prophetic oracle** (Jer 31:3, Eze 16:8, Isa 49:15): the love-language is covenantal and often metaphorical (marital imagery); responsible reading holds the metaphorical dimension; (d) **Epistle** (1Cor 13, 1Jo 4, Rom 5): the most theologically discursive form — allows propositional claims about love's nature; (e) **Gospel narrative** (Joh 3:16, Luk 7:38, Joh 15:13): love embedded in narrative events requiring attention to the narrative's argument; (f) **Song/Poem** (Song of Songs): erotic love in a canonical wisdom-poem; the allegorical interpretive tradition and the literal reading must both be held. No single form dominates — love's evidence is multi-formal.
- Anchor verses: 1Cor 13:4, Song 2:16, Jer 31:3, Psa 63:3
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-134 | T7.2.3**
- Tier: T7 — Evidential and Methodological Foundation
- Component: T7.2 — Verse and Literary Interpretation
- Prompt: 3 — What is the logical structure of key arguments in the verse evidence?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Three key argument structures: (a) **Causal** — 1Jo 4:19: 'we love because (hoti) he first loved us' — divine love is the causal ground of human love. 1Cor 13:13: 'the greatest of these is love' — superlative argument establishing love's primacy. (b) **Conditional** — Joh 14:15: 'if (ean) you love me, you will keep my commandments' — love as condition for obedience. Mat 5:44: 'love your enemies (command) so that (hopōs) you may be sons of your Father' — love as condition for identity-as-child-of-God. (c) **Comparative** — Joh 15:13: 'greater love has no one than this' — superlative-comparative establishing love's maximum. Psa 63:3: 'your steadfast love is better (tov) than life' — comparative valuing love above the highest natural good. The argument structures cluster around: love as cause, love as condition, and love as the superlative good. The data argues that love is causally prior, conditionally necessary, and comparatively supreme.
- Anchor verses: 1Jo 4:19, Joh 14:15, Joh 15:13, Psa 63:3
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-135 | T7.2.4**
- Tier: T7 — Evidential and Methodological Foundation
- Component: T7.2 — Verse and Literary Interpretation
- Prompt: 4 — What contextual setting carries the primary verse evidence — and what does that setting reveal?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Adds structure*
- Answer: Three dominant contextual settings: (a) **Covenantal** — the OT love vocabulary (chesed, ahavah, racham) is carried primarily in covenantal contexts (Sinai formula, Deuteronomy love-command, prophetic covenant-marriage imagery). This reveals love as the inner disposition of covenant — it is what the covenant relationship requires and produces at the inner-being level. (b) **Communal/ecclesial** — the NT love vocabulary (agapē in Paul and John) is carried in the context of the believing community (1Cor 13 in worship-chaos context; Joh 13:34 at the Last Supper; 1Th 3:12 in community growth prayer). This reveals love as the community's constitutive practice. (c) **Lament/petition** — Lamentations, Psalms of lament: love's permanence is specifically evidenced under conditions of suffering and judgment. This reveals that love's most definitive testimony is given precisely when circumstances deny it — chesed is most powerfully stated when experience is most desolate (Lam 3:22).
- Anchor verses: Lam 3:22, Joh 13:34, 1Cor 13:4, Psa 63:3
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-136 | T7.2.5**
- Tier: T7 — Evidential and Methodological Foundation
- Component: T7.2 — Verse and Literary Interpretation
- Prompt: 5 — Does any verse function as the primary anchor for this characteristic?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Two verses function together as the primary definitional anchor for love in the data: (a) **Lam 3:22**: 'The steadfast love (chesed) of the Lord never ceases; his mercies never come to an end' — the OT's most concentrated statement of love's permanence under maximum adverse conditions. The theological claim is absolute: love does not cease. (b) **Joh 15:13**: 'Greater love has no one than this: that someone lay down his life for his friends' — the NT's primary definition of love by its maximum expression. Together they bracket the love vocabulary: Lam 3:22 defines love by its permanence (it never stops); Joh 15:13 defines love by its cost (it gives everything). If only one is chosen: Lam 3:22 is the more foundational — it states what love ultimately is (permanent, reliable, the ground of hope in desolation); Joh 15:13 states what love ultimately does.
- Anchor verses: Lam 3:22, Joh 15:13
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-137 | T7.2.6**
- Tier: T7 — Evidential and Methodological Foundation
- Component: T7.2 — Verse and Literary Interpretation
- Prompt: 6 — What does the primary anchor verse reveal that no other verse reveals?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: **Lam 3:22** reveals that love's most definitive affirmation comes in the moment of maximum absence — the desolation of Jerusalem, the silence of God, the evidence of judgment everywhere. No other verse places love's permanence claim at the precise moment when it is most empirically falsifiable. The verse does not argue for love's permanence from evidence of love's presence — it asserts permanence amid evidence of absence. This reveals that chesed in the OT is not an empirical observation (I observe that God has been loving) but a theological confession (I confess that God's love does not cease, even when it does not appear). This is love at its most epistemically demanding: the confession of love against the evidence of its apparent absence. No other verse in the data makes this claim with this evidence-structure.
- Anchor verses: Lam 3:22
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-138 | T7.3.1**
- Tier: T7 — Evidential and Methodological Foundation
- Component: T7.3 — Human Science Frameworks
- Prompt: 1 — Which human science framework is most useful as an interpretive lens for this characteristic?
- Disposition: PARTIALLY ANSWERED
- Status tag: P
- Notation: *Gap identified*
- Answer: From the data's own content, two frameworks are most relevant without importing external framework content: (a) **Attachment theory** (developmental psychology) — the data's pattern of belovedness-as-identity-constituting, soul-failing-at-beloved's-absence (Song 5:6), and love-as-primary-relational-bond maps onto attachment theory's account of how the primary bond shapes the person's inner life and identity. The biblical data precedes and exceeds attachment theory's claims. (b) **Virtue ethics** (moral philosophy) — chesed written on the heart (Pro 3:3), chasid as person-type, love-as-character-quality — the data's account of love as a stable disposition that constitutes the person maps onto virtue theory's account of character. Gap: the specific content of attachment theory and virtue ethics is not available in the data package and must not be imported. The framework names are offered as pointers for Session D; the current response names the frameworks without introducing framework-specific content.
- Anchor verses: Song 5:6, Pro 3:3, Psa 4:3
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

- Disposition: NOT ANSWERED

Gap: the illumination-by-framework question requires Session D treatment where the programme's account of love can be compared to the frameworks without the comparison being constructed from the frameworks themselves.

#### Love Extensions — 14 word-specific prompts (L-001 through L-014)

**Q&A-142 | L-001**
- Tier: Love Extensions
- Component: L-001 — Foundational position
- Prompt: Does love hold a foundational position relative to other inner-being characteristics — does it govern, generate, or organise them?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Yes — the data provides a convergent answer from multiple angles. Gal 5:22 (OBS-103-128): love heads the singular fruit-of-Spirit list; the singularity of 'fruit' (not 'fruits') implies love as the one thing of which joy, peace, patience, etc. are expressions. 1Cor 13:13: 'the greatest of these is love' — ranked above faith and hope. Mat 22:37-40: all the Law and Prophets hang on the two love commandments — love organises the entire moral law. 1Jo 4:19: all human love flows from divine love — love is the causal origin of every other love-act. The data consistently positions love not as one virtue among others but as the virtue that organises, generates, and ranks the others. DIM-103-001 is resolved by this answer: love's 'inner-being architecture' is one where love governs all other relational dispositions. Lifecycle note: DIM-103-001 resolved via Q&A-142.
- Anchor verses: Gal 5:22, 1Cor 13:13, Mat 22:37-40, 1Jo 4:19
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-143 | L-002**
- Tier: Love Extensions
- Component: L-002 — Modes simultaneous or sequential
- Prompt: Where love has distinct modes of operation, are those modes held simultaneously or do they operate sequentially?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Both patterns appear in the data. Simultaneous: Exo 34:6 (OBS-103-069) — God is simultaneously rachum AND channun AND erek-appayim AND rab-chesed AND emet — five love-modes co-present as one divine character. Lam 3:22 (OBS-103-088) — chesed AND rachamim named together. Song 5:2 (OBS-103-108) — the beloved is simultaneously sister, love, dove, perfect one — multiple love-names applied simultaneously. Sequential: 1Jo 4:19 — divine love first, then human love in response (sequential). 1Pe 1:22 — obedience → purification → sincere love (sequential formation). Rom 5:5 → Gal 5:22 — Spirit infusion → fruit production (sequential). The data does not resolve to a single pattern — love's modes cohere simultaneously in their full expression (the divine portrait) and arise sequentially in their human formation.
- Anchor verses: Exo 34:6, Lam 3:22, 1Jo 4:19, 1Pe 1:22
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-144 | L-003**
- Tier: Love Extensions
- Component: L-003 — Directionality and object determination
- Prompt: Does love have an inherent directionality — is it always oriented toward an object — and what does the choice of object determine about love's moral character?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Yes — love is always directed. The grammar confirms this: agapaō always takes a direct object; the philo-compound system is entirely object-defining (love-of-X where X determines the compound). No instance of undirected love appears in the data — love is constitutively directional (OBS-103-017, OBS-103-009). The object determines love's moral character entirely: the inner mechanism is identical whether the object is God (filotheos — morally ordered) or pleasure (filēdonos — morally disordered) or money (filarguros). This is the data's most consistently evidenced structural feature: the same inner act of attachment produces radically different moral outcomes based solely on the object. The moral life in the biblical data is substantially a question of love's direction — not whether one loves but what one loves. This confirms L-004's anticipated finding (below).
- Anchor verses: Mat 22:37, 2Ti 3:2-4, Jam 4:4, 1Jo 4:19
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-145 | L-004**
- Tier: Love Extensions
- Component: L-004 — Identity diagnostic
- Prompt: Can love function as an identity diagnostic — does what a person does with this word reveal what kind of person they are?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Yes — this is one of the data's most strongly evidenced structural claims. 2Ti 3:2-4 (OBS-103-137) lists philautos (self-lover) and philēdonos (pleasure-lover) vs filotheos (God-lover) as the diagnostic markers distinguishing the last-days person from the faithful person. Joh 3:19 (OBS-103-147): 'people loved the darkness' — the love-choice is the diagnostic of judgment. Joh 13:35 (OBS-103-129): 'by this all will know that you are my disciples, if you have love for one another' — the community's love-practice is the external diagnostic of their identity. Mat 10:37 (OBS-103-151): whoever loves father or mother more than Christ 'is not worthy of me' — the hierarchy of love is the diagnostic of worthiness. What a person loves is not merely a preference — it is a revelation of what they are. The love-diagnostic is both internal (self-knowledge) and external (publicly legible community identity).
- Anchor verses: 2Ti 3:2-4, Joh 13:35, Joh 3:19, Mat 10:37
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-146 | L-005**
- Tier: Love Extensions
- Component: L-005 — Below conscious attention
- Prompt: Does love operate at a level below conscious attention or deliberate will — and if so, what does this imply about its depth in the inner being?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Yes — the data provides evidence of love operating below the threshold of deliberate conscious attention. Song 5:2 (OBS-103-108): 'I slept, but my heart was awake' — love-awareness persists in sleep, below waking consciousness. 1Ki 3:26 (OBS-103-105): the mother's rachamim for her son is described as physiological movement (nichmeruh — heated, turbulent) — an involuntary somatic response. Jer 31:20 (OBS-103-117): God's inner parts 'hamu' (murmur, are agitated) for Ephraim — the movement of the inner organs is described as spontaneous, not deliberate. The compassion-movement (splanchnizō, Luk 15:20) triggers before deliberate action (running, embracing). These instances suggest love has a pre-reflective dimension — an inner orienting toward the beloved that is already present before the person consciously engages it. Implication: love is not fully within the person's deliberate control at its deepest level; it is constitutive of the inner person at a depth below ordinary conscious access.
- Anchor verses: Song 5:2, 1Ki 3:26, Jer 31:20, Luk 15:20
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-147 | L-006**
- Tier: Love Extensions
- Component: L-006 — Taxonomy of misdirected forms
- Prompt: Does the vocabulary of love include a systematic taxonomy of its own misdirected forms — and if so, what structural logic organises that taxonomy?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Yes — the philo-compound disordered forms constitute a taxonomy (OBS-103-036, OBS-103-017): filarguria/filarguros (love of money — 3 groups), filēdonos (love of pleasure), filoneikia/filoneikos (love of dispute), filoprōteuō (love of being first), filia tou kosmou (friendship with world — Jam 4:4), agapaō-darkness/world (Joh 3:19, 2Ti 4:10), agavah (lust — H5691), filautos (love of self — 2Ti 3:2). The structural logic organising the taxonomy: all disordered loves are the same inner mechanism (directed attachment) applied to one of three wrong object-classes: (a) **Material objects** — money, pleasure; (b) **Social-positional objects** — primacy, dispute-victory; (c) **The self** — self-love, friendship with the world as self-assertion. The taxonomy is not arbitrary — it maps the full range of objects that compete with God and the neighbour as the proper objects of love. The disordered loves are a systematic counter-ordering of the inner person's relational architecture.
- Anchor verses: 1Ti 6:10, 2Ti 3:2-4, Jam 4:4, Joh 3:19
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-148 | L-007**
- Tier: Love Extensions
- Component: L-007 — Growth
- Prompt: Can love increase or grow in the inner being — and if so, by what means?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Consistent with prior analysis*
- Answer: Already addressed at T5.1 (Q&A-091) and T5.1.2 (Q&A-092). Yes — 1Th 3:12 ('may the Lord make you increase and abound in love'); Rut 3:10 (this chesed greater than the first). Means: divine action (Lord makes it increase), Spirit's work (Gal 5:22), training (Tit 2:4), obedience-pathway (1Pe 1:22). No additional findings beyond Q&A-091 and Q&A-092.
- Anchor verses: 1Th 3:12, Rut 3:10, 1Pe 1:22
- Finding type: N/A

**Q&A-149 | L-008**
- Tier: Love Extensions
- Component: L-008 — Definitive outward expression
- Prompt: Does love have a definitive outward expression — a form that constitutes what love is rather than merely evidencing it?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Yes — the data names two constitutive outward expressions: (a) **Self-giving** — Joh 15:13 (OBS-103-125): 'greater love has no one than this: to lay down one's life for one's friends.' The self-giving is not the evidence of love — it is love's maximum constitutive form. The act constitutes the love at its greatest — without the self-giving there is no greater love, only a lesser form. (b) **Obedience** — Joh 14:15: 'if you love me, you will keep my commandments.' Commandment-keeping is not merely love's fruit — it is love's definitive form toward Christ. The absence of commandment-keeping in the professed lover of Christ constitutes a question about whether the love is genuine. The kiss (filēma, katafileō) is also a constitutive rather than merely evidential act — the Judas-kiss (Luk 22:48) is dangerous precisely because it uses love's constitutive act to signal the opposite.
- Anchor verses: Joh 15:13, Joh 14:15, Luk 22:48
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-150 | L-009**
- Tier: Love Extensions
- Component: L-009 — Constitutive of divine essence
- Prompt: Is love named in Scripture as constitutive of the divine essence — what God is — rather than merely as a divine attribute or act?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Yes — explicitly in 1Jo 4:8 ('God is love — ho theos agapē estin') and 1Jo 4:16 ('God is love'). The predicate nominative construction in Greek (theos agapē) makes love not a description of what God does but an identification of what God is. This is the programme's most significant theological claim: love is not one of God's attributes among others but the identification of God's being. The data also evidences this from the OT side: Song 8:6 (OBS-103-096) names love's flame as 'the very flame of the Lord' (shalhevetyah) — love's intensity is grounded in the divine name. Exo 34:6 (OBS-103-069) names love/chesed as the first and most prominent of God's proclaimed attributes. The NT claim (God is love) has OT preparation in the priority of chesed in the divine self-characterisation.
- Anchor verses: Song 8:6, Exo 34:6
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-151 | L-010**
- Tier: Love Extensions
- Component: L-010 — Structural opposite under same moral logic
- Prompt: Does love's structural opposite operate under the same moral logic as love itself — can hatred also be rightly or wrongly directed?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Yes — and the data makes this explicit. Psa 97:10 (OBS-103-115): 'O you who love the Lord, hate evil' — hatred of evil is commanded of those who love God. Righteous hatred is not love's failure but love's necessary complement: you cannot love God and be indifferent to what opposes him. Lev 19:17 (OBS-103-114): 'you shall not hate your brother in your heart' — hatred of the brother is wrong. The same inner-being mechanism (hatred as directed-aversion) can be rightly directed (at evil) or wrongly directed (at the brother). This is the precise structural parallel to love: love rightly directed (toward God and neighbour) vs love wrongly directed (toward money, pleasure, world). Hatred operates under the same moral logic as love: the mechanism is morally neutral; the object determines the moral quality. The ordered inner life requires both rightly directed love AND rightly directed hatred.
- Anchor verses: Psa 97:10, Lev 19:17, Pro 10:12
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-152 | L-011**
- Tier: Love Extensions
- Component: L-011 — Disposition versus act
- Prompt: What is the relationship between love as inner disposition and love as outward act — are they competitors, co-expressions, or in a different structural relationship?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: The data positions them in a **generative relationship** — disposition generates act. The chesed that is written on the heart (Pro 3:3, OBS-103-090) is the disposition that produces the acts of Ruth's chesed (Rut 3:10, OBS-103-089) and the acts of social kindness in the neighbour-relationships. Love of Christ as inner disposition produces commandment-keeping as outward act (Joh 14:15, OBS-103-140). The compassion-movement (inner) produces running, embracing, kissing (outer) in Luk 15:20 (OBS-103-057). The relationship is not competitive (as if outer act were less genuine than inner disposition) nor merely co-present (as if they were unrelated). Disposition and act are related as inner origin and outer expression — the act is the disposition's actualisation in a specific relational moment. 1Ki 8:18 (OBS-103-103) confirms: God accepts the inner disposition (it was in your heart) even when the act is not performed — the disposition has value prior to and independent of the act. But the disposition that never produces an act is not evidenced as genuine love in the data — love without expression is not thematised as sufficient.
- Anchor verses: Pro 3:3, Joh 14:15, Luk 15:20, 1Ki 8:18
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-153 | L-012**
- Tier: Love Extensions
- Component: L-012 — Epistemic dimension
- Prompt: Does love carry an epistemic dimension — is knowing and being known a structural component of love's operation?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Yes — the epistemic dimension of love is one of the data's most distinctive findings. Joh 15:15 (OBS-103-052): love's definitive act is knowledge-disclosure — Jesus names the friends as those to whom he has made known all that he heard from the Father. The friend-love relationship is constituted by mutual knowledge-sharing. Hos 6:6 (OBS-103-091): 'knowledge of God' (da'at elohim) co-prioritised with chesed — love and knowing are structural companions in the OT. Jer 31:34 (OBS-103-072): in the new covenant, each person will know God directly — the eschatological love-community is one of immediate knowledge. Joh 21:17 (OBS-103-153): Peter's love-confession appeals to Christ's omniscience ('Lord, you know everything; you know that I love you') — being known by Christ is the ground of the love-confession. The epistemic dimension: love is the relational structure within which knowing becomes possible; knowledge is what love shares; being known is the most intimate expression of being loved.
- Anchor verses: Joh 15:15, Hos 6:6, Jer 31:34, Joh 21:17
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

**Q&A-154 | L-013**
- Tier: Love Extensions
- Component: L-013 — Publicly legible signal
- Prompt: Does love function as a publicly legible signal — a means by which something about the inner community or person is read by those outside?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *Consistent with prior analysis*
- Answer: Already addressed at T4.5.2 (Q&A-088) and multiple points. Yes — Joh 13:35 ('by this all people will know') is the primary evidence. The community's mutual love is publicly legible to 'all people' (pantas) — it functions as the community's primary external sign. The individual's love-choices (what they love) also function publicly as identity diagnostics (2Ti 3:2-4 list is observable; the Pharisees' money-love was observable — Luk 16:14). Love is both internally real (inner disposition) and externally readable (community sign and individual identity marker). No additional findings beyond prior Q&A responses.
- Anchor verses: Joh 13:35, Luk 16:14
- Finding type: N/A

**Q&A-155 | L-014**
- Tier: Love Extensions
- Component: L-014 — Social reorganisation
- Prompt: Does love produce a reorganisation of social dynamics — and if so, in what direction does it reorganise them?
- Disposition: ANSWERED
- Status tag: A
- Notation: *New finding*
- Answer: Yes — and the data names the direction explicitly. The reorganisation operates in three directions: (a) **Restructuring of kinship** — Mat 12:50 (OBS-103-063): the family is restructured around shared orientation toward God rather than natural kinship. Love's community replaces the natural family as the primary social unit. (b) **Inversion of competitive hierarchy** — Rom 12:10 (OBS-103-119): 'outdo one another in showing honor' — the social competition is reversed from honour-claiming to honour-giving. Love reorganises from rivalry to generosity. (c) **Inclusion of the excluded** — Mat 5:44 (OBS-103-143): enemy-love includes those whom natural social dynamics exclude. The direction of love's social reorganisation is consistently: from exclusion toward inclusion, from taking toward giving, from natural kinship toward chosen community. The community constituted by love (Joh 13:35) is a social body organised on principles that invert the natural social order.
- Anchor verses: Mat 12:50, Rom 12:10, Mat 5:44, Joh 13:35
- Finding type: THEOLOGICAL_NOTE

## Stage 2c — Synthesis Entries

**Stage 2c commenced: 2026-04-30**
**Entries required:** 7 intra-tier (T1–T7 each) + 21 inter-tier (unique pairs T1–T7) = 28 total
**Format per entry:** SYN marker | Outcome (D/F/N) | Prose | Source Q&A field
**T0 excluded from Stage 2c — held for Session D**

---

### Intra-Tier Synthesis Entries

**SYN-INTRA-103-001 | T1 — Definition intra-tier**
- Outcome: D — Described
- Synthesis: Love's definition resolves to a structured family of inner-being orientations sharing one mechanism — directed attachment toward an object — whose moral character is entirely determined by the object chosen. Within this shared mechanism, the vocabulary distinguishes three structural registers: love as disposition (the stable inner orientation — chesed, agapē as character), love as act (the commanded and exercised expression — agapaō, enemy-love), and love as condition (the identity-constituting state of being-loved — agapētos). These are not three separate loves but three aspects of love's single operation: the person has a deep stable orientation (disposition), exercises it in specific acts (act), and exists within the love-relationship as constituted by it (condition). The vocabulary arc runs from the ontologically highest (God is love — 1Jo 4:8) through the morally normative (chesed, commanded agapē) to the affective-natural (phileō, dod) to the morally inverted (love of darkness, love of self). No other characteristic in the programme commands a comparable vocabulary range. The definition's boundary with adjacent characteristics (compassion, mercy, kindness) is partially drawn: love is the broader orientation; compassion is love's suffering-triggered mode; mercy and kindness are love's formal relational expressions. The boundaries require Session D precision.
- Source Q&A: Q&A-013, Q&A-014, Q&A-016, Q&A-018, Q&A-019, Q&A-021, Q&A-022, Q&A-024, Q&A-033, Q&A-036

**SYN-INTRA-103-002 | T2 — Constitutional Location intra-tier**
- Outcome: D — Described
- Synthesis: Love is the programme's most constitutionally comprehensive characteristic — it occupies all five constitutional levels simultaneously: spirit-sourced (implied via Spirit-as-agent, Rom 5:5, Gal 5:22), soul-located (Song 5:6 — soul failing at beloved's absence; Mat 22:37 — love with all your soul; Joh 15:13 — laying down the soul), heart-inscribed (Pro 3:3; Rom 5:5 infused into hearts), mind-engaged (Mat 22:37 — love with all your mind; Joh 15:15 — love as knowledge-sharing), and body-expressed (kiss, embrace, tears, womb-movement across multiple groups). The constitutional movement pattern is consistently downward: Spirit origin → heart reception → soul experience → body expression. Love's heart-inscription (Pro 3:3) is the closest evidence to a constitutional deposit — the metaphorical writing of chesed into the heart's deepest register produces a lasting dispositional quality (the chasid person-type). The primary finding: love is not confined to any single constitutional level but operates across all levels in an integrated movement from deepest to most outward. This comprehensive constitutional architecture is consistent with love's function as the programme's organising characteristic.
- Source Q&A: Q&A-037, Q&A-041, Q&A-042, Q&A-044, Q&A-045, Q&A-047, Q&A-051, Q&A-055, Q&A-056, Q&A-057

**SYN-INTRA-103-003 | T3 — Inner Faculties intra-tier**
- Outcome: D — Described
- Synthesis: Love engages all eleven inner faculties, but five show the richest engagement: (1) Identity and self-understanding — love is the primary faculty through which the person knows who they are: being-loved (agapētos) constitutes identity from the outside; what-one-loves constitutes identity from the inside. The person is doubly defined by love. (2) Relational capacity — love is the faculty's active content: it builds (Joh 13:34), sustains (Lam 3:22), and restores (Luk 15:20) relational capacity. (3) Memory — love's sustaining faculty: love without memory cannot maintain itself through absence (Jer 31:20 — 'I do remember him still'). (4) Moral sensitivity — love calibrates what the inner person registers as morally significant; the love-of-God requirement generates the hate-evil requirement (Psa 97:10). (5) Attention — love determines what the person perceives as worth attending to (Phili 4:8 — think on what is lovely). The weaker engagements: creativity (indirect, evidenced through Song-form) and conscience (inferred, not directly named). Overall: love is the faculty-most-engaged characteristic in the programme, operating through perception, reason, memory, imagination, desire, emotion, moral sensitivity, conscience (indirectly), identity, and relational capacity simultaneously.
- Source Q&A: Q&A-066, Q&A-067, Q&A-068, Q&A-069, Q&A-072, Q&A-073, Q&A-074, Q&A-075, Q&A-076

**SYN-INTRA-103-004 | T4 — Relational Interfaces intra-tier**
- Outcome: D — Described
- Synthesis: Love's relational architecture is structured by three directional axes — GOD → HUMAN, HUMAN → GOD, HUMAN → HUMAN — with divine love structurally prior and causally generative of all subsequent love. 1Jo 4:19 ('we love because he first loved us') is the axis-precedence statement: the first axis is not responsive to but constitutive of the second and third. The GOD → HUMAN direction moves through four mechanisms: covenantal declaration (naming the beloved — Jer 12:7, Mat 3:17), Spirit-infusion (Rom 5:5), redemptive acts (Joh 3:16), and covenantal covering (Eze 16:8). The HUMAN → GOD direction requires total inner mobilisation (Mat 22:37 — all heart, soul, mind) and the clearing of rival loves as its condition (1Jo 4:19, 1Ti 6:10). The HUMAN → HUMAN direction spans five structural types (neighbour, enemy, community, friendship, family) and creates the social architecture described in Q&A-088 (restructured kinship, public legibility, competitive generosity). The most significant finding in T4: the human-to-God direction is conditioned by prior reception of divine love — the capacity for human love toward God is itself a gift. The one structural gap: T4.6 (spiritual beings) is absent from the evidence.
- Source Q&A: Q&A-077, Q&A-078, Q&A-079, Q&A-080, Q&A-081, Q&A-082, Q&A-083, Q&A-084, Q&A-085, Q&A-087, Q&A-088, Q&A-089

**SYN-INTRA-103-005 | T5 — Formative and Developmental intra-tier**
- Outcome: D — Described
- Synthesis: Love's formation operates through a multi-layered process in the data. The primary pathway is receptive: divine love received (1Jo 4:19) → Spirit infusion (Rom 5:5, Gal 5:22) → heart-reception → soul-response → community expression. Secondary pathways: obedience → soul purification → sincere love (1Pe 1:22); forgiveness received → love generated (Luk 7:47 — via SD-020); training within community (Tit 2:4). Love can grow (1Th 3:12) and increase through the Lord's action. Its reversibility is asymmetric: divine love is irreversible by nature (Jer 31:3 — everlasting; Lam 3:22 — never ceasing); human love is subject to redirection through competing love-allegiances (2Ti 4:10 — Demas). The eschatological trajectory is toward perfection and direct knowledge: partial now (mediated by community, neighbour-teaching), moving toward fullness (perfect love casting out fear — 1Jo 4:18; direct divine knowledge — Jer 31:34; pleasures forevermore — Psa 16:11). Formation requires community — love cannot be formed in isolation; it requires both the divine giver and the human community as the formation context.
- Source Q&A: Q&A-091, Q&A-092, Q&A-093, Q&A-094, Q&A-095, Q&A-096, Q&A-097, Q&A-098, Q&A-099

**SYN-INTRA-103-006 | T6 — Structural Relationships intra-tier**
- Outcome: D — Described
- Synthesis: Love's structural position in the programme is that of the central node in the inner-being vocabulary's relational architecture. Co-occurrence data: 196 with compassion, 105 with strength, 68 with peace, 62 with faith — confirming love's connections to the full range of C17 characteristics and extending to C20 (strength/authority). Shared anchor data: 48 verses shared across multiple registries, with Exo 34:6 (5 registries) and Gal 5:22 (5 registries) as the highest-density shared anchors — confirming love as the vocabulary cluster around which the programme's most significant cross-registry verses gather. Sequential position: love stands downstream of divine action (received) and upstream of the ethical-moral life (generative of commandment-keeping, Spirit-fruits, community identity). Causal productivity: love generates joy, rest, grief, obedience, praise — the programme's most causally productive characteristic. Vocabulary sharing: term sharing ratio 0.701, the highest in C17 — love shares vocabulary with compassion, mercy, kindness, goodness, desire, and peace. The primary gap: distinctions from adjacent characteristics (compassion, mercy, kindness) remain partially drawn; Session D is the resolution context.
- Source Q&A: Q&A-101, Q&A-102, Q&A-104, Q&A-105, Q&A-107, Q&A-108, Q&A-110, Q&A-111, Q&A-112, Q&A-116, Q&A-117

**SYN-INTRA-103-007 | T7 — Evidential Foundation intra-tier**
- Outcome: D — Described
- Synthesis: Love's evidential foundation is the most comprehensive in the programme. The primary terms (chesed, agapē/agapaō, racham/rachamim, ahavah, dod, phileō) cover the full constitutional range: willed-covenantal (chesed), Spirit-produced self-giving (agapē), somatic-compassionate (racham), intense-erotic (ahavah/dod), and naturally affective (phileō). The vocabulary structure itself distinguishes disposition/act/condition, received/given, and quality/person-type — making it architecturally precise. The semantic range of the primary terms spans from divine ontology (God is love) to moral inversion (love of darkness) — the widest semantic arc in the programme. The primary anchor is Lam 3:22 — love's most definitive affirmation precisely at the moment of maximum empirical falsification: a theological confession rather than an empirical observation. The LXX connection is partially evidenced (agapē as chesed-translated); full LXX analysis is limited by NO_WORD_ANALYSIS flags. The human science frameworks identified (attachment theory, virtue ethics) are named as Session D pointers but not elaborated — the instruction prohibits importing framework content not grounded in the data.
- Source Q&A: Q&A-122, Q&A-123, Q&A-124, Q&A-125, Q&A-126, Q&A-127, Q&A-130, Q&A-131, Q&A-132, Q&A-134, Q&A-136, Q&A-137


---

### Inter-Tier Synthesis Entries

**SYN-INTER-103-001 | T1 × T2 — Definition and Constitutional Location**
- Outcome: D — Described
- Synthesis: Love's definition and its constitutional location are mutually illuminating. The definition identifies love as disposition + act + condition operating through directed attachment toward an object. The constitutional mapping shows where this triple operation is located: the disposition is heart-inscribed (Pro 3:3) and spirit-sourced (implied via Rom 5:5), stable across constitutional levels; the act is will-engaged (Mat 22:37 — commanded) and soul-mobilised (Joh 15:13 — soul laid down); the condition of being-loved is received at the heart level (Rom 5:5 — poured in) and experienced at the soul level (Zep 3:17 — quieting). The constitutional movement pattern (Spirit → heart → soul → body) maps directly onto the definition's three registers: the deepest dispositional origin (spirit/heart) grounds the stable orientation; the soul-level is where love is experienced as feeling; the body-level is where act and condition become visible. Together: the constitutional location analysis confirms that love's definition is not a surface account but a constitutional claim — love operates at every depth of the inner person, which is precisely what the 'whole heart, soul, and mind' commandment (Mat 22:37) requires.
- Source Q&A: Q&A-016, Q&A-018, Q&A-044, Q&A-055, Q&A-056, Q&A-057

**SYN-INTER-103-002 | T1 × T3 — Definition and Inner Faculties**
- Outcome: D — Described
- Synthesis: Love's definition as directed-attachment-toward-an-object generates a characteristic pattern of faculty engagement. Because love is always toward an object, it necessarily engages attention (what is attended to is the beloved — Phili 4:8), reason (judgment of the object's worth and the hierarchy of competing loves — Mat 10:37), memory (remembering the beloved sustains love — Jer 31:20), and identity (what is loved constitutes who one is — Q&A-075). The definition's object-determination principle (moral quality determined by object) maps onto the moral sensitivity faculty: the faculty that calibrates moral perception is calibrated by love's direction — you notice what you love, and what you love as most important determines what you register as morally significant (Psa 97:10 — love-of-God generates hate-of-evil). The definition's tripartite structure (disposition/act/condition) maps onto the faculty architecture: disposition engages the will and conscience; act engages the relational capacity and body; condition engages identity and emotion. No faculty operates independently of love's fundamental structure.
- Source Q&A: Q&A-016, Q&A-066, Q&A-067, Q&A-068, Q&A-073, Q&A-075, Q&A-144

**SYN-INTER-103-003 | T1 × T4 — Definition and Relational Interfaces**
- Outcome: D — Described
- Synthesis: Love's definition as directed attachment reaches its relational specification in T4's three-axis architecture. The object-determination principle (Q&A-144) — that love's moral quality depends entirely on its object — is enacted relationally when the proper objects are named: God (vertical-ascending), neighbour and enemy (horizontal), and the beloved community (horizontal-mutual). The definition's three registers map onto the relational axes: the dispositional register (stable inner orientation) grounds the covenantal-faithful love in the GOD→HUMAN axis (God's chesed never ceasing — Lam 3:22); the active register (commanded, exercised) grounds the love of neighbour and enemy (Lev 19:18, Mat 5:44); the condition register (being-loved as identity) is the GOD→HUMAN axis's effect in the person (agapētos — constituted as beloved). The relational interfaces reveal what the definition describes abstractly: love's mechanism in concrete directional operation. The most significant inter-tier finding: the definition's requirement that love be directed toward an object is fulfilled eschatologically when the object is perfectly and permanently God — Jer 31:34, 1Jo 4:18 (perfect love).
- Source Q&A: Q&A-014, Q&A-016, Q&A-077, Q&A-080, Q&A-083, Q&A-087, Q&A-144

**SYN-INTER-103-004 | T1 × T5 — Definition and Formative Developmental**
- Outcome: D — Described
- Synthesis: Love's definition as disposition + act + condition maps onto the developmental sequence in T5. Condition (being-loved) comes first in the sequence — 1Jo 4:19 ('he first loved us') — the person is constituted as beloved before they can love in return. Disposition (stable inner orientation) is formed through the Spirit's infusion (Rom 5:5), obedience-pathway (1Pe 1:22), and training (Tit 2:4) — the formation process produces the stable dispositional form. Act (exercised love) is the formation process's outcome — the person who has been loved, whose disposition has been formed, exercises love toward God, neighbour, and enemy. The reversibility asymmetry (divine love irreversible; human love subject to redirection — Q&A-094) maps onto the definition's three registers: the condition of being-divinely-loved is irreversible (God does not withdraw the beloved-status once conferred — Jer 31:3); the human disposition is subject to redirection through competing loves; the human love-acts can fail without invalidating the conditional ground. The eschatological trajectory (toward perfect love — 1Jo 4:18) describes the movement toward the definition's fullest form: stable disposition + unconstrained act + permanent condition of perfect love.
- Source Q&A: Q&A-016, Q&A-091, Q&A-094, Q&A-095, Q&A-096

**SYN-INTER-103-005 | T1 × T6 — Definition and Structural Relationships**
- Outcome: D — Described
- Synthesis: Love's definition as the programme's most semantically comprehensive inner-being characteristic is confirmed and deepened by the structural relationship analysis. The term sharing ratio (0.701 — highest in C17) and the co-occurrence breadth (196 with compassion through to 29 with mercy) reflect the definition's conclusion: love is not a bounded standalone characteristic but the semantic centre of a cluster. The sequential finding (love as mediating-and-generative node — Q&A-105) maps onto the definition's tripartite structure: love is downstream (condition-received from God), central (disposition that organises), and upstream (act that generates all subsequent ethical life). The definition's vocabulary arc (from divine being to love of darkness — Q&A-131) is confirmed by the structural relationship data: the vocabulary extends into every adjacent registry (through XREF sharing, co-occurrence, and shared anchors), touching every corner of the programme. The structural analysis thus confirms the definitional claim: love is not merely a characteristic among others but the organising principle of the inner-being vocabulary.
- Source Q&A: Q&A-016, Q&A-101, Q&A-104, Q&A-105, Q&A-110, Q&A-117, Q&A-131

**SYN-INTER-103-006 | T1 × T7 — Definition and Evidential Foundation**
- Outcome: D — Described
- Synthesis: The evidential foundation confirms and specifies the definition at every point. The vocabulary analysis confirms the four-mode structure of the definition (Q&A-122, Q&A-123): chesed (covenantal-dispositional), racham (somatic-compassionate), ahavah/dod (intense-erotic), phileō/agapē (affective-natural and willed-unconditional). The grammatical range analysis confirms the tripartite definition (Q&A-123): verb (act) + noun (disposition) + adjective-passive (condition). The semantic range analysis confirms the vocabulary arc (Q&A-124, Q&A-131). The primary anchor (Lam 3:22 — Q&A-136, Q&A-137) confirms the definition's most counterintuitive feature: love at its most definitional is not evidenced by love's presence but confessed against its apparent absence. The definition says love is permanent, unwavering, faithful — and the evidential ground for this claim is a verse written in the context of Jerusalem's destruction. The evidential foundation is thus not primarily experiential but confessional — the definition's permanence-claim is a theological assertion, grounded in the character of God rather than in the consistency of human experience.
- Source Q&A: Q&A-016, Q&A-122, Q&A-123, Q&A-124, Q&A-130, Q&A-131, Q&A-136, Q&A-137


**SYN-INTER-103-007 | T2 × T3 — Constitutional Location and Inner Faculties**
- Outcome: D — Described
- Synthesis: Love's constitutional architecture and its faculty engagement are structurally aligned. The heart's engagement with love (Q&A-044, Q&A-045) corresponds to the heart's known integrating function across the programme: the heart is the location of knowing (Joh 15:15 — knowledge-disclosure as love's act), willing (Mat 22:37 — love commanded), feeling (Song 5:2 — heart awake in love-awareness), and moral awareness (Pro 3:3 — chesed inscribed). Each of the heart's functions corresponds to a faculty: knowing → reason and memory; willing → will; feeling → emotion; moral awareness → moral sensitivity. The soul-level constitutional location (Song 5:6 — soul failing at beloved's absence) corresponds to the identity and relational capacity faculties: the soul whose vitality is partly constituted by the love-object is the soul whose identity (T3.10) and relational capacity (T3.11) are most deeply invested in love. The Spirit-sourced origin of love (implied) corresponds to the deep pre-reflective faculty level (L-005 — love below conscious attention): the Spirit's infusion produces love at a depth below ordinary faculty-awareness. Constitutional depth and faculty depth are directly correlated.
- Source Q&A: Q&A-041, Q&A-044, Q&A-045, Q&A-055, Q&A-057, Q&A-075, Q&A-076

**SYN-INTER-103-008 | T2 × T4 — Constitutional Location and Relational Interfaces**
- Outcome: D — Described
- Synthesis: The constitutional location data and the relational interface data converge on the same structural claim: love's inner depth is its relational reach. The deeper love is constitutionally (heart-inscribed, soul-constitutive, Spirit-sourced), the further its relational reach — from neighbour-love (soul-level reciprocal) to enemy-love (will-level against grain) to divine love (Spirit-level transcendent). The constitutional movement pattern (Spirit → heart → soul → body — Q&A-056) maps onto the relational directional pattern: divine love enters at the deepest constitutional level (Spirit, heart) and produces relational acts at the outermost level (community legibility, bodily expression). The GOD→HUMAN axis operates at the constitutional depth where love is received (heart-infusion — Rom 5:5); the HUMAN→GOD axis requires total constitutional mobilisation (Mat 22:37 — all heart, soul, mind); the HUMAN→HUMAN axis is the outward bodily expression of the internal constitutional reality. Constitutional and relational are thus not two separate dimensions of love but the inside and outside of the same movement.
- Source Q&A: Q&A-041, Q&A-055, Q&A-056, Q&A-077, Q&A-079, Q&A-080, Q&A-087

**SYN-INTER-103-009 | T2 × T5 — Constitutional Location and Formative Developmental**
- Outcome: D — Described
- Synthesis: The formation process in T5 works precisely through the constitutional locations identified in T2. Spirit infusion (Rom 5:5) enters at the deepest level (Spirit → heart), establishing love's constitutional ground. Obedience-pathway purifies the soul (1Pe 1:22) — the soul-level constitutional location is the target of formation's clearing work. Training in the community (Tit 2:4) operates at the body-habit level — forming love through repeated communal acts that imprint the body's relational patterns. The heart-inscription of chesed (Pro 3:3) is the formation's goal-state: love sufficiently formed that it is constitutionally inscribed, no longer needing to be generated afresh for each act. The eschatological trajectory (perfect love, direct knowledge, pleasures forevermore) describes the perfection of the constitutional architecture: all levels operating without obstruction, permanently, toward the proper object. Constitutional location is thus not a static description but a dynamic formation target: each level can be more or less formed in love, and the formation process addresses each level in sequence.
- Source Q&A: Q&A-044, Q&A-056, Q&A-091, Q&A-095, Q&A-096

**SYN-INTER-103-010 | T2 × T6 — Constitutional Location and Structural Relationships**
- Outcome: D — Described
- Synthesis: Love's comprehensive constitutional location (all five levels) is structurally consistent with its position as the programme's central co-occurrence node. A characteristic that operates at every constitutional level will co-occur with the broadest range of other characteristics — because any verse that names soul, heart, mind, spirit, or body is potentially within love's evidential terrain. The co-occurrence breadth (top 25 covering registries from C17 through C20 and beyond) reflects the constitutional breadth: strength and authority (C20) co-occur with love because the same verses that address God's inner character include both love and power vocabulary — the divine portrait (Exo 34:6) is constitutionally comprehensive. The vocabulary sharing ratio (0.701 — highest in C17) similarly reflects the constitutional comprehensiveness: love shares vocabulary with compassion (at the somatic/racham level), with goodness (at the heart/tov level), with desire (at the ahav/phileō root level), with peace (at the soul-rest level). Constitutional breadth and vocabulary breadth are the same phenomenon viewed from different angles.
- Source Q&A: Q&A-055, Q&A-101, Q&A-102, Q&A-110, Q&A-111

**SYN-INTER-103-011 | T2 × T7 — Constitutional Location and Evidential Foundation**
- Outcome: D — Described
- Synthesis: The evidential foundation supports and grounds the constitutional location claims. Each constitutional level identified in T2 has specific vocabulary evidence in T7: Spirit-level origin — Gal 5:22 (fruit of the Spirit), Rom 5:5 (poured into hearts through the Spirit); soul-level — Song 5:6 (soul failing), Mat 22:37 (all your soul), Joh 15:13 (lay down the soul); heart-level — Pro 3:3 (heart inscription), Rom 5:5 (into our hearts); mind-level — Mat 22:37 (all your mind), Joh 15:15 (knowledge disclosure); body-level — kiss/embrace/tears/inner-organ-movement vocabulary across multiple groups. The lexical range of the primary terms (Q&A-122 — chesed, racham, agapē, dod, phileō) corresponds precisely to the five constitutional levels: each term carries a different constitutional register as its primary habitat. The evidential foundation thus not only confirms the constitutional claims but shows them to be lexically grounded in the vocabulary's own structure.
- Source Q&A: Q&A-041, Q&A-044, Q&A-047, Q&A-051, Q&A-055, Q&A-122, Q&A-123


**SYN-INTER-103-012 | T3 × T4 — Inner Faculties and Relational Interfaces**
- Outcome: D — Described
- Synthesis: The faculty engagement pattern in T3 is produced by and oriented toward the relational interfaces in T4. Love's identity-faculty (T3.10) is constituted through the relational interface: being-loved by God (GOD→HUMAN axis) establishes the identity of agapētos; what-one-loves (active direction) establishes identity through the chosen object. The relational capacity faculty (T3.11) is the faculty through which the three relational axes are exercised: the GOD→HUMAN axis engages the relational capacity as receiver; the HUMAN→GOD axis engages it as giver; the HUMAN→HUMAN axis engages it in both directions simultaneously. Memory (T3.3) sustains the relational interface: love toward God is sustained through remembering his chesed (Jer 31:20); love in community is sustained through shared history. Moral sensitivity (T3.8) is calibrated by the relational interface structure: love-of-God calibrates the moral perception of what is evil (Psa 97:10); love-of-neighbour calibrates the perception of what is just. The deepest inter-tier finding: the faculty engagement pattern is not incidental — it is precisely the faculty configuration required by the relational architecture. The relational structure generates the faculty requirements.
- Source Q&A: Q&A-068, Q&A-073, Q&A-075, Q&A-076, Q&A-077, Q&A-079, Q&A-085, Q&A-087

**SYN-INTER-103-013 | T3 × T5 — Inner Faculties and Formative Developmental**
- Outcome: D — Described
- Synthesis: Formation in T5 operates through the same faculties identified in T3, producing their development. Memory is formed through the covenantal story — Israel's memory of God's love (Jer 2:2 — 'I remember the devotion of your youth') is the ground for love's formation in both directions; formation requires knowing the love-history. Imagination is formed through eschatological vision: the forward-projection of love's fullness (Psa 27:13, Jer 31:34) orients present formation toward its goal. Identity formation is the T3.10/T5 overlap: being-named-beloved (Mat 3:17, Rom 1:7) is the formation's constitutive moment — identity received through love is the ground from which love-acts are exercised. The relational capacity faculty (T3.11) is the faculty that formation produces: the formation process (Spirit infusion, obedience-purification, training) produces a person with increasing relational capacity for love's three directional axes. The community's role in formation (Q&A-097) corresponds to the relational capacity faculty's communal engagement: the faculty cannot develop in isolation because love cannot exist without a beloved.
- Source Q&A: Q&A-068, Q&A-069, Q&A-075, Q&A-076, Q&A-091, Q&A-095, Q&A-096, Q&A-097

**SYN-INTER-103-014 | T3 × T6 — Inner Faculties and Structural Relationships**
- Outcome: D — Described
- Synthesis: The faculty engagement breadth in T3 is consistent with love's structural position as the programme's central sequential node in T6. A characteristic that engages all eleven faculties will necessarily stand at the intersection of the programme's full inner-being vocabulary — because any characteristic that engages one faculty will co-occur with love insofar as love also engages that faculty. The memory-faculty engagement explains part of the co-occurrence with despair (R044 — 55 shared verses): lament appeals to the memory of God's love (Lam 3:22) as its ground. The identity-faculty engagement explains the co-occurrence with calling (R019 — 51 shared): identity-as-beloved and identity-as-called are grammatically co-ordinate (Rom 1:7). The moral-sensitivity engagement explains co-occurrence with guilt (R073 — 32 shared): moral sensitivity calibrated by love recognises guilt as the state that precedes the forgiveness that generates love (Luk 7:47). Faculty engagement and structural relationships thus form a coherent explanatory system: the faculty profile generates the co-occurrence pattern.
- Source Q&A: Q&A-066, Q&A-068, Q&A-073, Q&A-075, Q&A-101, Q&A-102, Q&A-104

**SYN-INTER-103-015 | T3 × T7 — Inner Faculties and Evidential Foundation**
- Outcome: D — Described
- Synthesis: The vocabulary evidence grounds the faculty claims with lexical precision. Identity faculty (T3.10): agapētos (person-type of being-loved), chasid (person-type of chesed), filos (person-type of phileō) — all three are lexically grounded person-type terms (Q&A-127). Moral sensitivity faculty (T3.8): the hate-vocabulary embedded as OWNER (H8130 sane — Q&A-126) grounds the claim that love requires and produces righteous hatred — the structural opposite provides the moral sensitivity calibration. Memory faculty (T3.3): the verb-form analysis (Q&A-123) shows that chesed as noun-primary form implies a dispositional quality that persists — memory is the chesed-noun's faculty correlate. Attention faculty (T3.1): phileō's etymology (from philos — friend) implies a relational salience structure — the one who is phileō-loved becomes salient to the lover's attention-field. The vocabulary's etymological structure (Q&A-122) is thus the lexical ground of the faculty engagement pattern: the root meanings point toward the faculties each term primarily activates.
- Source Q&A: Q&A-066, Q&A-073, Q&A-075, Q&A-122, Q&A-125, Q&A-126, Q&A-127

**SYN-INTER-103-016 | T4 × T5 — Relational Interfaces and Formative Developmental**
- Outcome: D — Described
- Synthesis: The relational interface structure and the formation process are interdependent: the formation process is directed toward equipping the person for love's three relational axes, and the relational axes are the context in which formation occurs. GOD→HUMAN axis as formation ground: divine love received (1Jo 4:19) is the formative act that establishes the person's capacity for all subsequent love — receiving is formation's enabling event. HUMAN→GOD axis as formation goal: total inner mobilisation (Mat 22:37 — all heart, soul, mind) is the fully formed love toward God; partial mobilisation marks love still in formation. HUMAN→HUMAN axis as formation context: community (1Pe 1:22, Tit 2:4) is both the goal-state (mutual love as community identity — Joh 13:35) and the formation context (love formed through exercising love within community). The reversibility asymmetry (divine love irreversible; human love subject to redirection) maps onto the axis structure: the GOD→HUMAN axis is the stable ground; the HUMAN→GOD and HUMAN→HUMAN axes are the formation-dependent expressions. Formation deepens the second and third axes; the first axis does not depend on formation.
- Source Q&A: Q&A-077, Q&A-080, Q&A-087, Q&A-091, Q&A-094, Q&A-095, Q&A-097

**SYN-INTER-103-017 | T4 × T6 — Relational Interfaces and Structural Relationships**
- Outcome: D — Described
- Synthesis: The three relational axes in T4 generate the structural relationship pattern in T6. The GOD→HUMAN axis explains love's highest co-occurrences with the programme's theological vocabulary: calling (R019 — 51 shared, identity-as-beloved and identity-as-called), faith (R059 — 62 shared, the inner condition for receiving divine love), and compassion (R023 — 196 shared, the compassionate-responsive mode of divine love). The HUMAN→HUMAN axis explains the co-occurrence with peace (R117 — 68 shared, peacemaking as love's horizontal expression) and community-related vocabulary. The sequential structure (divine love prior → human love responsive → ethical life) explains love's mediating position (Q&A-105): it stands between the GOD→HUMAN axis and the HUMAN→HUMAN axis as the transmission point. Love received from God becomes love given to neighbour — the sequential position is the relational interface described structurally. The 48 shared anchor verses are the evidential sites where these relational intersections are most visible: Exo 34:6 (GOD→HUMAN axis at maximum density), Gal 5:22 (HUMAN→HUMAN axis generated by Spirit), Joh 13:34 (HUMAN→HUMAN axis constituted by GOD→HUMAN love as model).
- Source Q&A: Q&A-077, Q&A-087, Q&A-101, Q&A-104, Q&A-105, Q&A-116, Q&A-117


**SYN-INTER-103-018 | T4 × T7 — Relational Interfaces and Evidential Foundation**
- Outcome: D — Described
- Synthesis: The evidential foundation directly supports each of the three relational axes. GOD→HUMAN axis — most densely evidenced: Exo 34:6 (divine self-declaration of love as primary attribute), Jer 12:7 (beloved of God's soul), Mat 3:17 (beloved Son named), Joh 3:16 (God so loved the world), Rom 5:5 (love poured into hearts through Spirit). The lexical evidence for this axis runs from the OT's chesed-God group (169 active verses — largest single group in the registry, Q&A-038) through the NT's agapē-God group (35 relevant). HUMAN→GOD axis — Psa 63:3 (chesed above life), Mat 22:37 (total inner mobilisation), Joh 14:15 (love producing obedience); these are carried by the agapaō-love-of-God group (571-001) and the chesed-human group (536-002). HUMAN→HUMAN axis — Lev 19:18 (neighbour-love commandment), Mat 5:44 (enemy-love), Joh 13:34 (new commandment), Joh 13:35 (community identity); these span the rea-group (173 active), the agapaō-mutual group (571-004, 53 relevant), and the filadelfia group (558-001). The evidential foundation confirms that all three axes have strong lexical and verse-level grounding, with the GOD→HUMAN axis carrying the greatest evidential weight.
- Source Q&A: Q&A-077, Q&A-080, Q&A-087, Q&A-122, Q&A-132, Q&A-136

**SYN-INTER-103-019 | T5 × T6 — Formative Developmental and Structural Relationships**
- Outcome: D — Described
- Synthesis: The formation process and the structural relationships are mutually reinforcing systems. The formation pathway (divine love received → Spirit infusion → soul purification → community expression) maps onto the sequential structural position: love's formation follows the same sequence as love's structural position in the programme — first received (downstream of divine action), then formed (mediating), then expressed (generative of ethical life). The growth-capacity of love (1Th 3:12 — Q&A-092) explains the programme's most puzzling co-occurrence finding: strength and authority (C20, 105 and 69 shared verses respectively). Love growing under the Lord's enabling encounters contexts of power — covenantal love among the people of God is exercised within structures of authority, governance, and strength. The love-power co-occurrence reflects the formation context: love formed within communities is formed within structures of authority. The eschatological trajectory (toward perfect love and direct knowledge) describes the structural relationships' completion: when love reaches its eschatological form, the partial sequential relationships (love received → love given → ethical life) are resolved into the direct love-knowledge of the new covenant (Jer 31:34).
- Source Q&A: Q&A-092, Q&A-095, Q&A-096, Q&A-101, Q&A-102, Q&A-104, Q&A-105

**SYN-INTER-103-020 | T5 × T7 — Formative Developmental and Evidential Foundation**
- Outcome: D — Described
- Synthesis: The evidential foundation grounds the formation claims at the lexical level. The growth-capacity finding (Q&A-092) is grounded in the verbal form agapaō and the noun-verb movement: chesed as noun (stable quality) requires formation before it functions as such; the transition from occasional loving acts (verb) to stable covenantal character (noun-quality) is the formation process in lexical form. The reversibility asymmetry (divine love irreversible; human love redirectable — Q&A-094) is grounded in the vocabulary's own structure: the divine forms of chesed and agapē carry permanence qualifiers (olam — everlasting; Lam 3:22 — never ceasing) that the human love forms do not. The primary anchor (Lam 3:22 — Q&A-136) is itself a formation text: the confession of love's permanence in extremity is a formation of the inner person toward trust in what cannot be seen. The formation process produces the person capable of making the Lam 3:22 confession — the developmental trajectory toward love's perfection includes the formation of the inner person's capacity to confess love against empirical evidence.
- Source Q&A: Q&A-091, Q&A-094, Q&A-095, Q&A-123, Q&A-136, Q&A-137

**SYN-INTER-103-021 | T6 × T7 — Structural Relationships and Evidential Foundation**
- Outcome: D — Described
- Synthesis: The structural relationship data and the evidential foundation are the most mutually confirming pair in the synthesis matrix. The co-occurrence breadth (T6.1) is directly explained by the vocabulary breadth (T7.1.10 — the widest semantic arc in the programme): a vocabulary that spans from divine being to love of darkness will co-occur with every other inner-being characteristic because it occupies every register of the inner-being vocabulary. The shared anchor density (48 verses — T6.6) is explained by the primary anchor's function (Lam 3:22 — T7.2.5/T7.2.6): the programme anchors the most significant cross-registry verses at love because love is the definitional centre from which adjacent characteristics derive their meaning. The vocabulary sharing ratio (0.701 — T6.4) is explained by the root-level connections (T7.1.2): the racham root connects love, compassion, and mercy; the ahav root connects love and desire; the tov root connects love and goodness. The structural relationship data is, at its core, the observable programme-level effect of the lexical architecture that the evidential foundation analysis reveals. Structural breadth and lexical breadth are the same reality at different levels of analysis.
- Source Q&A: Q&A-101, Q&A-110, Q&A-111, Q&A-112, Q&A-116, Q&A-117, Q&A-122, Q&A-130, Q&A-131
